### CrossShardReceiptDedup.tla Ôćĺ cross-shard inbound-receipt dedup state machine (T-R1 / T-R2 / T-R3 / T-R4)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `accounts` (Domains Ôćĺ [balance: Nat]), `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey), `accumulated_inbound` (Nat), `pending_receipts` (Seq(Receipt)), `snapshot_state` (SnapshotState or NoSnapshot), `history` (Seq(DedupKey)) |
| `Inv_BalanceNonNegative` | per-recipient `balance >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed; documents the contract. ApplyFirst only credits (never debits); Restore preserves Nat-typed values from the snapshot |
| `Inv_AccumulatedInboundMonotonic` | `accumulated_inbound >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed lower bound (the strict monotonicity claim across non-Restore steps lives in the action-form Prop_DedupAlwaysHolds + the structure of ApplyFirst increments) |
| `Inv_DedupKeyIsPair` | T-R3 state-machine companion: every entry in `applied_receipts` is a `(src_shard, tx_hash)` pair ÔÇö same `tx_hash` from different `src_shards` are distinct keys. Mirrors the C++ `std::pair<ShardId, std::string>` key type at `src/chain/chain.cpp:139` (the `applied_inbound_receipts_` definition) |
| `Inv_NoDoubleCredit` | T-R1 + T-R2 composed: per-recipient balance change equals the sum of UNIQUE receipt amounts targeting that recipient (no duplicate-inflation). State-form upper bound: `balance <= MaxAmount * Cardinality(applied_receipts)` ÔÇö the tighter equality lives in the temporal `Prop_DedupAlwaysHolds` |
| `Inv_AppliedImpliesCredited` | every entry in `applied_receipts` was installed by exactly one `ApplyFirst` step. Structurally enforced: ApplyFirst's pre-condition `KeyOf(r) \notin applied_receipts` blocks re-firing on the same key; the `history` sequence witnesses one entry per applied key |
| `Prop_DedupAlwaysHolds` (temporal) | action-form: every transition is one of (a) UNCHANGED applied_receipts (SubmitReceipt / Equivocate / ApplyDuplicate / Snapshot), (b) extension by exactly one DedupKey (ApplyFirst), or (c) replacement by snapshot_state.applied_receipts (Restore) ÔÇö no other delta is permitted |
| `Prop_EventualApply` (temporal) | under fairness on `ApplyFirst`, any pending receipt with a fresh key eventually applies (`k \in applied_receipts`) OR the queue drains via duplicate-apply (`Len(pending_receipts) = 0`) ÔÇö the eventual-progress / no-stuck-pending guarantee |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other nine specs above). The configuration in `CrossShardReceiptDedup.cfg` (3 shards, 2 domains, 2 hashes, MaxAmount=3, MaxHeight=4) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `accounts` (Domains Ôćĺ [balance: Nat] ÔÇö per-recipient credit ledger), `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey ÔÇö the protocol's `applied_inbound_receipts_` lifted into TLA+ set semantics), `accumulated_inbound` (Nat ÔÇö monotone counter, the chain-level lift of the C++ per-block `block_inbound` accumulator at chain.cpp:1377-1380), `pending_receipts` (Seq(Receipt) ÔÇö submitted but not yet applied), `snapshot_state` (SnapshotState or NoSnapshot ÔÇö last serialized triple, models the S-033 + S-037 + S-038 round-trip), `history` (Seq(DedupKey) ÔÇö audit log of ApplyFirst credits, witnesses Inv_AppliedImpliesCredited). Actions modeled: `SubmitReceipt` (legitimate ingress ÔÇö any well-formed receipt may be queued; the apply-side dedup gate is the safety net), `ApplyFirst` (the fresh-key apply branch at chain.cpp:1363-1381 ÔÇö credits recipient, inserts key, bumps counter), `ApplyDuplicate` (the silent-skip duplicate branch at chain.cpp:1365 `if (applied_inbound_receipts_.count(key)) continue;`), `Snapshot` (S-037 serialize step at chain.cpp:1586-1592), `Restore` (S-037 restore step at chain.cpp:1778-1783; the T-R4 dedup-set-survives-restore property), `Equivocate` (adversarial ÔÇö the same dedup-key arrives via two different submission paths, modeling worst-case wire-level replay/race). The 11-field C++ CrossShardReceipt struct is abstracted to the four invariant-relevant fields (src_shard, tx_hash, to, amount) ÔÇö the remaining seven (dst_shard, src_block_index, src_block_hash, from, fee, nonce, dst_addr_hint) are FA7 cryptographic-binding territory, orthogonal to the apply-side dedup primitive.

This spec drills into the apply-side detail that FB3 (Receipts.tla) modeled at minimum granularity and FB2 (Sharding.tla) modeled at flow granularity. The triangle FB2 Ôćö FB3 Ôćö FB14 covers the cross-shard receipt mechanism from three complementary angles: emission + admission (FB2), per-block dedup-set monotonicity (FB3), and the apply-level dedup primitive with snapshot-survivable state + multi-shard tx_hash collision handling (FB14). The Inv_DedupKeyIsPair invariant is the non-trivial strengthening over FB3: a single-key model cannot witness the T-R3 "(s1, h1) and (s2, h1) are two distinct keys" property; FB14 makes the pair structure first-class and verifies the protocol's actual key type.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/CrossShardReceiptDedup.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).
### EquivocationApply.tla Ôćĺ FA6 equivocation-slashing apply state machine (Equivocate / Apply / Ghost / AlreadyDeactivated)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `registrants` (Domains Ôćĺ [active, inactive_from] with `inactive_from \in 0..Sentinel`), `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ 0..MaxStake), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat-bounded by INITIAL_TOTAL_STAKE = MaxStake ┬Ě |Domains|), `height` (0..MaxHeight), `pending_events` (Seq of EquivocationEvent) |
| `Inv_StakeNonNegative` | per-domain `stakes[d] >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed; documents the contract. Apply* branches zero stakes[d] (to 0, not negative); Equivocate / AdvanceHeight never decrement |
| `Inv_SlashedNeverExceedsTotal` | A1-companion conservation: `SumStakes + accumulated_slashed <= INITIAL_TOTAL_STAKE` ÔÇö every Apply* branch consumes from stakes[d] into accumulated_slashed (zero-sum on the pair). The Ghost branch is a no-op (stakes already 0); the active and AlreadyDeactivated branches drain stakes[d] -> 0 with the matching contribution. The <= is non-strict because Ghost contributes nothing |
| `Inv_DeactivatedAfterSlash` | T-E1 atomic coupling: any domain with `stakes[d] = 0 /\ inactive_from /= Sentinel` has `active = FALSE` ÔÇö the slash-and-deregister are applied together at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1344-1356` (the `if (sit != stakes_.end())` and `if (rit != registrants_.end())` branches are independent in the C++ but the apply-layer never sets one without the other reaching a consistent post-state). The structural witness of the coupling |
| `Inv_SlashedMonotonic` | action-level: `accumulated_slashed' >= accumulated_slashed` across every `[Next]_vars` step. Only ApplyEquivocation and ApplyEquivocationAlreadyDeactivated add to the field, both by the pre-apply stakes[d] (a Nat); Equivocate / ApplyEquivocationGhost / AdvanceHeight preserve |
| `Inv_NoDoubleSlash` | action-level: any single Apply* step contributes at most the pre-apply stakes[d] to accumulated_slashed. Multiple equivocation events for the same offender each fire Apply* separately, but the SECOND such event finds `stakes[d] = 0` (Ghost branch ÔÇö no contribution). Encoded as: if `accumulated_slashed' > accumulated_slashed` for head offender d, then `accumulated_slashed' - accumulated_slashed = stakes[d]` (the pre-apply value) |
| `Prop_EventualSlash` (temporal) | under fairness on `AdvanceHeight` + the three Apply* branches, any non-empty `pending_events` eventually drains. The three Apply* branches together cover the full guard space at the head (active Ôćĺ ApplyEquivocation; fully wound down Ôćĺ Ghost; inactive with stake Ôćĺ AlreadyDeactivated); fairness on the disjunction gives the eventual-progress claim. The MaxHeight escape covers the model-bound termination case |
| `Prop_StateMonotone` (temporal) | `[][...]_vars` form: per-domain `stakes'[d] <= stakes[d]` at every step. No action increases stakes in this spec ÔÇö there is no "un-slash" / "re-stake" branch in the apply-equivocation state machine (STAKE-tx restake is FB8 territory). Combined with `Inv_DeactivatedAfterSlash`, gives the full "slash is one-way and permanent" claim |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other nine specs above). The configuration in `EquivocationApply.cfg` (3 domains, MaxHeight=4, MaxStake=5, Sentinel=1000) is sized for an interactive TLC run in well under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `registrants` (Domains Ôćĺ [active, inactive_from] ÔÇö matching the C++ `RegistryEntry` shape at `include/determ/chain/chain.hpp`; the model collapses `active_from` into a single `active` boolean since the apply path only consults `active_from <= h < inactive_from`), `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö the locked stake amount; matches `StakeEntry::locked`), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat ÔÇö matches `Chain::accumulated_slashed_` at chain.cpp:1395), `height` (Nat), `pending_events` (Seq of EquivocationEvent ÔÇö abstracting the producer-side `pending_equivocations_` aggregation + the per-block `equivocation_events` field). Actions modeled: `Equivocate` (adversarial ÔÇö appends to pending_events; abstracts EUF-CMA / V11), `ApplyEquivocation` (active branch ÔÇö chain.cpp:1344-1356), `ApplyEquivocationGhost` (T-E4 branch ÔÇö already wound down, no-op), `ApplyEquivocationAlreadyDeactivated` (dual-mechanism ÔÇö inactive but still has stake), `AdvanceHeight` (temporal driver). Sentinel=1000 >> MaxHeight + 1 = 5 satisfies ConfigOK and keeps `height + 1` writes monotone away from the "never deactivated" marker. The three Apply* branches are mutually exclusive on their guards and together cover the full head-of-queue guard space, ensuring `Prop_EventualSlash` under fairness.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/EquivocationSlashingApply.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).
### AbortApply.tla Ôćĺ AbortEvent apply state machine (RecordAbort / Phase1 / Phase2 / DomainInclusion)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ 0..InitialStake), `abort_records` (Domains Ôćĺ [count: Nat] ÔÇö the S-032 cache shape), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat-bounded by INITIAL_TOTAL_STAKE = InitialStake ┬Ě \|Domains\|), `round` (0..MaxRound), `pending` (Seq of AbortEvent with phase Ôłł {1, 2}), `registry_untouched` (BOOLEAN sentinel for T-A4) |
| `Inv_StakeNonNegative` | per-domain `stakes[d] >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed; documents the contract. ApplyPhase1Abort uses the `min(stakes[d], SUSPENSION_SLASH)` floor at chain.cpp:1324 to bound the deduction; the other Apply* branches and RecordAbort / AdvanceRound never decrement stakes |
| `Inv_NoFullForfeitureOnAbort` | T-A1 + headline distinction from equivocation T-E1: action-level invariant that any step reducing `stakes[d]` to 0 (post = 0, pre > 0) must come from a state where `pre < SUSPENSION_SLASH`. The boundary case `pre = SUSPENSION_SLASH Ôćĺ post = 0` is the strict-equality drain; the `min()` floor at chain.cpp:1324 structurally prevents post < 0. Equivocation has no such bound ÔÇö `EquivocationApply.ApplyEquivocation` zeroes `stakes[d]` regardless of pre-apply value |
| `Inv_AbortRecordsMonotonic` | T-A3 / S-032 cache contract: per-domain `abort_records'[d].count >= abort_records[d].count` across every `[Next]_vars` step. Every Apply* branch increments by exactly 1 (chain.cpp:1319); RecordAbort / AdvanceRound preserve. The S-032 cache is the authoritative count consumed by `build_from_chain` for suspension-tracker accounting; its monotonicity is what lets snapshot/restore round-trip the count without replay |
| `Inv_NoRegistryDeactivation` | T-A4 structural witness: the `registry_untouched` BOOLEAN sentinel stays TRUE across every reachable state because no AbortEvent apply branch ever mutates registry state. Mirrors the chain.cpp:1313-1328 apply loop's structural absence of any `registrants_[...] = ...` assignment, in pointed contrast to chain.cpp:1354's `rit->second.inactive_from = b.index + 1` in the equivocation loop. The complementary claim that equivocation DOES deactivate is `EquivocationApply.Inv_DeactivatedAfterSlash`; the two specs jointly witness the abort-vs-equivocation asymmetry at the apply layer |
| `Inv_SlashedMonotonic` | action-level: `accumulated_slashed' >= accumulated_slashed` across every `[Next]_vars` step. Only ApplyPhase1Abort mutates the field, by the non-negative `deduct = min(stakes[d], SUSPENSION_SLASH)` value (a Nat). ApplyPhase2Abort / ApplyAbortDomainInclusion / RecordAbort / AdvanceRound all preserve. Matches `Chain::accumulated_slashed_` monotonicity at chain.cpp:1395 |
| `Prop_EventualApply` (temporal) | under fairness on `AdvanceRound` + the three Apply* branches, any non-empty `pending` eventually drains. The three Apply* branches together cover the full guard space at the head ((phase 1, stake > 0) Ôćĺ Phase1; (phase 2, stake > 0) Ôćĺ Phase2; (any phase, stake = 0) Ôćĺ DomainInclusion); fairness on the disjunction gives the eventual-progress claim. The MaxRound escape covers the model-bound termination case |
| `Prop_Phase2NoSlash` (temporal) | T-A2 headline: `[][...]_vars` action invariant ÔÇö a step whose head pending event has `phase = 2` AND fires Apply* (consumes from pending) preserves `accumulated_slashed`. The abort-event apply path distinguishes Phase-1 (slash + record) from Phase-2 (record only); equivocation has no such phase distinction. Matches the `if (ae.round != 1) continue;` guard at chain.cpp:1314 that short-circuits the slash branch while leaving the abort_records bump at chain.cpp:1317-1320 untouched |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other ten specs above). The configuration in `AbortApply.cfg` (3 domains, MaxRound=4, InitialStake=30, SUSPENSION_SLASH=10) is sized for an interactive TLC run in well under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö matching `StakeEntry::locked` at `include/determ/chain/chain.hpp`; the unlock_height field is FB8 / StakeLifecycle.tla territory and not consumed by the AbortEvent apply path), `abort_records` (Domains Ôćĺ [count: Nat] ÔÇö the S-032 cache shape at `include/determ/chain/chain.hpp::AbortRecord`; the `last_block` field is also bumped at chain.cpp:1320 but is FA-track / suspension-tracker territory and orthogonal to the apply-layer invariants), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat ÔÇö matches `Chain::accumulated_slashed_` at chain.cpp:1395), `round` (Nat ÔÇö temporal driver; the consensus-round counter, separate from block index), `pending` (Seq of AbortEvent ÔÇö abstracting the producer-side aggregation + per-block `Block::abort_events` field), `registry_untouched` (BOOLEAN ÔÇö sentinel proving T-A4 vacuously). Actions modeled: `RecordAbort` (adversarial ÔÇö appends to pending; abstracts V8 abort-claim verification + signature aggregation), `ApplyPhase1Abort` (slash + record at chain.cpp:1313-1328 with `round == 1`), `ApplyPhase2Abort` (record only ÔÇö the `round != 1` skip at chain.cpp:1314 + the unconditional records bump at chain.cpp:1317-1320), `ApplyAbortDomainInclusion` (T-A5 ÔÇö `stakes[d] = 0` collapses the phase distinction; matches the chain.cpp:1322-1323 `stakes_.find == stakes_.end()` short-circuit while the abort_records bump still fires), `AdvanceRound` (temporal driver). InitialStake=30 with SUSPENSION_SLASH=10 lets stakes[d] visit {30, 20, 10, 0} ÔÇö three Phase-1 aborts exhaustively drain a domain; the boundary `pre = SUSPENSION_SLASH Ôćĺ post = 0` step witnesses Inv_NoFullForfeitureOnAbort's strict-inequality contract. The three Apply* branches are mutually exclusive on their guards and together cover the full head-of-queue guard space, ensuring Prop_EventualApply under fairness.

**Distinction from FB15 EquivocationApply.tla:** the two specs together cover the two production "slash" mechanisms ÔÇö abort-suspension and equivocation. Three structural asymmetries are encoded in the invariants:

1. **Bounded vs full slash.** AbortApply's `Inv_NoFullForfeitureOnAbort` allows a single-step drain to 0 only when pre-apply stake was already below SUSPENSION_SLASH; EquivocationApply has no such bound ÔÇö `ApplyEquivocation` zeroes stakes regardless of pre-apply value (full forfeiture).
2. **Phase-discriminated slash.** AbortApply's `Prop_Phase2NoSlash` carves out the Phase-2 records-only branch; EquivocationApply has no phase axis ÔÇö every event slashes.
3. **No registry deactivation.** AbortApply's `Inv_NoRegistryDeactivation` is structurally vacuous (no action flips the sentinel); EquivocationApply's `Inv_DeactivatedAfterSlash` is the headline registry-mutation invariant. AbortEvent never sets `inactive_from`; equivocation always does (chain.cpp:1354).

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/AbortEventApply.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).

### AbortApply.tla Ôćĺ FA5 AbortEvent apply state machine (Phase1Slash / Phase2NoSlash / Ghost / Idempotent)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `registrants` (Domains Ôćĺ [active, inactive_from]), `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ 0..MaxStake), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat-bounded by INITIAL_TOTAL_STAKE = MaxStake ┬Ě |Domains|), `height` (0..MaxHeight), `pending_events` (Seq of AbortEvent with `phase \in {1, 2}` discriminator) |
| `Inv_StakeNonNegative` | per-domain `stakes[d] >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed; documents the contract. Phase-1 Apply branches debit stakes[d] by the proportional formula (floor((stakes[d] * SlashNumerator) / SlashDenominator)) which is bounded above by stakes[d] itself; Phase-2 Apply / Ghost / AdvanceHeight never decrement |
| `Inv_SlashedMonotonic` | action-level: `accumulated_slashed' >= accumulated_slashed` across every `[Next]_vars` step. Only ApplyPhase1Slash contributes (via the proportional formula); Equivocate / ApplyPhase2NoSlash / ApplyGhost / AdvanceHeight preserve. The action-level witness of the slash-is-one-way property at the apply layer |
| `Inv_Phase1ProportionalSlash` | T-A1 contract: when a Phase-1 AbortEvent applies to a domain with `stakes[d] > 0`, the slash amount equals `floor((stakes[d] * SlashNumerator) / SlashDenominator)` (matching the C++ proportional formula in `Chain::apply_block_locked` AbortEvent Phase-1 branch). The structural witness that Phase-1 is proportional, not full-forfeiture (FA-Apply-10 distinction between AbortEvent Phase-1 and EquivocationEvent) |
| `Inv_Phase2NoSlash` | T-A2 contract: any Phase-2 AbortEvent apply step preserves `stakes[d]` and `accumulated_slashed` byte-for-byte. Phase-2 is informational only ÔÇö no stake mutation. The structural witness for the protocol-design distinction in FA5 (Phase-2 indicates honest disagreement on a Byzantine input rather than provable misbehavior) |
| `Inv_RegistryUnchanged` | T-A3 contract: no Apply* branch in this spec flips `registrants[d].active` or writes `registrants[d].inactive_from`. AbortEvent never deactivates the offender ÔÇö unlike EquivocationEvent (FB15 / FA-Apply-10) which atomically slashes AND deactivates. The structural witness for the "abort is recoverable, equivocation is terminal" distinction |
| `Prop_EventualAbortApply` (temporal) | under fairness on `AdvanceHeight` + the three Apply* branches, any non-empty `pending_events` eventually drains. The three Apply* branches together cover the full guard space at the head (Phase-1 active Ôćĺ ApplyPhase1Slash; Phase-2 active Ôćĺ ApplyPhase2NoSlash; absent-from-stakes Ôćĺ ApplyGhost); fairness on the disjunction gives the eventual-progress claim. The MaxHeight escape covers the model-bound termination case |
| `Prop_StateMonotone` (temporal) | `[][...]_vars` form: per-domain `stakes'[d] <= stakes[d]` at every step. No action increases stakes in this spec ÔÇö there is no "un-slash" / "re-stake" branch in the apply-abort state machine (STAKE-tx restake is FB8 territory). Combined with `Inv_Phase1ProportionalSlash` + `Inv_Phase2NoSlash`, gives the full "Phase-1 slash is bounded + one-way; Phase-2 is no-op" claim |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other ten specs above). The configuration in `AbortApply.cfg` (3 domains, MaxHeight=4, MaxStake=5, SlashNumerator=1, SlashDenominator=3 ÔÇö modeling a 1/3-proportional slash to match the protocol's anti-cartel formula at apply time) is sized for an interactive TLC run in well under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `registrants` (Domains Ôćĺ [active, inactive_from] ÔÇö matching the C++ `RegistryEntry` shape; the model preserves the full shape to give `Inv_RegistryUnchanged` first-class structural witness without needing to consult an auxiliary "did this step modify registrants" predicate), `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö the locked stake amount; matches `StakeEntry::locked`), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat ÔÇö matches `Chain::accumulated_slashed_`), `height` (Nat), `pending_events` (Seq of AbortEvent with a `phase` discriminator). Actions modeled: `Equivocate` (adversarial ÔÇö appends a Phase-1 or Phase-2 AbortEvent to pending_events), `ApplyPhase1Slash` (active branch with `phase = 1`), `ApplyPhase2NoSlash` (active branch with `phase = 2`), `ApplyGhost` (ghost-evidence branch ÔÇö domain absent from stakes), `AdvanceHeight` (temporal driver). The three Apply* branches are mutually exclusive on their guards (phase discriminator + stakes membership) and together cover the full head-of-queue guard space, ensuring `Prop_EventualAbortApply` under fairness.

This spec is the companion to FB15 (EquivocationApply.tla) ÔÇö together they model the full slashing surface at the apply layer. The two specs differ on three axes that match the FA5 / FA6 protocol-design distinction: (1) Phase-1 AbortEvent is *proportional* slash (`Inv_Phase1ProportionalSlash`); EquivocationEvent is *full* forfeiture, (2) Phase-2 AbortEvent is *no-op* (`Inv_Phase2NoSlash`); there is no Phase-2 equivalent for EquivocationEvent, (3) AbortEvent never flips `registrants[d].active` (`Inv_RegistryUnchanged`); EquivocationEvent atomically deactivates. The shared structure (Apply / Ghost / AdvanceHeight; monotone `accumulated_slashed`; non-negative `stakes`) is the apply-layer slashing-correctness contract; the differences are the FA5 vs FA6 protocol-design contract.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/AbortEventApply.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).
### AppliedReceiptRestore.tla Ôćĺ cross-shard `applied_inbound_receipts_` snapshot/restore lifecycle (S-037 closure witness)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey ÔÇö the dedup set), `balances` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat), `accumulated_inbound` (Nat), `snapshot_state` (SnapshotState record or NoSnapshot sentinel), `pending` (Seq of Receipt ÔÇö head-first apply queue), `height` (0..MaxHeight action counter) |
| `Inv_RestoreEqualsPre` | T-AR2 (post-restore-equals-snapshot): at every reachable state with `snapshot_state /= NoSnapshot`, either `applied_receipts = snapshot_state.applied_receipts` (immediate post-restore window) or the snapshot's set is a subset of the live set (post-snapshot extension via ApplyFirstReceipt). The action `RestoreSnapshot` writes back the snapshot's set verbatim ÔÇö matches `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` at chain.cpp:1778-1783, the S-037 closure that rehydrates `applied_inbound_receipts_` from the new `applied_inbound_receipts` snapshot namespace |
| `Inv_DedupPersistsAcrossRestore` | T-AR3 (the headline S-037 property): every key in `snapshot_state.applied_receipts` is also in the live `applied_receipts`. The pre-S-037 bug would have witnessed a counter-example because the snapshot did not serialize the dedup-set; restore would silently rewind to {} and a re-submitted receipt would credit a second time. Post-S-037 the live set is always a superset (or equal) ÔÇö restore preserves verbatim. The contract that prevents the double-spend |
| `Inv_FreshCreditPostRestore` | T-AR4: a receipt whose dedup-key is NOT in the live `applied_receipts` remains admissible by ApplyFirstReceipt post-restore. Restore is not a permanent freeze ÔÇö only the snapshot-recorded keys are de-duplicated; fresh keys still credit. The operational claim is witnessed by the existence of reachable states where `|applied_receipts| > |snapshot_state.applied_receipts|` (SubmitReceipt Ôćĺ RestoreSnapshot Ôćĺ SubmitReceipt(fresh-key) Ôćĺ ApplyFirstReceipt trace) |
| `Inv_AccumulatedConsistent` | T-AR5: `accumulated_inbound` stays consistent with `applied_receipts` contents across snapshot/restore. State-form bound: `accumulated_inbound >= snapshot_state.accumulated_inbound` at every reachable state with `snapshot_state /= NoSnapshot`. ApplyFirstReceipt only increments; RestoreSnapshot rewinds the field to snapshot's value exactly. The field tracks the live applied_receipts' amount sum faithfully ÔÇö the per-block `block_inbound` counter at chain.cpp:1377-1380 lifted to chain-level monotone state |
| `Inv_BalanceNonNegative` | per-recipient `balances[d] >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed; documents the contract. ApplyFirstReceipt only credits (never debits); RestoreSnapshot writes Nat-typed snapshot values; ApplyDuplicate / TryDuplicatePostRestore / SubmitReceipt / TakeSnapshot preserve |
| `Inv_DedupKeyIsPair` | T-R3 lifted from FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup.tla): each entry in `applied_receipts` is a `(src_shard, tx_hash)` pair record. Same `tx_hash` from two different `src_shards` is two distinct entries. Mirrors `std::pair<ShardId, std::string>` at chain.cpp:139. The invariant is preserved across snapshot/restore ÔÇö the save/load round-trip does not collapse the pair structure into a single string |
| `Prop_RestoreIdempotent` (temporal) | action-level: TakeSnapshot Ôłś RestoreSnapshot is identity on `applied_receipts` when no intermediate ApplyFirstReceipt fires. State-form: after every RestoreSnapshot transition, `applied_receipts' = snapshot_state.applied_receipts`. Composed with TakeSnapshot's `snapshot_state'.applied_receipts = applied_receipts` semantics, the round-trip preserves the set verbatim |
| `Prop_NoDoubleApply` (temporal) | action-level: every step that extends `applied_receipts` adds exactly one key, AND that key was NOT in `applied_receipts` pre-step. The structural witness ÔÇö ApplyFirstReceipt's pre-condition `KeyOf(r) \notin applied_receipts` blocks re-firing on the same key; no other action extends the set (ApplyDuplicate / TryDuplicatePostRestore preserve; TakeSnapshot preserves; RestoreSnapshot rewinds to snapshot's set, which was itself a previously-built set satisfying the same property by induction). The temporal restatement of the no-double-credit property across snapshot/restore boundaries |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other ten specs above). The configuration in `AppliedReceiptRestore.cfg` (2 shards, 3 tx-hashes, 2 domains, MaxAmount=3, MaxHeight=4) is sized for an interactive TLC run in well under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey ÔÇö the dedup set matching `applied_inbound_receipts_` at chain.cpp:204-206), `balances` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö the per-recipient credit ledger), `accumulated_inbound` (Nat ÔÇö chain-level lift of the per-block `block_inbound` counter at chain.cpp:1377-1380), `snapshot_state` (SnapshotState record or NoSnapshot sentinel ÔÇö saved triple of applied_receipts + balances + accumulated_inbound), `pending` (Seq of Receipt ÔÇö head-first apply queue), `height` (Nat ÔÇö action counter bounding TLC). Actions modeled: `SubmitReceipt` (adversarial ÔÇö appends to pending; the gossip-ratified ingress after V13 dst-dedup), `ApplyFirstReceipt` (fresh-key apply branch at chain.cpp:1363-1381 ÔÇö T-R1 first-credit-wins), `ApplyDuplicate` (the silent-skip branch at chain.cpp:1365 `if (applied_inbound_receipts_.count(key)) continue;` ÔÇö T-R2 subsequent-attempts-silent-noop), `TakeSnapshot` (saves the apply-state triple ÔÇö matches chain.cpp:1586-1592, the S-037 closure adding the `applied_inbound_receipts` namespace), `RestoreSnapshot` (rewinds to the saved triple ÔÇö matches chain.cpp:1778-1783), `TryDuplicatePostRestore` (the headline adversarial action ÔÇö submits a receipt whose dedup-key is in the post-restore applied_receipts set, verifies ApplyDuplicate is the only enabled branch). The canonical S-037 closure witness trace (SubmitReceipt Ôćĺ ApplyFirstReceipt Ôćĺ TakeSnapshot Ôćĺ RestoreSnapshot, with applied_receipts equal to snapshot's at every step) is reachable within MaxHeight=4.

This spec is the focused intersection of FB6 (Snapshot.tla ÔÇö generic snapshot/restore round-trip identity) and FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup.tla ÔÇö per-block dedup-set monotonicity). FB6 modeled the round-trip on (balances, counters); FB14 modeled the dedup-set under a SubmitReceipt / ApplyFirst / ApplyDuplicate / Snapshot / Restore / Equivocate adversary with one-shot save/load semantics. FB17 zooms in on the explicit snapshot lifecycle on the dedup-set, with TryDuplicatePostRestore as the dedicated adversarial action that verifies the T-AR3 cross-snapshot dedup contract that S-037 closed in the C++ implementation. The pre-S-037 bug shape (counter-factual) would have witnessed a counter-example for `Inv_DedupPersistsAcrossRestore` because the snapshot's `applied_inbound_receipts` namespace was missing entirely; the spec is the machine-checkable witness of the S-037 fix.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/AppliedReceiptRestore.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).

### CrossShardOutboundApply.tla Ôćĺ source-side cross-shard TRANSFER apply state machine (T-O1 / T-O2 / T-O3 / T-O4 / T-O5 / T-O7)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `accounts` (Domains Ôćĺ [balance: Nat]), `accumulated_outbound` (Nat), `pending_receipts` (Seq(Receipt)), `pending_txs` (Seq(Transfer)), `height` (Nat) |
| `Inv_BalanceNonNegative` | per-domain `balance >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed; documents the contract. The `accounts[t.from].balance >= t.amount + t.fee` cost gate at the head of both ApplyLocalTransfer and ApplyCrossShardTransfer structurally enforces post-state Nat (mirrors `if (sender.balance < cost) continue;` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:744`); ApplyInsufficientBalance is UNCHANGED on accounts |
| `Inv_OutboundMonotonic` | T-O2: `accumulated_outbound >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö Nat-typed lower bound. The action-level non-decreasing claim is structurally enforced: ApplyCrossShardTransfer strictly increments by `t.amount` (a positive Nat); all other actions preserve. Matches the `accumulated_outbound_ += block_outbound` advance at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1394` and the C++ field's `uint64_t` non-decreasing contract |
| `Inv_NoLocalCreditOnCrossShard` | T-O3 (action-level): for any ApplyCrossShardTransfer step, `accounts'[t.to].balance = accounts[t.to].balance`. The structural witness for "destination credit lives on the OTHER shard, not here" ÔÇö the cross-shard branch's `accounts'` clause uses EXCEPT updating ONLY the from-key, the to-key (different domain) is preserved by EXCEPT semantics. Matches the `else { block_outbound += tx.amount; }` branch at `src/chain/chain.cpp:762-766` which structurally OMITS the recipient credit (in contrast to the same-shard branch at chain.cpp:756-761 which credits recipient via `checked_add_u64`) |
| `Inv_OutboundSumEqualsReceiptSum` | T-O4 (state-level): `accumulated_outbound = SumReceipts(pending_receipts)` ÔÇö every unit that leaves the source's accounted supply is matched by an emitted receipt amount. The A1 source-mass conservation contract. Holds by construction at Init (both 0); preserved by every action: ApplyCrossShardTransfer increments both by `t.amount`; all other actions leave both UNCHANGED on the sum-equality side. The structural witness for the FA7 T-7.1 corollary (per-shard A1 composes to global supply atomicity via the receipt path) |
| `Inv_SingleShardNoOutbound` | T-O7 (degenerate case): when `Cardinality(Shards) = 1`, `accumulated_outbound = 0` AND `pending_receipts = <<>>`. The structural witness for the `is_cross_shard` short-circuit at `src/chain/chain.cpp:198-202` (`if (shard_count_ <= 1) return false;`) ÔÇö the model's IsCrossShard helper enforces this via the `Cardinality(Shards) > 1` clause, making the ApplyCrossShardTransfer branch structurally unreachable. Vacuous when |Shards| > 1 (the default cfg); the single-shard cfg variant exercises the contract |
| `Prop_EventualApply` (temporal) | under fairness on the three apply branches + FinalizeBlock, any non-empty `pending_txs` eventually drains. The three apply branches together cover the full guard space at the head ((same-shard, sufficient) Ôćĺ Local; (cross-shard, sufficient) Ôćĺ Cross; (any, insufficient) Ôćĺ InsufficientBalance); fairness on the disjunction gives the eventual-progress claim. The MaxHeight escape covers the model-bound termination case |
| `Prop_SourceA1Conservation` (temporal) | T-O1 action-level: across every ApplyCrossShardTransfer step targeting head `t`, `accounts'[t.from].balance = accounts[t.from].balance - (t.amount + t.fee)` AND `accounts'[d].balance = accounts[d].balance` for every `d /= t.from /\ d /= t.to`. The structural witness for the FA7 source-debit contract (Lemma L-7.3): source-side debit precedes receipt emission and is bound to the receipt's amount field |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other eleven specs above). The configuration in `CrossShardOutboundApply.cfg` (2 domains, 2 shards, MyShard=s1, MaxAmount=3, MaxFee=2, InitialBalance=10, MaxHeight=4) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. Variables modeled: `accounts` (Domains Ôćĺ [balance] ÔÇö collapsed from the full AccountState since the nonce / stake / ed_pub side is FB7 / FB8 / FB5 territory; the cross-shard outbound apply path only consults the `balance` field), `accumulated_outbound` (Nat ÔÇö matches `Chain::accumulated_outbound_` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1394`; the chain-level counter that aggregates per-block `block_outbound` advances), `pending_receipts` (Seq(Receipt) ÔÇö the producer-side `b.cross_shard_receipts` field; the model collapses the 11-field CrossShardReceipt struct to the (to, amount) pair since FB18 only cares about apply-side emission count + amount accumulation), `pending_txs` (Seq(Transfer) ÔÇö the per-block tx queue), `height` (Nat ÔÇö action counter bounding TLC). Actions modeled: `SubmitTransfer` (adversarial/user surface ÔÇö any well-formed Transfer may be queued), `ApplyLocalTransfer` (same-shard branch at chain.cpp:752-761; debit sender, credit recipient, fee absorbed by creators), `ApplyCrossShardTransfer` (cross-shard branch at chain.cpp:762-766 + producer emission at producer.cpp:459-465; debit sender, increment accumulated_outbound, emit receipt, NO local credit), `ApplyInsufficientBalance` (the `continue` silent-skip at chain.cpp:744 ÔÇö no mutation, no orphan emission), `FinalizeBlock` (block-finalize tail at chain.cpp:1393-1394 ÔÇö the model's "block flushed to chain" transition).

This spec is the source-side companion to FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup ÔÇö destination-side dedup) and FB17 (AppliedReceiptRestore ÔÇö snapshot lifecycle of the destination dedup set). The triangle FB2 Ôćö FB14 Ôćö FB18 covers the cross-shard mechanism from three complementary angles: receipt-flow soundness (FB2 ÔÇö emitted + admitted), per-block dst-dedup (FB14 ÔÇö applied set monotonicity), and per-block source debit + accumulator (FB18 ÔÇö A1 source-mass departure). FB17 (AppliedReceiptRestore) sits orthogonal at the snapshot/restore lifecycle. The structural asymmetries between source-side (FB18) and destination-side (FB14):

1. **No dedup primitive on source.** FB18 has no `applied_outbound_receipts` analog because the source emits each cross-shard receipt exactly once per source tx (V12 ÔÇö Lemma L-7.1 ÔÇö binds receipts 1:1 to txs). The model's `pending_receipts.Append` is the structural witness ÔÇö every successful ApplyCrossShardTransfer extends the receipt seq by exactly one entry.
2. **No idempotency contract on source.** A double-submit of the same tx (same from/to/amount/fee tuple) on source produces two debits and two receipts ÔÇö the nonce gate at chain.cpp:739 catches this in production (FB7 territory); FB18 abstracts the nonce as the SubmitTransfer's adversarial freedom but doesn't model the gate (orthogonal concern).
3. **No snapshot survival concern on source.** Pre-S-037 the destination's dedup set was at risk on restore (FB17 closure); the source's `accumulated_outbound` field has always survived restore because it's a single Nat-typed accumulator covered by the safety-critical state_root namespace at chain.cpp:408. FB18 confirms this via the absence of a Snapshot/Restore action pair in its action set.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/CrossShardOutboundApply.md` (separately written by a parallel agent).
### NefPoolDrain.tla Ôćĺ E1 NEF pool drain state machine (SubmitRegister / ApplyFirstRegister / ApplyReRegister)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `registrants` (SUBSET Domains), `balances` (AllAddresses Ôćĺ 0..InitialNefPool ÔÇö includes ZerothAddress as the pool home), `pending_register` (Seq(Domains)), `height` (Nat action counter) |
| `Inv_PoolNonNegative` | `balances[ZerothAddress] >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö the floor-half drain (`P \div 2`) is closed on Nat; once the pool reaches 0, the terminal `0 \div 2 = 0` keeps it there |
| `Inv_GeometricExhaustion` | T-N1 quantified upper bound: for every `k \in 0..|Domains|`, if `|registrants| >= k` then `2^k * balances[ZerothAddress] <= InitialNefPool`. The K-th distinct first-time register applies the K-th floor-half; arithmetic gives `pool <= floor(P / 2^K)`. The headline geometric-drain witness ÔÇö pre-existing FB11 had only the non-negativity floor, not the upper-bound progression |
| `Inv_A1Conservation` | T-N5 supply identity: `balances[ZerothAddress] + sum_{d \in Domains} balances[d] = InitialNefPool` at every reachable state. Every NEF action is an internal poolÔćĺdomain redistribution; no action mints or destroys. The sentinel-balance pattern collapses the FB11 `nef_pool` + `accounts` two-variable identity into a single sum-of-balances identity |
| `Inv_DrainOnlyOnFirstRegister` | T-N2 action-level invariant: any `balances'[ZerothAddress] < balances[ZerothAddress]` step must be paired with a fresh domain entering `registrants`. The headline defense against the registration-churn drain attack ÔÇö re-register cannot drain. Matches the `first_time_register` bool gate at `src/chain/chain.cpp:795-796` |
| `Prop_EventualExhaustion` (temporal) | T-N6 eventual-progress: under fairness on SubmitRegister + ApplyFirstRegister, eventually `balances[ZerothAddress] = 0` OR `|registrants| = |Domains|` (all domains have first-registered and the pool has drained as far as the model's domain budget permits). The escape branch is required because TLC operates on bounded models ÔÇö for `InitialNefPool = 8, |Domains| = 3`, the pool reaches 1 (not 0) after 3 first-registers; further drain requires more domains |
| `Prop_RegistrationIsTerminal` (temporal) | T-N7 action-level: `d \in registrants => d \in registrants'` across every `[Next]_vars` step. Once a domain enters registrants, it stays. No Deregister action is modeled in this scope ÔÇö for the NEF drain surface, registration is one-way and permanent. The temporal witness that the floor-half drain is monotone over the registrants partial order |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other eleven specs above). The configuration in `NefPoolDrain.cfg` (3 domains {a, b, c}, InitialNefPool=8, MaxHeight=4, ZerothAddress=zeroth sentinel) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. Variables modeled: `registrants` (SUBSET Domains ÔÇö the set of domains that have first-registered), `balances` (AllAddresses Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö collapses the C++ `accounts_` map + the ZEROTH-address pool into a single function indexed by Domains \cup {ZerothAddress}; the sentinel-pattern lifts the A1 supply identity into a sum-of-balances over the lifted index set), `pending_register` (Seq(Domains) ÔÇö the submitted-but-not-applied register-tx queue; matches the C++ apply order at chain.cpp:734 `for (auto& tx : b.transactions)`), `height` (Nat ÔÇö action counter bounding TLC). Actions modeled: `SubmitRegister` (any caller can submit any domain for register ÔÇö the adversarial surface), `ApplyFirstRegister` (the first-time apply branch at chain.cpp:813-833 ÔÇö drains pool by floor-half, credits drained amount, adds domain to registrants), `ApplyReRegister` (the already-registered apply branch ÔÇö consumes from pending without mutating drain state, witnesses T-N3). InitialNefPool=8 lets the floor-half drain fire 4 times (8 Ôćĺ 4 Ôćĺ 2 Ôćĺ 1 Ôćĺ 0) before reaching the absorbing 0-state; with 3 domains the model exhausts at pool=1 after 3 first-registers (T-N1 K=3 case). The T-N4 zero-pool noop branch (pool=0 Ôćĺ ApplyFirstRegister with 0 drain) is not reachable in the 3-domain InitialNefPool=8 cfg but is structurally witnessed by the ApplyFirstRegister action body ÔÇö the same `drain = pool \div 2` formula, evaluated at pool=0, yields 0 with no further mutation; reproducibly reachable in a 4-domain InitialNefPool=8 or 3-domain InitialNefPool=4 cfg variant.

**Distinction from FB11 SubsidyDistribution.tla:** the two specs together cover the NEF drain from complementary angles. FB11 models the NEF drain alongside block-subsidy distribution and collapses Submit + Apply into a single Register action (the apply-side enforcement is the focus); FB19 zooms in on the NEF-only surface and pulls the submit/apply lifecycle into an explicit pending sequence so the apply-order semantics + the re-register stutter are observable at the state-machine layer. The FB11 `Inv_NefDrainsOnceperDomain` is the action-level pair (registered FALSEÔćĺTRUE) witness; FB19's `Inv_DrainOnlyOnFirstRegister` is the same claim restated in terms of the registrants-set delta (set-membership growth). The headline FB19-specific invariant is `Inv_GeometricExhaustion` ÔÇö the quantified upper bound `2^k * pool <= InitialNefPool` is not present in FB11; FB19 elevates the floor-half drain semantics to a parametric inequality over the number of distinct first-registers.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/NefPoolDrain.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).
### MultiEventComposition.tla Ôćĺ composed per-block apply pipeline (Construct / Apply / AdvanceHeight)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | T-MC1: shape of `balances` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat), `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat), `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey ÔÇö shared with FB14), `accumulated_outbound` (Nat ÔÇö write-only outbound counter), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat ÔÇö shared FB15+FB16 accumulator), `height` (0..MaxHeight*3), `pending_block` (PendingBlock record with four sub-event SUBSET fields, or NoPendingBlock sentinel) |
| `Inv_A1Conservation` | T-MC2: supply-axis identity across composed apply. `SumStakes + accumulated_slashed <= Cardinality(Domains) * MaxStake` ÔÇö slashing rebooks stake mass into the accumulator; total stake-axis mass is preserved across every ApplyBlock step. The composed step decrements stakes[d] by `abort_slash + equiv_slash` and increments accumulated_slashed by the same sum across all domains, preserving the bound. The transfer + receipt + subsidy side of the supply identity is FB5 / FB10 / FB11 territory and inherited via the per-event-invariants-compose conjunction |
| `Inv_DeterministicOrder` | T-MC3: the headline composition contract. When `pending_block /= NoPendingBlock`, ConstructBlock is structurally disabled (its pre-condition requires `pending_block = NoPendingBlock`), so the only balance/stake-mutating action is the deterministic ApplyBlock. Apply order within the block is fixed at the C++ source-line level (chain.cpp:734 tx loop Ôćĺ 1313 abort loop Ôćĺ 1344 equiv loop Ôćĺ 1363 receipt loop Ôćĺ 1286 distribution loop); the spec's single-step ApplyBlock transition is the state-machine witness of that fixed ordering |
| `Inv_PerEventInvariantsCompose` | T-MC4: the conjunction of the most-load-bearing single-event invariants, each lifted from its source spec. (a) `balances[d] >= 0` (FB5 / FB10), (b) `stakes[d] >= 0` (FB15 / FB16), (c) `accumulated_slashed >= 0` (FB15 / FB16), (d) `accumulated_outbound >= 0` (FB2 / FB14), (e) every dedup-key has the DedupKey shape (FB14 T-R3). The invariant is the structural witness that COMPOSITION does not break ANY single-event invariant ÔÇö TLC exhausts every ConstructBlock + ApplyBlock interleaving within the model bound |
| `Inv_AppliedReceiptsMonotonic` | FB14 T-R4 lifted to the composition layer: applied_receipts is set-only-grows. ApplyBlock only extends (via `applied_receipts \cup {DedupKeyOf(r) : r \in fresh_receipts}`); ConstructBlock and AdvanceHeight preserve. The structural witness of cross-block dedup persistence under composition |
| `Inv_SlashedMonotonic` | FB15 / FB16 lifted: `accumulated_slashed >= 0` and no action decreases it. The shared slash-accumulator's monotonicity holds across all four sub-event apply paths (transfers, receipts, subsidies do not touch it; aborts + equivocations only add) |
| `Inv_OutboundMonotonic` | FB2 / FB14 lifted: `accumulated_outbound >= 0`. The write-only outbound counter is preserved by ApplyBlock (the spec's apply path does not emit cross-shard outbound ÔÇö that surface is the source-chain's block-finalize stage, modeled in the companion `MultiEventComposition.md` prose proof) |
| `Prop_EventualApply` (temporal) | T-MC6: under WF on ApplyBlock, any pending block eventually drains. The state-level form: `pending_block /= NoPendingBlock => <>(pending_block = NoPendingBlock)`. Combined with the AdvanceHeight stutter, gives the eventual-apply progress guarantee under fairness |
| `Prop_ReplayMatch` (temporal) | T-MC5: after ApplyBlock fires, `applied_receipts` contains every dedup-key from the block's receipts sub-event set. A hypothetical re-apply of the same block would route every receipt through the duplicate branch (FB14 dedup gate), preserving the end-state. The structural witness of the apply-idempotency contract that snapshot/restore + replay depend on |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other eleven specs above). The configuration in `MultiEventComposition.cfg` (3 domains, MaxAmount=2, MaxStake=5, MaxHeight=3, 2 hashes, 2 shards) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `balances` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö per-domain balance ledger), `stakes` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö per-domain locked stake), `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey ÔÇö cross-block dedup set; shape shared with FB14), `accumulated_outbound` (Nat ÔÇö write-only outbound counter), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat ÔÇö shared FB15+FB16 accumulator at chain.cpp:1395), `height` (Nat ÔÇö action counter), `pending_block` (PendingBlock record or NoPendingBlock sentinel). Actions modeled: `ConstructBlock(ts, abs, eqs, rs)` (non-deterministic block admission with bounded sub-event set sizes; the ONLY non-determinism point per T-MC3), `ApplyBlock` (the canonical apply pipeline ÔÇö composes transfers, aborts, equivocations, and receipts into a single deterministic transition matching the C++ chain.cpp:734-1305 apply loop order), `AdvanceHeight` (temporal driver / stutter). The four sub-event classes are bounded at ConstructBlock admission (transfers <= 2, aborts <= 1, equivs <= 1, receipts <= 1) to keep the SUBSET state-space tractable.

This spec is the FB-track composition of FB5 (AccountState ÔÇö transfers), FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup ÔÇö receipts), FB15 (EquivocationApply ÔÇö equivocations), FB16 (AbortApply ÔÇö aborts), and FB10 (FeeAccounting) + FB11 (SubsidyDistribution) ÔÇö fee + subsidy distribution. Each prior spec verifies its sub-event class in isolation; FB20 verifies that COMPOSITION does not break any single-event invariant AND that the canonical apply order is fixed at the C++ source-line level. The deterministic-pipeline contract (T-MC3) is the headline composition-spec property ÔÇö validators receiving sub-event sequences in any interleaving across producer-aggregation + gossip + admission ALL produce the same post-apply state because the C++ apply path replays in the canonical order regardless of arrival order. The DedupKey type is shared verbatim with FB14, ensuring the cross-block dedup-set's structure is preserved under composition.

### StakeForfeitureCascade.tla Ôćĺ STAKE / DEREGISTER / UNSTAKE / Equivocate cascade state machine

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | T-C1: shape of `accounts` (Domains Ôćĺ [balance, stake_locked]), `registrants` (Domains Ôćĺ [active, inactive_from]), `unlock_heights` (Domains Ôćĺ 0..Sentinel), `accumulated_slashed` (0..INITIAL_TOTAL_VALUE), `height` (0..MaxHeight), `pending` (Seq(Event) with kind Ôłł {STAKE, DEREGISTER, UNSTAKE, EQUIVOCATE}) |
| `Inv_StakeNonNegative` | T-C2: `accounts[d].stake_locked >= 0` at every reachable state ÔÇö the composed cascade never drives the field negative. Nat-typed; documents the contract. ApplyStake adds, UnstakePost zeroes, ApplyEquivocate zeroes; no action subtracts below 0 |
| `Inv_NoBalanceOnSlashedAccount` | T-C3: structural witness that an Equivocate-deactivated registry entry (active=FALSE AND inactive_from /= Sentinel AND inactive_from = height OR inactive_from = height + 1) has stake_locked = 0 post-slash ÔÇö the headline "slash is one-way, full-forfeiture is permanent" claim lifted into the cascade |
| `Inv_A1Conservation` | T-C6: composed cascade supply identity: `SumBalances + SumStakes + accumulated_slashed = INITIAL_TOTAL_VALUE` at every reachable state. The headline supply-conservation claim for the full cascade. Every action preserves the sum: ApplyStake is balance Ôćĺ stake_locked, UnstakePost is stake_locked Ôćĺ balance, ApplyEquivocate is stake_locked Ôćĺ accumulated_slashed (rebooking), all other actions are stutters on the value-bearing variables |
| `Inv_UnstakePostSlashIsNoOp` | T-C4: post-slash UnstakePost is harmless. Action-form: applying UnstakePost when stake_locked[d] = 0 is a stutter on (balance, stake_locked) ÔÇö balance' = balance + 0 = balance. The structural witness that the post-slash UnstakePost compose-then-fire ordering does not double-credit the offender. Matches the C++ apply-path's `sit->second.locked -= amount` reduction at locked=0 |
| `Inv_OrderSensitivity` | T-C5: action-form witness that Equivocate-then-UnstakePost vs UnstakePost-then-Equivocate yield diverging (balance) end-states. The composed cascade is order-sensitive on (balance) but order-insensitive on (stake_locked, accumulated_slashed-sum). TLC enumerates both branches under the action interleaving and verifies the two distinct end-states are reachable. The headline "composition outcome depends on event order" claim of FB21 |
| `Inv_SlashedMonotonic` | FB15 lifted to the cascade: `accumulated_slashed >= 0` and no action decreases it. ApplyEquivocate only adds, all other actions preserve. Cross-cascade verification that the FB15 monotonicity is robust under the cascade interleaving |
| `Inv_UnlockMonotonic` | FB8 lifted to the cascade: per-domain `unlock_heights[d]` is monotone non-decreasing across every `[Next]_vars` step. ApplyDeregister arms, UnstakePost clears-to-Sentinel (the largest possible value, > MaxHeight + UnstakeDelay + 1 by ConfigOK). Cross-cascade verification of FB8's headline non-decrease claim |
| `Prop_EventualResolution` (temporal) | T-C7: under WF on AdvanceHeight + each Apply* action, the pending queue eventually drains to empty OR the model bound is reached (`height >= MaxHeight`). Apply-time progress guarantee for the full cascade; the bounded-model escape clause keeps TLC tractable |
| `Prop_NoDoubleForfeit` (temporal) | T-C8: across every `[Next]_vars` step, a single domain contributes at most pre-step `stake_locked[d]` to accumulated_slashed. The second equivocation for the same offender hits the ApplyEquivocateGhost branch and contributes 0 ÔÇö the structural witness of FB15 T-E4 lifted into the cascade. Combined with `Inv_SlashedMonotonic`, gives the full "an account can only be fully-slashed once" guarantee |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twelve specs above). The configuration in `StakeForfeitureCascade.cfg` (2 domains {a, b}, MaxHeight=4, MaxStake=5, UnstakeDelay=2, Sentinel=1000) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `accounts` (Domains Ôćĺ [balance: Nat, stake_locked: Nat] ÔÇö collapses the C++ `accounts_` balance + `stakes_` locked fields into a single record per domain since the cascade is the smallest scope where they must be tracked atomically), `registrants` (Domains Ôćĺ [active: BOOLEAN, inactive_from: 0..Sentinel] ÔÇö same shape as FB8 + FB15), `unlock_heights` (Domains Ôćĺ 0..Sentinel ÔÇö the FB8 unlock-arming field), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat ÔÇö shared with FB15 / FB16 / FB20 via the chain.cpp:1395 accumulator), `height` (Nat ÔÇö chain-height action counter, bounds TLC), `pending` (Seq(Event) ÔÇö admission queue with FIFO drain). Actions modeled: `SubmitStake`, `SubmitDeregister`, `SubmitUnstake`, `SubmitEquivocate` (adversarial admission ÔÇö the validator could be byzantine; the apply-layer guards filter out the truly invalid claims), `ApplyStake` (balance Ôćĺ stake_locked move on success), `ApplyStakeReject` (insufficient-balance silent-skip stutter), `ApplyDeregister` (arms unlock_height = height + 1 + UnstakeDelay), `ApplyDeregisterRejectAlreadyInactive` (second-DEREGISTER stutter ÔÇö FB8 stricter model), `UnstakePre` (pre-unlock fee-refund branch at chain.cpp:881-888), `UnstakePost` (post-unlock refund branch at chain.cpp:889-893), `ApplyEquivocate` (full forfeiture + registry deactivation ÔÇö chain.cpp:1344-1356), `ApplyEquivocateGhost` (stake_locked = 0 second-equivocation no-op ÔÇö FB15 T-E4), `AdvanceHeight` (temporal driver). UnstakeDelay=2 + MaxHeight=4 gives the model enough headroom to exercise both pre-unlock and post-unlock UNSTAKE attempts under either ordering with Equivocate.

The headline cross-domain coverage matrix:

  * **Stake Ôćĺ Deregister Ôćĺ wait Ôćĺ Unstake** (happy path; FB8 territory verified as the no-slash baseline)
  * **Stake Ôćĺ Equivocate** (immediate slash; stake_locked Ôćĺ 0 / accumulated_slashed += stake)
  * **Stake Ôćĺ Deregister Ôćĺ Equivocate Ôćĺ UnstakePost** (order A ÔÇö slash first; UnstakePost is no-op per T-C4)
  * **Stake Ôćĺ Deregister Ôćĺ UnstakePost Ôćĺ Equivocate** (order B ÔÇö Unstake first; Equivocate hits ghost branch per T-C8)
  * **Stake Ôćĺ UnstakePre (pre-unlock)** (fee-refund stutter; FB8 UnstakeFailEarly lifted)
  * **Stake Ôćĺ Equivocate Ôćĺ Equivocate** (second equivocation hits ghost branch; T-C8 verifies it contributes 0)
  * **Two-domain isolation**: cross-domain "slash one, don't touch the other" ÔÇö Inv_A1Conservation across the second domain witnesses the slash is account-scoped

The order-sensitivity contract (T-C5) is the distinguishing claim of FB21 against its predecessors. FB8 verifies the happy-path lifecycle in isolation (no equivocation surface). FB15 verifies the slash lifecycle in isolation (no UNSTAKE surface). FB16 verifies bounded slashing in isolation (no full-forfeiture surface; the `std::min` floor). FB20 verifies the composed pipeline at the block level, but the four sub-event classes apply within a single canonical step and there is no in-block ordering ambiguity to observe. FB21 zooms in on the STAKE-axis specifically and admits the cross-event interleaving across BLOCK boundaries ÔÇö the same account can have a STAKE event admitted in block N, a DEREGISTER in block N+1, an EQUIVOCATE and an UNSTAKE both submitted (in either order) for block N+2 ÔÇö and TLC exhausts every reachable ordering. The diverging end-states (balance = pre-stake-balance vs balance = pre-stake-balance + amount) witness that the cascade is composition-order-sensitive on value but composition-order-invariant on slash mass.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/StakeForfeitureCascade.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).

### F2ViewReconciliation.tla Ôćĺ v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives (compute_view_root / reconcile_union / reconcile_intersection + V21..V26)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `contribs` (MemberIds Ôćĺ ContribMsg with three (root, list) pairs), `block_eq` / `block_abort` / `block_inbound` (each `\subseteq Hashes`), `generated` (BOOLEAN bit gating the post-enumeration invariants) |
| `INV_UnionMonotonic` | INV-1: adding any honest member's list to the K-committee can only GROW the union. State-form: every hash committed by any member appears in `block_eq`. Structural witness of the reconcile_union loop body at `src/node/producer.cpp:347-350` (`for (auto& list : member_lists) for (auto& h : list) u.insert(h);`) ÔÇö SET semantics dedupes, but each member's contribution can only ADD to the running set, never subtract |
| `INV_IntersectionAntiMonotonic` | INV-2: adding any list (including an EMPTY one) can only SHRINK the intersection. State-form: every hash in `block_inbound` appears in EVERY member's `view_inbound_list`. Structural witness of the reconcile_intersection iterative-shrink loop at `src/node/producer.cpp:362-369` (`std::set_intersection` produces `tmp ÔŐć isect` on every iteration, and the early-exit at `isect.empty()` confirms the empty-set absorbing element) |
| `INV_OrderIndependent` | INV-3: ReconcileUnion(perm(L)) = ReconcileUnion(L) for every permutation P of the member ordering; same for ReconcileIntersection. The Q3 canonical-sort guarantee ÔÇö producer's choice of member ordering does not change the canonical lists every validator re-derives. SET-based primitives over an indexed family are intrinsically domain-permutation-invariant (the SET of mapped values is unchanged); the C++ side's `std::set` insertion + `std::set_intersection` both produce sorted outputs regardless of input iteration order |
| `INV_UnionIdempotent` | INV-4: if every member commits the same list (as a SET), the canonical union equals that single member's SET. The duplicate-merge contract ÔÇö three members all observing `{ev1, ev2}` produces `{ev1, ev2}` (not `{ev1, ev1, ev1, ev2, ev2, ev2}`). Structural witness of the `std::set<Hash>` container's idempotent insertion at producer.cpp:347 ÔÇö `u.insert(h)` on an already-present element is a no-op |
| `INV_UnionCensorshipResistant` | INV-5: F2 censorship resistance (FA2 lift). If AT LEAST ONE member committed `h` in their view_eq_list, `h` must be in the F2 canonical equivocation set. The Q1 union-rule contract: a single honest observer is sufficient to land slashing evidence. Combined with FA6 equivocation-slashing soundness, gives the end-to-end "one honest committee member suffices to slash an equivocating offender" property. Structural witness: every `h` in any member's list flows through the producer.cpp:349 insertion into the merged set |
| `INV_IntersectionConservative` | INV-6: F2 conservative inbound ÔÇö `h Ôłł block_inbound` IFF EVERY member's list contains `h`. The Q1 intersection-rule biconditional: one bad relayer cannot unilaterally cause credit (Ôçĺ direction), AND a unanimous observation guarantees inclusion (ÔçÉ direction). Structural witness: the producer.cpp:357-372 iterative `std::set_intersection` reduces to the K-fold intersection, which by definition contains exactly the elements present in all K input sets |
| `INV_AllContribsValid` | V21..V24 reachability: every generated contrib passes the per-contrib well-formedness check. V21: each `view_X_list` length ÔëĄ CAP = 64. V22..V24: each claimed root equals `ComputeViewRoot(view_X_list)`. The HonestContrib helper enforces V22..V24 by construction (each root field is computed from its paired list); the BoundedSeqs ceiling enforces V21. Matches the validator's per-contrib gate at `src/node/producer.cpp:391-436` (validate_contrib_view_roots) |
| `INV_BlockReconcilesContribs` | V25..V26 reachability: the block's canonical lists exactly match the F2 reconciliation of the K contribs. V25 (union over equivocation_events + abort_events) + V26 (intersection over inbound_receipts). The DeriveCanonical helper enforces this by construction; the GenerateHonest action sets `block_X' = canonical.X` after enumerating the per-member views. Matches the validator's composite gate at `src/node/producer.cpp:458-496` (validate_view_reconciliation) |
| `INV_BandwidthCapHonored` | F2-SPEC ┬žQ3 bandwidth budget: every view-list ÔëĄ F2_VIEW_LIST_CAP = 64. Holds by construction of `BoundedSeqs` (which is bounded above by `|Hashes|` ÔëĄ CAP in the recommended .cfg). Matches the C++ guard at producer.cpp:407-417 (`if (msg.view_X_list.size() > F2_VIEW_LIST_CAP) return false;`) and the F2_VIEW_LIST_CAP constant at `include/determ/node/producer.hpp:212` |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other thirteen specs above). The recommended `F2ViewReconciliation.cfg` (K=3, Hashes={h1, h2, h3}, CAP=64) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The reconciliation primitives are pure functions; the algebraic invariants (INV-1..INV-6) hold structurally, so the GenerateHonest action's job is to enumerate every reachable per-member assignment over the bounded Hash universe and let TLC verify the invariants against each one. Variables modeled: `contribs` (function MemberIds Ôćĺ ContribMsg with three `[root, list]` field-pairs ÔÇö matches the C++ `ContribMsg` extension at `include/determ/node/types.hpp` view_eq_root + view_eq_list etc.), `block_eq` / `block_abort` / `block_inbound` (SETs of Hashes ÔÇö the spec-layer representation of the canonical lists; the C++ side's sorted-vector representation is bijective on sets), `generated` (BOOLEAN bit ÔÇö TRUE once GenerateHonest fires, gates the post-enumeration invariants from spuriously firing at the empty-Init state). Actions modeled: `GenerateHonest` (single non-deterministic enumeration of K honest contribs + the F2-derived canonical block lists; produces ONLY V21..V26-passing tuples by construction), `Stutter` (post-generation no-op; TLC verifies the invariants persist at the reachable end-state).

The state-machine driver is intentionally minimal because the primitives under test are pure functions ÔÇö the algebraic claims being verified hold over EVERY possible per-member assignment, not just the ones produced by a particular protocol trace. The enumeration covers every reachable `(eq_assign, ab_assign, inb_assign) Ôłł [MemberIds Ôćĺ BoundedSeqs]┬│` tuple within the bounded Hash universe; for |Hashes|=3 and K=3, BoundedSeqs has 1 + 3 + 9 + 27 = 40 elements (sequences of length 0, 1, 2, 3 with replacement), giving 40^9 Ôëł 2.6├Ś10^14 raw assignments before TLC's symmetry-reduction. The SET-form invariants collapse this dramatically: any two assignments producing the same per-member SETs are equivalent for INV-1..INV-6, so the practical state-space TLC explores is at the level of distinct per-member SET-tuples ÔÇö roughly 2^|Hashes| = 8 per slot, giving 8^9 Ôëł 1.3├Ś10^8 distinct equivalence classes. Even under the worst-case enumeration, the per-state INV-* check is constant-time over the K-member committee.

This spec captures the consensus-view soundness of the v2.7 F2 ship that closes the S-030 D2 footnote in `Safety.md` ┬ž5.3 and the open audit finding in `SECURITY.md` ┬žS-030. Combined with the apply-layer S-033 + S-038 closure (the producer's `body.state_root` population per the S-038 wiring) and FA1's existing per-height safety machinery, F2 lifts FA1's conclusion from "ÔëĄ 1 digest per height + footnote" to "ÔëĄ 1 block instance per height" ÔÇö the consensus + apply layers now jointly cover every consensus-bound field of the Block record. The reconciliation primitives are the structural witnesses of that lift: they are deterministic, order-independent, and idempotent over the K contributors' view commitments, so every honest validator re-derives the same canonical lists from the same K Phase-1 commits regardless of gossip arrival order.

Companion prose specification: `docs/proofs/F2-SPEC.md` (the design document; this TLA+ spec formalizes the ┬žQ1 reconciliation rules + ┬žQ3 bandwidth cap + ┬žQ5 Phase-2 signature semantics at the state-machine layer). The FA1 safety proof (`docs/proofs/Safety.md` ┬ž5.3) will be updated to remove the D2 footnote once F2 ships; the prose update is tracked separately under the v2.7 ship workstream.

### FrostVerify.tla Ôćĺ FA-Crypto-Verify (FROST-Ed25519 verify soundness via Ed25519 delegation)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `key_pubs` (total function `Keys Ôćĺ GroupPubKeyT` with each pub a 32-element sequence over Bytes), `generated` (SUBSET of Keys ÔÇö tracks which identifiers have been bound by `GenKeypair`), `signed_sigs` (SUBSET of `Keys ├Ś Messages ├Ś FrostSigT` ÔÇö the canonical-aggregate set produced by `SignMessage`), `valid_pairs` (SUBSET of `GroupPubKeyT ├Ś Messages ├Ś FrostSigT` ÔÇö the abstract `Ed25519Verify` acceptance relation populated only by honest signing per EUF-CMA A2), `tampered_sigs` (SUBSET of FrostSigT ÔÇö byte-tampered variants), `verify_log` (Seq of records `[pub, msg, sig, result, case]` ÔÇö the observable history of verify calls indexed by scenario tag), `scenario` (Ôłł {"init", "keygen", "signed", "verified"} ÔÇö phase marker) |
| `INV_RoundTripSoundness` | INV-1: for any canonical aggregate signature produced by `SignMessage` over `msg` under `key_pubs[k]`, `FrostVerify(sig, key_pubs[k], msg)` returns TRUE. Models T-1 forward direction in `FrostVerifyDelegation.md` ┬ž3 (the analytic proof's L-1 + L-2 + delegation chain). State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "canonical"` has `result = TRUE`. Structural witness of the runtime regression at `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 1 (`frost_verify: round-trip with real Ed25519 sig PASSES`) |
| `INV_TamperRejection` | INV-2: for any byte-tampered sig (`sig' Ôëá canonical sig`), `FrostVerify(sig', pub, msg) = FALSE`. Models corollary T-1.1 (tampered-signature rejection) under the Ed25519 EUF-CMA assumption A2 (forging an Ed25519 sig under an honest key has probability ÔëĄ 2Ôü╗┬╣┬▓ÔüŞ per attempt; the spec abstracts that bound to determinism via `valid_pairs` membership). State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "tampered_sig"` has `result = FALSE`. The `Tamper` action's universal-quantifier clause `\A k2 Ôłł generated : \A m2 Ôłł Messages : <<key_pubs[k2], m2, sig_prime>> \notin valid_pairs` makes the rejection structural. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 2 (`frost_verify: tampered signature byte REJECTED`) |
| `INV_WrongKeyRejection` | INV-3: for any canonical aggregate produced under `group_pub_A`, verification against any distinct `group_pub_B` returns FALSE. Models corollary T-1.2 (wrong-key rejection) under Ed25519 EUF-CMA. State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "wrong_key"` has `result = FALSE`. The `VerifyWrongKey` action filters `k_other` by `key_pubs[k_other] Ôëá key_pubs[k]`; `valid_pairs` only contains `<<key_pubs[k], msg, sig>>` (not `<<key_pubs[k_other], msg, sig>>`), so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 3 (`frost_verify: wrong group pubkey REJECTED`) |
| `INV_TamperedMsgRejection` | INV-4: for any canonical aggregate produced over `msg`, verification against any distinct `msg' Ôëá msg` returns FALSE. Models corollary T-1.3 (tampered-message rejection) under Ed25519 EUF-CMA + SHA-512 collision resistance (the challenge `c = H2(R ÔÇľ group_pubkey ÔÇľ msg')` differs from `c(msg)` except in the negligible 2Ôü╗┬▓ÔüÁÔüÂ collision case). State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "tampered_msg"` has `result = FALSE`. The `VerifyTamperedMsg` action filters `msg_other` by `msg_other Ôëá msg`; `valid_pairs` only contains the original-message triple, so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 4 (`frost_verify: tampered message REJECTED`) |
| `INV_EmptyMsgWellDefined` | INV-5: the `FrostVerify` operator is total over `(FrostSigT ├Ś GroupPubKeyT ├Ś Messages)`, including the empty-message case (RFC 8032 ┬ž5.1 PureEdDSA explicitly supports zero-length input). The C++ implementation at `src/crypto/frost.cpp:117` passes `message.data(), message.size()` directly into `determ::crypto::verify` without an early-return on `message.empty()`; the spec-layer assertion is "every `verify_log` entry has `result Ôłł BOOLEAN`" ÔÇö well-typedness of the verify result regardless of `|msg|`. Guards against any future regression that would split the verify path on message length. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 5 (`frost_verify: empty-message round-trip PASSES`) |
| `INV_TypeContract` | INV-6: the structural type contract pinned by the two `static_assert` clauses at `src/crypto/frost.cpp:108` (`sizeof(FrostSig) == sizeof(Signature)` ÔÇö both 64 bytes, `R ÔÇľ z`) and `:113` (`sizeof(Point) == sizeof(PubKey)` ÔÇö both 32 bytes, Ed25519 compressed point). Every FrostSig in the model is a 64-element sequence over Bytes; every GroupPubKey is a 32-element sequence. RFC 9591 ┬ž6.6 + RFC 8032 ┬ž5.1.7 fix these encoded sizes; the static_asserts give compile-time evidence at the C++ layer; the TLA+ assertion is a sequence-length invariant on `signed_sigs[3]`, `tampered_sigs`, `key_pubs[k]`, and the `pub` / `sig` fields of every `verify_log` entry |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-one specs above). The recommended `FrostVerify.cfg` (Keys = {k1, k2}, Messages = {m1, m2}, Bytes = {b0, b1}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 10 seconds on a single core. The five-action workflow (GenKeypair Ôćĺ SignMessage Ôćĺ Tamper Ôćĺ Verify{Canonical, Tampered, WrongKey, TamperedMsg}) enumerates every reachable combination of (signed-set ├Ś tampered-set ├Ś verify-call) up to the bounded universe; the four phase markers in `scenario` ({"init", "keygen", "signed", "verified"}) sequence the actions and bound the state space. Variables modeled: `key_pubs` (function `Keys Ôćĺ GroupPubKeyT` ÔÇö the modeled pubkey value for each generated keypair identifier; `[k \in Keys |-> ZeroPubBytes]` at Init, overwritten by `GenKeypair`'s `EXCEPT` clause), `generated` (SUBSET of Keys ÔÇö tracks which identifiers have been bound, distinct from `DOMAIN key_pubs` because the function is total at Init), `signed_sigs` (SUBSET of `Keys ├Ś Messages ├Ś FrostSigT` ÔÇö the canonical-aggregate set), `valid_pairs` (SUBSET of `GroupPubKeyT ├Ś Messages ├Ś FrostSigT` ÔÇö the abstract Ed25519Verify acceptance relation populated only by honest signing), `tampered_sigs` (SUBSET of FrostSigT ÔÇö byte-tampered variants guaranteed disjoint from any canonical triple under any `(pub, msg)` combination), `verify_log` (Seq of records ÔÇö the observable history; indexed by scenario tag so INV-1..INV-5 can be evaluated per-case), `scenario` (Ôłł {"init", "keygen", "signed", "verified"}). Actions modeled: `GenKeypair` (nondeterministically pick a fresh key identifier + a 32-byte pubkey value), `SignMessage` (atomically populate `signed_sigs Ôł¬= {<<k, msg, sig>>}` and `valid_pairs Ôł¬= {<<key_pubs[k], msg, sig>>}` ÔÇö the joint extension captures RFC 9591 ┬ž3 Theorem 1's "aggregate is a structural Ed25519 sig" property), `Tamper` (extend `tampered_sigs` with a byte-tampered variant + universally assert non-membership in `valid_pairs`), `VerifyCanonical` / `VerifyTampered` / `VerifyWrongKey` / `VerifyTamperedMsg` (call `FrostVerify` and log the result under the appropriate scenario tag).

The state-machine driver is intentionally minimal because the property under test is the soundness of a pure-function delegation contract ÔÇö `FrostVerify(sig, pub, msg) == Ed25519Verify(pub, msg, sig)` per the analytic proof's L-2 ÔÇö and the algebraic claims (INV-1..INV-6) hold over every reachable `(signed_sigs, valid_pairs, tampered_sigs)` tuple. The `valid_pairs` set is the spec-layer abstraction of the Ed25519 EUF-CMA assumption A2 (Preliminaries ┬ž2.2): only honestly-signed `(pub, msg, sig)` triples are in the set, and any triple absent from it represents the "forgery fails" branch (concrete bound ÔëĄ 2Ôü╗┬╣┬▓ÔüŞ per attempt; the spec abstracts to determinism). The `Tamper` action's universal-quantifier clause is the structural enforcement of EUF-CMA at the state-machine layer: every byte-tampered sig is explicitly excluded from `valid_pairs` under every `(pub, msg)` combination, capturing the "no polynomial-time adversary can forge" assumption deterministically. The state-space TLC explores is at the level of the workflow trace through the four scenario phases ├Ś the bounded keypair / message / byte universes; the recommended config gives roughly `2 keys ├Ś 2 messages ├Ś 2^64 sigs ├Ś 2^32 pubs = 2^99` raw triples, but TLC's symmetry reduction + the canonical-set semantics collapses this to under 10┬│ distinct reachable workflow states.

This spec captures the verify-side soundness of the v2.10 Phase A `frost_verify` primitive ÔÇö the first FROST-Ed25519 primitive shipped end-to-end (per `F2-V210-IMPLEMENTATION-PLAN.md` Phase A ┬ž123). The primitive is a thin delegation to `determ::crypto::verify` (the existing OpenSSL EVP_PKEY_ED25519 wrapper at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:79-91`); the soundness reduces to L-1 (RFC 9591 ┬ž3 Theorem 1: FROST aggregate is a structural Ed25519 sig) + L-2 (`determ::crypto::verify` wraps RFC 8032 ┬ž5.1.7 cofactored verify). Combined with the existing FA6 equivocation-slashing proof (which already depends on Ed25519 EUF-CMA over honest validator keys) and the upcoming FA-Crypto-DKG + FA-Crypto-Sign tracks (v2.10 Phases B + D), this spec gives the verify-side state-machine soundness that future v2.10 randomness-binding consumers (block-validation under `randomness_root`; FA3 selective-abort proof regression) can be drafted against.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `FrostVerifyDelegation.md` ┬ž5):
- DKG ceremony soundness (`v2.10-DKG-SPEC.md` + future FA-Crypto-DKG proof when Phase B ships).
- Threshold-signing protocol soundness (v2.10 Phase D ÔÇö future FA-Crypto-Sign proof).
- Side-channel resistance of the underlying Ed25519 implementation (OpenSSL's constant-time guarantee is per their documentation; not modeled at the TLA+ layer).
- Byte-level enumeration of the Ed25519 verify equation (`[8 ┬Ě z] ┬Ě G == [8] ┬Ě R + [8 ┬Ě c] ┬Ě group_pubkey`) ÔÇö the spec models `Ed25519Verify` as an abstract acceptance relation, not as the elliptic-curve arithmetic. The FA-Crypto-Verify analytic proof (`FrostVerifyDelegation.md`) cites the RFC 9591 / RFC 8032 algebraic argument; the FB-track here checks the state-machine consistency of the delegation abstraction.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/FrostVerifyDelegation.md` (the FA-Crypto-Verify proof shipped in Round 18 deliverable; T-1 + L-1 + L-2 + corollaries T-1.1 / T-1.2 / T-1.3). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof's adversary model (┬ž5): tampered-signature, wrong-public-key, and tampered-message surfaces are each closed by `valid_pairs` non-membership; round-trip soundness is closed by `SignMessage`'s joint extension of `signed_sigs` and `valid_pairs`; the empty-message corollary is closed by `INV_EmptyMsgWellDefined`'s well-typedness assertion; the structural-type corollary (the two `static_assert` clauses) is closed by `INV_TypeContract`'s sequence-length predicates.

### MakeContribCommitment.tla Ôćĺ FA-Crypto-MakeContrib (v1-byte-identity + DTM-F2-v1 replay defense)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `record` (total function `InputTuple Ôćĺ OutputRange` where OutputRange is `{SENTINEL} Ôł¬ {V1Commit(...)} Ôł¬ {F2Commit(...)}`), `generated` (SUBSET of InputTuple ÔÇö tracks which input tuples have been enumerated by the `Generate` action) |
| `INV_V1ByteIdentity` | INV-1: for every generated `(idx, prev, txs, dh, ZERO, ZERO, ZERO)` tuple, `record[t] = V1Commit(t.idx, t.prev, t.txs, t.dh)`. Lifts T-1 (v1 byte-identity) of `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` ┬ž1. The C++ short-circuit at `src/node/producer.cpp:242-258` (the `if (any_view)` body is skipped when `is_zero_hash(view_eq_root) && is_zero_hash(view_abort_root) && is_zero_hash(view_inbound_root)`) is the structural witness; the spec layer captures this as `MakeCommit` reducing to `V1Commit` when `AllViewsZero` holds. Runtime regression: `src/main.cpp` assertion `make_contrib_commitment: all-zero views == v1 short-circuit` (line 9608) |
| `INV_F2PathTriggered` | INV-2: when at least one view root is non-zero, `MakeCommit` evaluates to `F2Commit(...)` and is distinct from `V1Commit(...)` on the same `(idx, prev, txs, dh)` prefix. Lifts T-2 forward direction. The C++ `if (any_view)` branch at producer.cpp:249-258 appends the `"DTM-F2-v1"` literal plus the three view roots; the spec layer captures the disjoint-pre-image-families argument via the `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator tag in the output tuple. The cryptographic underpinning is L-3 of the companion proof (length argument: 104 vs 209 bytes Ôçĺ distinct SHA-256 inputs Ôçĺ distinct outputs under A2) |
| `INV_PerRootBinding` | INV-3: each individual non-zero view root in any single position (eq only, abort only, or inbound only) produces a distinct `MakeCommit` output. The three slots are bound at distinct field positions in the SHA-256 input, so a non-zero value in one slot cannot collide with the same non-zero value in another slot. Per-root domain separation. Structural witness: the F2 branch at producer.cpp:255-257 appends each root in fixed order (`view_eq_root` first, then `view_abort_root`, then `view_inbound_root`); the position of the non-zero byte run differs across the three single-non-zero shapes. Runtime regressions: `make_contrib_commitment: {eq,abort,inbound}_root binds the hash` + `make_contrib_commitment: each root contributes independently` (src/main.cpp:9626-9633) |
| `INV_DomainSeparation` | INV-4: no v1-shape pre-image equals any F2-shape pre-image. Lifts T-2 + L-3 ÔÇö the `"DTM-F2-v1"` literal at the start of the F2 extension makes the two families syntactically disjoint. State-form: for every pair of generated input tuples `(t1, t2)` where `t1` has all-zero views (= v1 family) and `t2` has any non-zero view (= F2 family), `record[t1] Ôëá record[t2]`. The spec-layer abstraction is the `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator distinctness; the C++ side's structural witness is the length difference (104 vs 209 bytes) + the literal-tag defense-in-depth |
| `INV_Determinism` | INV-5: `MakeCommit` applied twice to the same input tuple yields the same output. Captures L-2 of the companion proof (SHA256Builder is deterministic via OpenSSL's `EVP_DigestUpdate` byte-stream determinism at `src/crypto/sha256.cpp:25-28`). State-form: `record[t] = MakeCommit(t.idx, t.prev, t.txs, t.dh, t.eq, t.ab, t.inb)` for every generated `t`. The pure-function property holds by definitional substitution at the spec layer; TLC verifies the invariant against every reachable enumeration |
| `INV_FieldBinding` | INV-6: every consensus-bound v1-prefix field (idx, prev, txs, dh) binds the hash ÔÇö the output changes if that field changes.
