Captures the field-binding contract that the analytic proof's L-2 establishes via SHA-256 collision resistance (content-bound). State-form: for each generated `t` and each candidate replacement value `idx2 / prev2 / txs2 / dh2 Ôëá t.idx / t.prev / t.txs / t.dh`, `MakeCommit(replacement, ...) Ôëá record[t]`. The three view-root slots are not retested here because INV-3 (PerRootBinding) covers them more tightly. The cryptographic underpinning is A2 + L-2; the spec layer captures it via the InnerRoot + V1Commit + F2Commit operators embedding every field directly into the output tuple |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-two specs above). The recommended `MakeContribCommitment.cfg` (BlockIdx = {i1, i2}, Hashes = {ZERO, h1, h2}, TxLists = {nil, t1, t2}, MaxTxs = 2) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The state-machine driver is intentionally minimal because the function under test is pure ÔÇö every algebraic invariant (INV-1..INV-6) holds over every reachable input tuple, not just the ones produced by a particular protocol trace. The single non-deterministic `Generate` action picks an input tuple, computes `MakeCommit(t.*)`, stores the result in a `record` map keyed by the tuple, and TLC verifies the invariants hold against the accumulated map at every reachable state. Variables modeled: `record` (total function `InputTuple Ôćĺ OutputRange` ÔÇö the accumulated output map; at Init every key maps to a sentinel `<<"unset">>` 1-tuple, every `Generate` step overwrites one key with a real `V1Commit` or `F2Commit` tuple), `generated` (SUBSET of InputTuple ÔÇö the set of keys that have been assigned a real value; used to gate the invariants from spuriously firing at Init). Actions modeled: `Generate` (non-deterministically pick an unenumerated input tuple + record the MakeCommit value), `Saturate` (post-enumeration stutter when every tuple has been seen).

The SHA-256 abstraction. The C++ `SHA256Builder` at `src/crypto/sha256.cpp:25-28` forwards every `append(...)` call to OpenSSL's `EVP_DigestUpdate`, which per FIPS 180-4 ┬ž6.1.2 incorporates each byte into the message schedule in the order received; identical append-sequences produce identical outputs, byte-distinct sequences produce distinct outputs except with probability ÔëĄ 2Ôü╗┬╣┬▓ÔüŞ per attempt (the A2 / Preliminaries ┬ž2.1 collision-resistance assumption + the L-4 cumulative bound). The spec-layer abstraction lifts this to determinism on the bounded pre-image universe: `V1Commit` and `F2Commit` are pure TLA+ operators that return structurally distinct tuples for structurally distinct pre-images, and identical tuples for identical pre-images. This is the same "abstract hash = pre-image identity" pattern that `Consensus.tla` uses for `Digest`, `Snapshot.tla` uses for `state_root`, and `FrostVerify.tla` uses for `valid_pairs`. The `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator tags in the output tuples capture the disjoint-pre-image-families contract (L-3 of the companion proof: 104-byte v1 pre-image vs 209-byte F2 pre-image Ôçĺ distinct lengths Ôçĺ distinct SHA-256 inputs).

This spec captures the commit-side of the v2.7 F2 wire change: the `make_contrib_commitment` primitive at `src/node/producer.cpp:219-260` extends the pre-F2 (v1) commit shape with three view roots under a `"DTM-F2-v1"` domain tag. Two paired properties are pinned: (T-1) v1 backward compatibility ÔÇö a call with all three view roots equal to `Hash{}` (= the 32-zero `ZERO` element in the spec) produces a hash byte-identical to the pre-F2 implementation, so pre-F2 ContribMsg signatures continue to verify under the extended primitive without protocol-version negotiation; (T-2) DTM-F2-v1 replay defense ÔÇö a signature produced under one commit shape cannot be replayed under the other shape except with cryptographically negligible probability under A2. The runtime regressions at `src/main.cpp` (cited in ┬ž7 of `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md`) cover the bidirectional cross-shape verification matrix that an external implementer needs to reproduce: T-1.1 (v1 sig valid under v2 verifier when all-zero views), T-2.1 (F2 sig invalid under v1 verifier shape).

Combined with the apply-layer S-033 + S-038 closure (the producer's `body.state_root` population per the S-038 wiring) and FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (the validator-side reconciliation primitives that consume the view roots this commit binds), the consensus-layer half of S-030 D2 closure is now end-to-end at both the FA-track (analytic) and FB-track (state-machine) layers. The downstream signature-side claims T-1.1 and T-2.1 are downstream compositions of this spec's INV-1 / INV-2 / INV-4 + `FrostVerify.tla`'s INV-RoundTripSoundness / INV-TamperedMsgRejection under A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA); the spec layer establishes the commit-side distinctness algebraically and the cryptographic-soundness analytic proof in `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` ┬ž4 + ┬ž5 gives the sig-side closure.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` ┬ž6):
- Byte-level enumeration of the SHA-256 compression function. A2 abstracts the cryptographic content into "distinct pre-images map to distinct hashes"; the spec layer models that abstraction via the `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator tags.
- Side-channel resistance of the underlying SHA-256 implementation (OpenSSL's constant-time guarantee is per their documentation; not modeled at the TLA+ layer).
- The Ed25519 sig-side reduction in T-1.1 / T-2.1 (signature compatibility / non-replayability corollaries). Those depend on Ed25519 EUF-CMA and are `FrostVerify.tla` (FB23) / FA-Crypto-Verify territory. This spec covers only the commit-binding state machine; the sig-side reduction is a downstream composition of this spec + `FrostVerify.tla` under A1.
- The validator-side reconciliation that consumes the view roots this primitive binds. That is `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (FB22) / F2-SPEC.md ┬žQ1 territory.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` (the FA-Crypto-MakeContrib proof shipped in Round 18 deliverable; T-1 + T-2 + L-1..L-4 + corollaries T-1.1 / T-2.1). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: INV-1 lifts T-1 (the all-zero-views short-circuit identity at producer.cpp:242-258); INV-2 + INV-3 + INV-4 lift T-2 (the disjoint-pre-image families argument via L-3's length-distinguishing property); INV-5 lifts L-2 (SHA256Builder determinism); INV-6 lifts the field-binding content-bound contract from L-2. The T-1.1 and T-2.1 corollaries are downstream compositions with FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` under A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA).

### RateLimiterEviction.tla Ôćĺ FA-RateLimiter F-1 closure (idle-bucket eviction in `net::RateLimiter`)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `buckets` (function `ActiveKeys Ôćĺ [tokens, last_touch]`), `next_sweep_at` (Nat), `now` (`0..MaxTimeSteps`), `evicted_count` (Nat), `was_evicted` (SUBSET Keys) |
| `INV_BucketLifetimeBounded` | INV-1 / T-1: every active bucket has been touched within the last `EvictionThreshold + SweepInterval` time units. Captures point 6 of the F-1 "Closure (shipped)" subsection in `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` ┬ž6.2 (the memory bound: a bucket survives at most `eviction_threshold_sec_ + sweep_interval_sec_` seconds without being touched). Structural witness: the C++ amortized-sweep branch at `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:95-103` fires at most every `sweep_interval_sec_` seconds, and the eviction predicate at line 135 (`now - it->second.last > threshold`) catches every bucket past its individual threshold at the cadence boundary. Fires only when `EvictionThreshold > 0` (disabled-eviction mode is covered by INV-5) |
| `INV_EvictionMonotone` | INV-2 / T-3: `evicted_count` never decreases across any step. Captures audit-trail soundness ÔÇö operators can read `evicted_count` over time and observe a monotone counter. Structural witness: `SweepIdle` and the amortized-sweep branch of `Consume` only ADD to `evicted_count` (by `Cardinality(StaleKeys) >= 0`); no action decrements it. State-form: `evicted_count \in Nat` (Nat-typed; documents the contract). The action-level monotonicity is captured by the absence of any action that decrements |
| `INV_ResurrectionSafe` | INV-3 / T-2: if a key was evicted (k Ôłł `was_evicted`) and is currently in `buckets` (k Ôłł `ActiveKeys`), the bucket starts at FULL capacity. Captures point 4 of the F-1 closure ("semantic safety: an evicted bucket re-creates as full-capacity on next touch"). Structural witness: the C++ first-touch branch at `rate_limiter.hpp:106-108` sets `b.tokens = burst_` when `b.last.time_since_epoch().count() == 0` (the just-inserted default-constructed Bucket). Observationally indistinguishable from the un-evicted bucket having refilled ÔÇö the default `eviction_threshold_sec_ = 600s` gives at least 60├Ś safety factor over realistic refill times (`burst_/rate_per_sec_` ~= 10s with default config) |
| `INV_SweepIdempotent` | INV-4 / T-4: SweepIdle applied twice with no intervening time advance and no Consume yields the same `buckets` the second time. Captures the erase-or-skip loop body at `rate_limiter.hpp:134-141` (`if (now - it->second.last > threshold) { erase; ++evicted; } else { ++it; }` ÔÇö each entry is decided independently, so a re-sweep finds no fresh deletions). State-form: after any sweep firing (forced or amortized), any key whose `last_touch` predates the most recent sweep window must have been re-touched after ÔÇö captured via the bound `(next_sweep_at > SweepInterval Ôłž buckets[k].last_touch < next_sweep_at - SweepInterval) Ôçĺ (now - buckets[k].last_touch <= EvictionThreshold)`. Fires only when `EvictionThreshold > 0` |
| `INV_ConfigureEvictionZeroDisables` | INV-5 / T-5: when `EvictionThreshold = 0`, no key is ever evicted. Captures the legacy unbounded-growth behavior pinned as a config option per `rate_limiter.hpp:56` (`configure_eviction(double threshold_sec, double interval_sec = 60.0)` ÔÇö passing `threshold_sec <= 0` DISABLES eviction entirely) and the disabled-eviction short-circuit at `rate_limiter.hpp:129` (`if (eviction_threshold_sec_ <= 0.0) return 0;` in `sweep_idle_locked`). Structural witness: `SweepIdle`'s IF-branch at the spec layer short-circuits when `EvictionThreshold = 0`, leaving `buckets`, `evicted_count`, and `was_evicted` UNCHANGED. State-form: `evicted_count = 0 Ôłž was_evicted = {}` whenever `EvictionThreshold = 0` |
| `INV_AmortizedSweepLowerBoundsResidual` | INV-6 / T-6: at any time t, the number of stale keys still resident in `buckets` is bounded by the cadence-fresh count. Captures the amortization argument ÔÇö a key past `EvictionThreshold` idle seconds was either (a) caught by the most recent sweep (so it's not in `buckets`) or (b) only just became stale in the current `SweepInterval` window. Structural witness: the amortized-sweep cadence at `rate_limiter.hpp:99-101` (`next_sweep_at_ = now + sweep_interval_sec_;`) ensures the next sweep fires no later than `SweepInterval` seconds after the previous one. State-form: for every stale key k, `now - buckets[k].last_touch <= EvictionThreshold + SweepInterval`. Fires only when `EvictionThreshold > 0` |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-three specs above). The recommended `RateLimiterEviction.cfg` (Keys = {k1, k2, k3}, MaxTimeSteps = 10, EvictionThreshold = 3, SweepInterval = 2, MaxTimeStep = 2) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The three-action state machine (Consume, AdvanceTime, ForcedSweep) exercises every reachable interleaving of bucket-touch, clock-advance, and operator-triggered eviction within the bounded universe. Variables modeled: `buckets` (function `ActiveKeys Ôćĺ Bucket` where Bucket = `[tokens: {FULL, EMPTY}, last_touch: Nat]` ÔÇö matches the C++ `std::map<std::string, Bucket> buckets_` at rate_limiter.hpp:151 with the token level collapsed to FULL/EMPTY since the F-1 invariants depend on `last_touch` not on the precise integer-fractional token amount), `next_sweep_at` (Nat ÔÇö the time the next amortized sweep fires; matches `std::chrono::steady_clock::time_point next_sweep_at_` at rate_limiter.hpp:149), `now` (Nat ÔÇö the abstract monotonic clock matching `std::chrono::steady_clock::now()` at rate_limiter.hpp:89; the RFC-mandated monotonicity is enforced by the AdvanceTime action's `now' = now + delta` with `delta >= 1`), `evicted_count` (Nat ÔÇö spec-only cumulative counter; the C++ side returns per-call evicted counts from `sweep_idle_locked` but doesn't maintain a cumulative counter, so the spec lifts them to a cumulative for INV-2 monotonicity), `was_evicted` (SUBSET Keys ÔÇö spec-only audit set of keys evicted at least once; lets INV-3 observe resurrection across the trace, where the C++ side has no equivalent set because eviction is destructive on `buckets_`). Actions modeled: `Consume(k)` (touch key k; if `now >= next_sweep_at` run the amortized sweep first then bucket-touch ÔÇö mirrors the C++ flow at lines 95-117 with the sweep-before-touch ordering), `AdvanceTime` (monotonic clock advance bounded by MaxTimeStep per step to keep the state space tractable), `ForcedSweep` (external `sweep_idle()` call from the public API at rate_limiter.hpp:79-82 ÔÇö no-op when eviction is disabled), `SaturateClock` (stutter at the time horizon).

The state-machine driver exercises the F-1 mitigation's hot path (Consume's sweep-before-touch branching) and the two operator-facing surfaces (`configure_eviction` parameterized via spec constants + `sweep_idle` exposed as `ForcedSweep`). The token level is abstracted to FULL/EMPTY because the F-1 invariants (lifetime-bound, resurrection-safety, sweep-idempotence, configure-zero-disables, amortization) depend only on `last_touch`, not on the precise refill arithmetic ÔÇö L-1 of `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` already gives `tokens Ôłł [0, C]` orthogonally. The clock is modeled as Nat-typed monotonic time units rather than the C++ `std::chrono::steady_clock::duration` because the bound arithmetic (`now - last_touch <= EvictionThreshold + SweepInterval`) is the same up to unit conversion; L-5 of the prose proof gives the C++ side's monotonicity, the spec layer enforces it via the AdvanceTime action's `delta >= 1` clause.

This spec captures the just-shipped F-1 mitigation that closes the long-standing unbounded-`buckets_`-growth finding in `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` ┬ž6.2. Pre-F-1 the `std::map<std::string, Bucket> buckets_` grew monotonically: every distinct key ever consumed created an entry, with no path to remove entries. An attacker with access to many distinct source IPs (e.g., IPv6 /64 ÔÇö `2^64` addresses per residential prefix, or /48 ÔÇö `2^80` addresses in others) could grow `buckets_` arbitrarily by sending one consume-triggering request per unique IP, at ~64 bytes per entry ÔÇö 100M unique requests would reach ~6.4 GB RAM. The F-1 closure adds time-decay eviction: every `consume()` opportunistically checks if `now >= next_sweep_at_`; if so, walks the map and erases entries whose `b.last` is older than `eviction_threshold_sec_`. Cost: O(N) per prune trigger, amortized O(1) per consume. The default config (`eviction_threshold_sec_ = 600`, `sweep_interval_sec_ = 60`) bounds `buckets_.size()` to the per-bucket worst-case lifetime ÔÇö a bucket survives at most `600 + 60 = 660` seconds without being touched.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` ┬ž6.2):
- The pre-F-1 soundness theorems T-1 (bounded burst), T-2 (no DoS amplification), T-3 (per-IP independence), T-4 (HELLO-exemption safety), T-5 (refill monotonicity), T-6 (capacity-vs-rate trade-off). All remain valid under the F-1 mitigation because the eviction policy operates on `last_touch` only, leaving the token-bucket refill arithmetic at rate_limiter.hpp:109-113 untouched. The prose proof's ┬ž6 covers these theorems in detail.
- Concurrent-mutex correctness. The C++ side serializes via `std::mutex mu_` at rate_limiter.hpp:150; the spec uses TLA+ atomic actions to model the serialized window. The Preliminaries.md ┬ž3 network model assumption (asio thread-pool concurrency) is what makes the mutex sufficient at the C++ layer; the FA-track prose proof covers the mutex argument.
- Per-second-precision floating-point arithmetic. The C++ `elapsed * rate_per_sec` calculation at line 111 is modeled at the spec layer as a FULL/EMPTY transition because the F-1 invariants depend on `last_touch`, not on the precise integer-fractional token amount. L-1 of the prose proof gives the `[0, C]` interval bound for token levels.
- HELLO-exemption gate at `src/net/gossip.cpp:148`. That is FA-track T-4 territory (the HELLO size + idempotence + connection-rate-throttle bound); orthogonal to the F-1 eviction mitigation.
- Per-method weighting on RPC. Finding F-3 of the prose proof's ┬ž6.2 acknowledged as Option 1b deferred to a follow-on (per-method token-multiplier table; ~50 LOC + 1 day of weight tuning + a regression test).

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` (the FA-RateLimiter proof; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 + T-6 + L-1..L-7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof's ┬ž6.2 "Closure (shipped)" F-1 mitigation subsection: INV-1 lifts the ┬ž6.2 point-6 memory bound (a bucket survives at most `eviction_threshold + sweep_interval` seconds); INV-2 captures the audit-trail soundness of the cumulative `evicted_count`; INV-3 lifts ┬ž6.2 point-4 (semantic safety ÔÇö evicted bucket re-creates as full-capacity, observationally indistinguishable from the un-evicted bucket having refilled); INV-4 captures the erase-or-skip loop body's idempotence at rate_limiter.hpp:134-141; INV-5 lifts the configure-zero-disables config option at rate_limiter.hpp:56 + 129; INV-6 captures the amortization argument (the cadence bounds residual stale-key count). The pre-F-1 theorems T-1..T-6 remain valid under the F-1 mitigation and are out of scope here ÔÇö the prose proof's ┬ž1 + ┬ž4 + ┬ž5 cover them.

### BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla Ôćĺ FA-StateIntegrity (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 + apply-time gate composition)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `chains` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) where Block = [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs]), `local_state` (Nodes Ôćĺ [height, txs: SUBSET TxUniverse]), `chain_at_rest` (Nodes Ôćĺ SerializedChain Ôł¬ {NoSerialization}), `pending_inbox` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block)), `apply_throws` / `load_throws` (Nodes Ôćĺ BOOLEAN), `tampered_at` (Nodes Ôćĺ 0..MaxHeight Ôł¬ {"none"}) |
| `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` | T-1: if `chain_at_rest[n]` has been tampered (`tampered_at[n] /= "none"`), the wrapped chain blob fails one of two integrity checks ÔÇö either `validate_chain` returns FALSE (case (a): interior-block tamper, caught by the `prev_hash` chain consistency at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58`) OR `head_hash` recompute differs from `cr.head_hash` (case (b): head-block tamper, caught by the wrap check at `src/chain/chain.cpp:2046-2050`). Case (c) "adversary forges committee signatures to mask the tamper" reduces to A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA per Preliminaries ┬ž2.2) and is FA-track territory (out of scope for the state-machine layer; cf. FrostVerify.tla / FB23 for the abstract EUF-CMA model) |
| `INV_ApplyGateFiresOnMismatch` | T-2: across every reachable state, every block in `chains[n]` has either `state_root = ZeroRoot` (pre-S-038 backward-compat zero-skip ÔÇö `WireFormatBackwardCompat.md` T-1) OR `state_root = state_root_of(head_state(prefix))` where `prefix` is the chain up to that block. The standing-invariant form of "the S-033 gate at chain.cpp:1432-1444 always fires on divergent blocks before they reach `blocks_.push_back`" ÔÇö a divergent block would violate the disjunction but the gate's throw prevents installation. The DivergentTxPropose adversarial action exercises the gate-firing path by depositing a block with a fabricated `state_root` into `pending_inbox`; the next `ApplyBlockOnReceive` latches `apply_throws[n] = TRUE` and refuses to advance |
| `INV_SelfApplyConsistent` | T-3: across every reachable state, every block in `chains[n]` produced by node n (i.e., installed via `ProduceBlock(n)`) has `state_root` in `{ZeroRoot, state_root_of(head_state(prefix))}`. The structural witness that the producer's tentative-chain dry-run pattern at `src/node/node.cpp:1024-1117` guarantees gate-pass on self-apply: the tentative chain's `compute_state_root()` equals the live chain's `compute_state_root()` after the same body is applied to both, by FA-Apply-1 (AccountState.tla / FB5). Self-apply NEVER triggers the gate's loud-fail path because the producer feeds the gate with a value it itself computed via the same deterministic operator |
| `INV_CrossNodeConsistency` | T-4: for any two honest nodes n1, n2, if `chains[n1] = chains[n2]` (byte-identical chain sequences), then `state_root_of(local_state[n1]) = state_root_of(local_state[n2])`. The FA-Apply-1 byproduct lifted to the spec layer: equal block sequences applied from equal starting states reach byte-identical post-apply states by apply determinism. The non-trivial coverage point is the antecedent ÔÇö when chains differ (e.g., one node has applied a fork the other hasn't), the invariant degenerates to vacuous; the fork-choice layer (FA1 / S-029) handles fork pruning in production. This spec asserts the cleaner FA-Apply-1 consequence: equal prefixes Ôçĺ equal roots |
| `INV_NoSilentDivergence` | T-5: the headline composition claim. If two honest nodes n1, n2 have `local_state[n1].height = local_state[n2].height` AND `state_root_of(local_state[n1]) /= state_root_of(local_state[n2])` (i.e., the same height with different state_roots ÔÇö a divergence), then at least one of `apply_throws[n1]`, `apply_throws[n2]`, `load_throws[n1]`, `load_throws[n2]` is TRUE. The structural witness that every state divergence is loud-failed at the appropriate boundary ÔÇö either at receive (apply_throws via T-2) or at load (load_throws via T-1). The composition is total over the state-integrity surface: there is no reachable state where two honest nodes silently diverge |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-three specs above). The recommended `BlockchainStateIntegrity.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2, n3}, MaxHeight = 3, TxUniverse = {t1, t2}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. The six-action state machine (ProduceBlock, ApplyBlockOnReceive, SerializeChain, LoadChain, TamperAtRest, DivergentTxPropose) exercises every reachable interleaving of producer-side state_root population, receiver-side gate firing, at-rest serialize/load round-trips, and the two adversary surfaces (disk-level tamper + Byzantine producer). Variables modeled: `chains` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ Seq(Block)` where Block has [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs] ÔÇö matches the C++ `std::vector<Block> blocks_` at `include/determ/chain/chain.hpp` with the per-block field structure collapsed to the four state-integrity-relevant fields), `local_state` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ [height, txs: SUBSET TxUniverse]` ÔÇö the canonical state projection abstracted to (height, accumulated_tx_set) per FA-Apply-1's apply-determinism contract), `chain_at_rest` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ SerializedChain Ôł¬ {NoSerialization}` where SerializedChain has [head_hash, blocks] ÔÇö matches the S-021 wrapped JSON form `{head_hash, blocks}` at chain.cpp:1944-1985), `pending_inbox` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ Seq(Block)` ÔÇö the gossip-ratified inbound queue; abstracts the wire-level V1..V20 admission gates), `apply_throws` / `load_throws` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ BOOLEAN` ÔÇö latching sentinels for "an integrity gate has fired at this node"; lifts the C++ exception propagation into observable state-machine markers), `tampered_at` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ 0..MaxHeight Ôł¬ {"none"}` ÔÇö spec-only audit field tracking the height-index of the most recent TamperAtRest mutation; lets INV_LoadDetectsTampering observe the post-tamper state). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (the C++ Node::try_finalize_round at node.cpp:1024-1117 ÔÇö six steps collapsed into a single atomic action: build_body, tentative-chain dry-run for state_root computation, populate body.state_root, apply on live chain, broadcast to other nodes' inboxes), `ApplyBlockOnReceive(n)` (the receiver-side path ÔÇö drains head of pending_inbox; on prev_hash continuity + state_root match advances the chain, on mismatch latches apply_throws and refuses to advance per the A9 atomic-apply rollback), `SerializeChain(n)` (Chain::save at chain.cpp:1944-1985 ÔÇö writes the wrapped JSON blob; resets tampered_at to "none"), `LoadChain(n)` (Chain::load at chain.cpp:1987-2054 ÔÇö replays the blob with prev_hash continuity + head_hash recompute; on mismatch latches load_throws), `TamperAtRest(n)` (the disk-level adversary surface ÔÇö mutates one block's txs field at an arbitrary target_height; the wrap header's stored head_hash is NOT patched, so the next LoadChain MUST detect either via interior prev_hash mismatch or via head head_hash mismatch), `DivergentTxPropose(n, dest)` (the Byzantine-producer adversary ÔÇö node n deposits a block with a fabricated state_root into dest's inbox; the next ApplyBlockOnReceive MUST latch apply_throws on the gate's mismatch fire).

This spec captures the just-shipped composition theorem of `docs/proofs/BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-1..T-5) establishes that four independently-shipped mechanisms (S-021 chain.json wrap, S-033 state_root Merkle commitment, S-038 producer-side population, the apply-time gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446) together exhaust the state-mutation surface across three operational boundaries (at-rest / produce / receive). The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into six actions + five invariants:

1. **Surface decomposition** is captured by the action set ÔÇö ProduceBlock covers the producer boundary, ApplyBlockOnReceive covers the receiver boundary, SerializeChain + LoadChain cover the at-rest boundary, TamperAtRest + DivergentTxPropose are the two adversary surfaces.
2. **The five theorem statements** are each lifted to a standing invariant ÔÇö T-1 Ôćĺ INV_LoadDetectsTampering (disjunction over case (a) interior tamper and case (b) head tamper; case (c) forge-sigs is A1 / FA-track), T-2 Ôćĺ INV_ApplyGateFiresOnMismatch (every installed block satisfies state_root = computed root by construction), T-3 Ôćĺ INV_SelfApplyConsistent (every self-produced block has the tentative-dry-run-computed state_root), T-4 Ôćĺ INV_CrossNodeConsistency (FA-Apply-1 lifted), T-5 Ôćĺ INV_NoSilentDivergence (the composition's end-state property).
3. **The composition is total over the state-integrity surface** ÔÇö the spec's TLC enumeration of every reachable interleaving witnesses that every divergent block introduction (via DivergentTxPropose) is loud-failed at receive (apply_throws latches before chain advances), and every divergent chain at rest (via TamperAtRest) is loud-failed at load (load_throws latches before chains[n] is installed). No silent divergence is reachable under the bounded model; the proof's structural argument (four mechanisms ├Ś four surfaces = total coverage) is the unbounded counterpart.

The abstract-hash model (compute_hash and state_root_of as pure functions returning tagged tuples) is the standard TLA+ projection of A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance) ÔÇö distinct pre-images map to distinct outputs by tuple inequality. The cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (Preliminaries.md ┬ž2.1); the FB-track here checks the state-machine consistency of the surface composition under the abstract-hash discipline.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` ┬ž6):
- Pre-S-038 historical blocks bypass T-2 (intentional backward-compat). The spec captures this via the `b.state_root = ZeroRoot` disjunct in INV_ApplyGateFiresOnMismatch and INV_SelfApplyConsistent. Post-S-038 every produced block has non-zero state_root (modeled by ProduceBlock's step-4 population at `body.state_root = state_root_of(post_state)`).
- Out-of-namespace state divergence (any future state field NOT threaded into `Chain::compute_state_root` would land outside the commitment). The spec models compute_state_root as a pure function of (height, txs) which is fully covered; the namespace-coverage lock-in is `tools/test_state_root_namespaces.sh` (12 assertions).
- Consensus-layer divergence prevention (S-030 D2 closure). That is FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` / `F2-SPEC.md` territory ÔÇö the apply-time gate is the receiver-side safety net, but the producer-side reconciliation that prevents divergent blocks from being assembled in the first place is the parallel mechanism.
- Snapshot pathway (covered by FA-Apply-2 / FB6 `Snapshot.tla`). The snapshot tail-head's stored `state_root` is checked against the freshly-restored `compute_state_root()` at chain.cpp:1778-1783; that surface is the parallel composition this spec doesn't model.
- Non-Byzantine bugs in `compute_state_root` itself. T-2 assumes `compute_state_root()` correctly hashes the actual `Chain` state. A bug that omits a state field from `build_state_leaves` would leave that field out of the commitment; T-2 would fail to detect divergence in it. The namespace-coverage regressions (┬ž7 of the prose proof) are the mitigation.
- The Ed25519 EUF-CMA / SHA-256 collision resistance bounds ÔÇö the spec lifts these to deterministic predicates ("distinct pre-images map to distinct hashes") via the abstract-hash model; the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` (the composition theorem shipped Round 21; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 with the per-surface adversary model in ┬ž5 and the test-suite citation table in ┬ž7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: the six actions cover the producer / receiver / at-rest / adversary surfaces enumerated in ┬ž5; the five invariants cover the five theorems in ┬ž1; the composition's structural totality (four mechanisms ├Ś four surfaces) is witnessed by TLC's enumeration of every reachable schedule under the bounded universe.

Cross-reference triangle. FB5 `AccountState.tla` (FA-Apply-1 ÔÇö apply determinism, the load-bearing input to T-3 + T-4 of this spec). FB6 `Snapshot.tla` (FA-Apply-2 ÔÇö the snapshot-pathway sibling surface; the S-021 wrap check has a parallel head_hash recompute at `restore_from_snapshot`). FB26 (this spec ÔÇö the load / apply / produce surface composition). Together, the three specs cover the full state-integrity surface at the state-machine layer.

### JsonValidation.tla Ôćĺ FA-S018 (S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth state machine)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `input_objects` (function Surfaces Ôćĺ SUBSET JsonObjects), `validation_log` (Seq of LogEntry where LogEntry has [surface, field_name, outcome, has_diagnostic]), `fired_surfaces` (SUBSET Surfaces); `Len(validation_log) <= MaxValidations` enforces the bounded-work cap |
| `INV_ClearDiagnostic` | T-1: every exception emitted by `RequireField` has a `field_name` attribute equal to the key being required. State-form witness: every entry in `validation_log` whose outcome is a failure (MissingField or WrongType) has its `field_name` field set to a key in `FieldNames` AND has `has_diagnostic = TRUE`. Structural argument: every LogEntry constructed via `MakeLogEntry` has its `field_name` slot set to the schema entry's key ÔÇö and the helper sets `has_diagnostic = TRUE` unconditionally. The C++ correspondent is the `"S-018: missing required JSON field 'FIELD'"` and `"S-018: JSON field 'FIELD' has wrong type: ..."` exception strings at `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp:39-48`; the structural witness for "every helper-emitted exception carries the field name in single quotes" |
| `INV_NoInternalLeakage` | T-2: no exception is emitted without the field-name context (e.g., a raw `nlohmann::detail::type_error`). State-form witness: every entry in `validation_log` (regardless of outcome) has `has_diagnostic = TRUE`. Structural argument: the `MakeLogEntry` helper sets `has_diagnostic = TRUE` unconditionally ÔÇö by construction every logged entry inherits the field-name context. The pre-S-018 leaky path (where a `nlohmann::detail::*` exception escapes without field-name context) would correspond to a LogEntry with `has_diagnostic = FALSE`, which is structurally unreachable in this spec because no action produces such an entry. The C++ correspondent is the `catch (const std::exception& e)` clause at `json_validate.hpp:44-48` that intercepts every nlohmann-internal exception and re-throws with `"S-018: JSON field 'FIELD' has wrong type: <inner>"` |
| `INV_DefenseInDepth` | T-3: any of the 5 surface entry points (Wire / RPC / Snapshot / Keyfile / Genesis) that calls `ValidateMessage` produces only field-name-tagged exceptions. State-form witness: every entry in `validation_log` has its `surface` field in `Surfaces` AND has `has_diagnostic = TRUE`. Structural argument: `ValidateAtSurface` is the only action that appends to `validation_log`, and its body restricts `s` to `Surfaces` by construction. Every entry in the log is therefore tagged with one of the five surfaces AND inherits the helper-emitted field-name context. No parallel bypass at any surface skips the helper contract. The C++ correspondents are the five entry points enumerated in ┬ž3.3 of the prose proof: `net::Message::deserialize` (Wire), `RpcServer::dispatch` structured-payload args (RPC), `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` collection wrappers (Snapshot), `crypto::load_node_key` (Keyfile), `GenesisConfig::from_json` (Genesis) |
| `INV_BoundedWork` | T-4: `ValidateMessage(obj, schema)` takes O(\|schema\|) time. State-form witness: `Len(validation_log) <= MaxValidations`. Structural argument: there is no action in the spec that iterates recursively or appends an unbounded number of entries. `ValidateAtSurface` appends exactly `Len(schema)` entries (a finite sequence-walk), and `Len(schema)` is bounded by `MaxSchemaLen` by construction of `BoundedSchemas`. The total log length is therefore bounded by `MaxValidations`. The C++ correspondents are the helpers' bodies at `json_validate.hpp:37-49` + `60-72` + `87-102`: one `contains()` + one `at()` + one `get<T>()` per call, all O(1) over the extracted value's already-bounded size; `json_require_array` adds an `is_array()` check; no loops, no recursion, no allocation beyond the failure-path exception string |
| `INV_OptionalBackwardCompat` | T-5: `OptionalField` returns the default value without emitting an exception when the key is absent. State-form witness: no entry in `validation_log` has outcome `"OptionalAbsent"` ÔÇö by construction `ExtractOptional` does NOT append to the log. Structural argument: `ExtractOptional`'s action body leaves `validation_log` UNCHANGED. The only outcomes that ever appear in the log are Pass / MissingField / WrongType (from the required-field path), and none of these are emitted by the `OptionalField` operator. The C++ correspondents are the `j.value(field, default)` pattern (e.g., `ContribMsg::aborts_gen` at `producer.cpp` reading `j.value("aborts_gen", uint64_t{0})`) and the `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` guard pattern (e.g., `Block::tx_root` / `delay_seed` / `delay_output` / `consensus_mode` / `bft_proposer` / `partner_subset_hash` / `state_root` at `Block::from_json`); both patterns silently take the default on absence, never emitting an exception |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-four specs above). The recommended `JsonValidation.cfg` (FieldNames = {amount, prev_hash, transactions}, MaxSchemaLen = 2, MaxValidations = 5) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The three-action state machine (ValidateAtSurface, ExtractOptional, SaturateSurface) exercises every reachable interleaving of surface entries ├Ś input JsonObjects ├Ś schema instances within the bounded universe. Variables modeled: `input_objects` (function `Surfaces Ôćĺ SUBSET JsonObjects` ÔÇö the per-surface accumulator of admitted JSON inputs; abstracts the 5 surfaces' per-entry-point admission paths into a single tracking surface for INV-3's surface-tag invariant), `validation_log` (Seq of LogEntry where LogEntry = [surface, field_name, outcome, has_diagnostic] ÔÇö the headline observable for INV-1/INV-2/INV-3/INV-4; every `ValidateAtSurface` invocation appends one entry per schema entry, capturing the C++ helper's per-required-field exception emission), `fired_surfaces` (SUBSET Surfaces ÔÇö tracks which surfaces have fired at least one validation; drives the SaturateSurface stutter once every surface has been exercised). Actions modeled: `ValidateAtSurface(s)` (the headline action ÔÇö pick a surface s, an input JsonObject, a schema; invoke ValidateMessage; append one LogEntry per schema entry; gated by the `Len(validation_log) + MaxSchemaLen <= MaxValidations` bound ÔÇö the structural T-4 enforcement), `ExtractOptional(s)` (the optional-field extraction ÔÇö pick a surface, an input, a key, a default; return either the present value or the default; never append to validation_log ÔÇö the structural T-5 enforcement), `SaturateSurface` (stutter once every surface has fired AND the log bound is reached).

This spec captures the just-shipped S-018 closure of `JsonValidationSoundness.md` at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-1..T-5) establishes that the three helpers in `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp` (`json_require<T>`, `json_require_hex`, `json_require_array`) together provide a clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth contract across every attack-relevant wire-format consumer. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into three actions + five invariants:

1. **The five-surface entry-point inventory** is captured by the `Surfaces` constant = {Wire, RPC, Snapshot, Keyfile, Genesis}. Each surface corresponds to one of the five entry points enumerated in ┬ž4.3 of the prose proof: wire (gossip envelope + per-message-type from_json), RPC (structured-payload args via the same S-018-hardened from_json), snapshot (`Chain::restore_from_snapshot` collection wrappers), keyfile (`crypto::load_node_key`), genesis (`GenesisConfig::from_json`). No parallel bypass at any surface skips the helper contract ÔÇö `ValidateAtSurface` restricts s to `Surfaces` by construction.
2. **The clear-diagnostic contract** is captured by the `MakeLogEntry` helper's invariant: every LogEntry has `has_diagnostic = TRUE` AND its `field_name` slot bound to the schema entry's key. Pre-S-018 the leaky path would produce LogEntries with `has_diagnostic = FALSE` (the raw nlohmann-internal exception escaping without field-name context), which is structurally unreachable in this spec because no action produces such an entry. The C++ side's catch-`std::exception` clause at `json_validate.hpp:44-48` is the structural witness for "every nlohmann-internal exception gets re-thrown with the field-name context."
3. **The bounded-work contract** is captured by the `Len(validation_log) + MaxSchemaLen <= MaxValidations` guard on `ValidateAtSurface` and the `BoundedSchemas` constraint on schemas. No action in the spec iterates recursively or appends an unbounded number of entries ÔÇö each ValidateMessage call walks a finite schema once.
4. **The optional-field backward-compat contract** is captured by `ExtractOptional`'s UNCHANGED clause on `validation_log`. The OptionalField operator never emits to the log; the C++ side's `j.value(field, default)` and `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` patterns silently take the default on absence.

The abstract-diagnostic model (`has_diagnostic` as a BOOLEAN tag derived from the outcome rather than a byte-level exception message string) is the spec-layer projection of "the exception's `what()` contains the field name in single quotes" ÔÇö the byte-level diagnostic substring matching is the regression test's job (`tools/test_s018_json_validation.sh`, 10/10 PASS). The cryptographic / size-cap / rate-limit gating layers that sit above the helpers (S-022, S-014, S-033 + S-038) are out of scope; S-018's role is field-level diagnostic clarity, NOT security-relevant rejection.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `JsonValidationSoundness.md` ┬ž6):
- The byte-level exception message text. The spec uses a BOOLEAN `has_diagnostic` tag to model "the exception's `what()` contains the field name in single quotes"; the byte-level diagnostic substring matching is the regression test's job (`tools/test_s018_json_validation.sh`).
- The catch-`std::exception` vs catch-`nlohmann::json::exception` choice. ┬ž4.2 of the prose proof argues catching `std::exception` is robust under RTTI-symbol-visibility variations; the spec collapses both branches into a single WrongType outcome with `has_diagnostic = TRUE`.
- The intentionally-non-converted residual sites enumerated in ┬ž6 of the prose proof (inner-loop array elements where the iterating container is already validated, CLI output formatters, client-side RPC response parser, `BlockSigMsg::dh_secret` optional-residual at `producer.cpp:212`). These are not exposed to peer-supplied JSON; the spec's five surfaces cover the attack surface that the helpers protect.
- The cryptographic / size-cap / rate-limit gating layers above the helpers (S-022 size caps, S-014 rate limiting, S-033 / S-038 state-root verification). S-018's role is field-level diagnostic clarity, NOT security-relevant rejection; the spec models only the diagnostic-clarity surface.
- The Ed25519 EUF-CMA / SHA-256 collision resistance bounds ÔÇö the spec lifts these to deterministic predicates ("distinct pre-images map to distinct hashes") via the abstract-hash discipline (used in sibling specs FB23 / FB24 / FB25 / FB26); not invoked directly here because S-018 is below the cryptographic verification layer.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/JsonValidationSoundness.md` (the FA-S018 proof shipped Round 22; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 with the per-helper conversion inventory in ┬ž3.3 + adversary model in ┬ž5 + test-suite citation in ┬ž7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: INV-1 lifts T-1's per-helper field-name-context emission; INV-2 lifts T-2's catch-`std::exception` clause; INV-3 lifts T-3's five-surface defense-in-depth; INV-4 lifts T-4's bounded-work / no-recursion / no-loop helper-body inspection; INV-5 lifts T-5's REQUIRED-vs-OPTIONAL distinction. The byte-level diagnostic-substring assertion is the regression test (`tools/test_s018_json_validation.sh`, 10/10 PASS) ÔÇö the FB-track state-machine layer and the runtime regression together cover both the structural-soundness and the byte-precision-string assertions.

Cross-reference. FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model), FB24 `MakeContribCommitment.tla` (S-030 D2 commit-binding model), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 lifetime-bound model), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition). FB27 (this spec ÔÇö the S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth state machine, sitting below the cryptographic / size-cap / rate-limit gating layers and providing the field-level diagnostic-clarity contract that operator triage relies on).

### S006ContribMsgEquivocation.tla Ôćĺ FA-S006 (Phase-1 same-generation ContribMsg equivocation detection state machine)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `pending_contribs` (Seq(ContribMsg) with "at most one entry per signer" structural constraint enforced by the ReceiveContribSameGen guard ÔÇö the sequence proxy is the TLC-initialization vehicle for the partial-fn-keyed-by-signer C++ `std::map<std::string, ContribMsg> pending_contribs_` at `include/determ/node/node.hpp`), `pending_equivocation_evidence` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent), `drained_events` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent), `valid_sigs` (SUBSET of [signer, commit_hash] tuples ÔÇö the spec-layer projection of `crypto::verify` acceptance), `event_origins` (SUBSET SourceGen ÔÇö the per-event audit-tag tracking the generation at which the event was constructed), `current_gen` (AbortGenerations ÔÇö the receiver's `current_aborts_.size()`), `received_contribs` (SUBSET ContribMsg ÔÇö audit set of every ContribMsg admitted by the receive path) |
| `INV_SameGenDetection` | T-1 (Same-Generation Duplicate Detection): for every pair of distinct ContribMsgs `cm1, cm2` in `received_contribs` with the same signer / block_index / aborts_gen but distinct commit_hashes, an EquivocationEvent against that signer at that block_index exists somewhere in the system ÔÇö either in `pending_equivocation_evidence` (not yet drained) or in `drained_events` (already baked into a block and routed through the apply pipeline). The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen's B4 branch (commit-mismatch on existing entry) constructs an event when the duplicate-detect predicate fires; the pool-dedup scan ensures at most one event per (equivocator, block_index) survives across the union pending ++ drained, but at least one always does (B4 always appends OR a prior B4 fired and produced the same-key event already). The C++ correspondent is the receive-path branch at `src/node/node.cpp:2122..2163` ÔÇö the `auto existing = pending_contribs_.find(msg.signer)` + `if (existing_commit != commit)` + EquivocationEvent construction sequence |
| `INV_CrossGenNoFalsePositive` | T-2 (Different-Generation Drop, No False Positive): no EquivocationEvent in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events has cross-generation sources. State-form witness: every event in the union has a corresponding entry in `event_origins` recording a single shared gen (the gen of its two ContribMsg sources, which by INV-1's preconditions are equal). The structural argument: ReceiveContribSameGen's pre-condition requires `aborts_gen = current_gen` for both the existing entry (admitted under a prior B2 at current_gen) and the incoming message (B4 entry guard); ReceiveContribDifferentGen short-circuits to UNCHANGED before reaching the duplicate-detect branch, modeling the C++ gen-gate at `node.cpp:2068` (`if (msg.aborts_gen != current_aborts_.size()) return;`). AdvanceGeneration clears pending_contribs on reset (modeling `reset_round`), so an honest signer's legitimate retry at a higher gen finds no existing entry to false-trigger against |
| `INV_EvidencePoolMonotone` | T-3 composition (FA-Apply-10 consume-side compatibility): the union `pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events` only ever grows across every `[Next]_vars` step. Action-form invariant `(pending' \cup drained') \supseteq (pending \cup drained)`. The structural argument: SignAndSend / ReceiveContribDifferentGen / AdvanceGeneration / Stutter all preserve both sets; ReceiveContribSameGen B4 either extends pending or preserves it (on pool-dedup hit); ApplyBlockDrainsPool moves entries from pending to drained (the union grows by 0). Composed with FB15 EquivocationApply.tla's pending_events / drained semantics ÔÇö the same pool the apply-side consumes. The C++ correspondent is the `Node::pending_equivocation_evidence_` vector + the producer's `build_body` consume site at `producer.cpp:452` + the FA-Apply-10 slash-on-apply at `chain.cpp:1344..1356` |
| `INV_TwoSigsValid` | T-4 (Two-Sig Proof Soundness): every entry in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events has its sig_a and sig_b in `valid_sigs` (the spec-layer projection of `crypto::verify` acceptance), AND those sigs are bound to the correct (signer, commit_hash) tuples via the structural equality `sig_a = [signer |-> equivocator, commit_hash |-> digest_a]` and `sig_b = [signer |-> equivocator, commit_hash |-> digest_b]`. The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen B4 constructs the event using the existing entry's sig (which was admitted via a prior B2 / B3 that required the incoming sig in valid_sigs) AND the incoming message's sig (also pre-checked at the B4 entry guard). The downstream V11 re-verification at `validator.cpp:307..322` is the corresponding apply-time witness; INV-4 captures the receive-time half of the two-layer check. EUF-CMA forgery resistance is FB23 FrostVerify.tla territory; the spec abstracts via the valid_sigs membership predicate |
| `INV_ReplaySafe` | T-5 (Replay-Safety): no two events in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events share a PoolDedupKey (equivocator, block_index). The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen B4's pool-dedup scan (the `dup_in_pool \/ dup_in_drained` guard) rejects any incoming event whose key already exists in the union, AND ApplyBlockDrainsPool moves entries to drained without duplication (the union does not gain a duplicate by the move). The C++ correspondent is the pool-dedup loop at `node.cpp:2147..2153` (the `for (auto& e : pending_equivocation_evidence_)` scan that skips events with matching `(equivocator, block_index)`). Composed with FB15 EquivocationApply.tla's `Inv_NoDoubleSlash`, this gives the cross-spec end-to-end claim: the same (equivocator, block_index) pair contributes at most one slash across the full detect Ôćĺ bake Ôćĺ apply pipeline |
| `INV_ChannelReuse` | T-3 sub-claim (no new wire format): every entry in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events satisfies `EquivocationEventShape` ÔÇö the same six-field shape produced by the rev.8 BlockSigMsg-level detector. The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen B4 uses the constructor pattern of the EquivocationEvent record type, with the same six fields the rev.8 BlockSigMsg detector populates (equivocator, block_index, digest_a, sig_a, digest_b, sig_b). No alternate struct, no additional fields, no parallel ContribMsg-equivocation subtype. The C++ correspondent is the `chain::EquivocationEvent` struct at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp:256..279` (unchanged from rev.8); the S-006 closure reuses it verbatim per the digest-agnostic argument in ┬ž2.2 of the prose proof. Implicit corollary: the unused legacy `contrib_equivocations_` field declared in `node.hpp` was removed (per `SECURITY.md` ┬žS-006 "Cleanup"), and the spec doesn't model the deleted dead code |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-five specs above). The recommended `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.cfg` (Signers = {a, b}, BlockIndices = {0, 1}, AbortGenerations = {0, 1}, Hashes = {h1, h2, h3}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The five-action state machine (SignAndSend, ReceiveContribSameGen, ReceiveContribDifferentGen, AdvanceGeneration, ApplyBlockDrainsPool) exercises every reachable interleaving of honest / Byzantine signing, same-gen / cross-gen arrivals, abort-quorum boundaries, and block-apply consume. Variables modeled: `pending_contribs` (Seq(ContribMsg) used as a partial-fn proxy ÔÇö the spec enforces "at most one entry per signer" structurally via the ReceiveContribSameGen guard; matches the C++ `std::map<std::string, ContribMsg> pending_contribs_` at `include/determ/node/node.hpp`), `pending_equivocation_evidence` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent ÔÇö the receive-time pool, matching `Node::pending_equivocation_evidence_`; SET semantics so the (equivocator, block_index) pool-dedup at `node.cpp:2147..2153` collapses duplicates), `drained_events` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent ÔÇö spec-layer audit of events consumed by block-apply; tracks cross-block / cross-spec replay safety), `valid_sigs` (SUBSET of [signer, commit_hash] tuples ÔÇö the set of Ed25519 sig pairs that have passed `crypto::verify`; populated by SignAndSend), `event_origins` (SUBSET SourceGen ÔÇö per-event audit tag tracking the gen at which the event was constructed; INV-2's structural witness for no-cross-gen-sources), `current_gen` (AbortGenerations ÔÇö the receiver's `current_aborts_.size()`), `received_contribs` (SUBSET ContribMsg ÔÇö audit set of every ContribMsg admitted; INV-1's coverage check predicate). Actions modeled: `SignAndSend(s, h, g, c)` (the adversarial / honest signer surface ÔÇö admits a `[signer, commit_hash]` pair to valid_sigs; Byzantine signers may sign multiple distinct commits over the same (block_index, aborts_gen) tuple, honest signers obey H2 of Preliminaries ┬ž4 but the spec doesn't enforce this ÔÇö the detector at ReceiveContrib catches the equivocation regardless), `ReceiveContribSameGen(s, h, c)` (the headline action ÔÇö the C++ receive path's four branches: B1 cross-gen short-circuits via the disabled-action equivalence, B2 first-arrival admits to pending_contribs, B3 byte-identical retry drops silently, B4 commit-mismatch on existing entry constructs the EquivocationEvent and routes via the pool-dedup scan), `ReceiveContribDifferentGen(s, h, g)` (the cross-generation drop branch ÔÇö disabled when `g = current_gen`, no-op otherwise, modeling the C++ gen-gate at line 2068), `AdvanceGeneration` (abort-quorum boundary ÔÇö increments current_gen to any greater value in AbortGenerations and clears pending_contribs, modeling `reset_round`), `ApplyBlockDrainsPool` (block-finalize consume ÔÇö moves the entire pending_equivocation_evidence pool into drained_events; the per-event FA-Apply-10 slash mechanics are FB15 territory). The four ReceiveContribSameGen branches are mutually exclusive on their inner-IF guards and together cover the full receive-path branching at `node.cpp:2056..2170`.

This spec captures the just-shipped S-006 closure of `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.md` at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-1..T-5) establishes that the receive-time Phase-1 detector at `Node::on_contrib` adds a second equivocation-detection surface ÔÇö at the Phase-1 commit layer ÔÇö without introducing a new wire format, new validator predicate, or new apply-side branch. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into five actions + six invariants:

1. **Same-generation duplicate detection (T-1)** is captured by INV_SameGenDetection ÔÇö every distinct-commit same-gen pair in received_contribs is matched by an EquivocationEvent in pending ++ drained. The C++ correspondent is the B4 branch at `node.cpp:2122..2163` which constructs the event when the duplicate-detect predicate `existing_commit != commit` fires. The pool-dedup at `node.cpp:2147..2153` ensures at most one event per (equivocator, block_index) survives, captured by INV_ReplaySafe.

2. **Cross-generation drop without false positive (T-2)** is captured by INV_CrossGenNoFalsePositive ÔÇö every event's origin record has a single gen. The C++ correspondent is the gen-gate at `node.cpp:2068` which short-circuits before the duplicate-detect branch; the spec models this via ReceiveContribDifferentGen's no-op body. AdvanceGeneration clears pending_contribs on reset, modeling the `reset_round` machinery ÔÇö an honest signer's legitimate retry at a higher gen finds no existing entry to false-trigger against.

3. **Composition with FA6 + FA-Apply-10 (T-3)** is captured by INV_EvidencePoolMonotone (the pool is the same pool the apply-side consumes) and INV_ChannelReuse (no new wire format). FB15 EquivocationApply.tla covers the apply-side mechanics; the two specs share the EquivocationEvent struct shape exactly. The C++ correspondent is the rev.8 EquivocationEvent struct at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp:256..279` ÔÇö reused verbatim by S-006 per the digest-agnostic argument in ┬ž2.2 of the prose proof.

4. **Two-sig proof soundness (T-4)** is captured by INV_TwoSigsValid ÔÇö every event has both sigs in valid_sigs and bound to the correct (signer, commit_hash) tuples. The C++ correspondent is the sig-verify gate at `node.cpp:2089` (`crypto::verify(entry->pubkey, commit.data(), commit.size(), msg.ed_sig)`); the corresponding gate fired on the existing entry's admission ensures both halves of the constructed event are pre-validated. The downstream V11 re-verification at `validator.cpp:307..322` is the belt-and-suspenders apply-time witness; INV-4 captures the receive-time half of the two-layer check.

5. **Replay-safety (T-5)** is captured by INV_ReplaySafe ÔÇö no two events share a PoolDedupKey across pending + drained. The C++ correspondent is the pool-dedup loop at `node.cpp:2147..2153` (the `for (auto& e : pending_equivocation_evidence_)` scan that skips events with matching `(equivocator, block_index)`). Composed with FB15 EquivocationApply.tla's `Inv_NoDoubleSlash`, this gives the cross-spec end-to-end claim: the same (equivocator, block_index) pair contributes at most one slash across the full detect Ôćĺ bake Ôćĺ apply pipeline.

The abstract-sig model (`valid_sigs` as a SUBSET of [signer, commit_hash] tuples populated only by SignAndSend) is the standard TLA+ projection of A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA) ÔÇö the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (FB23 FrostVerify.tla). The abstract-hash model (Hashes as a finite universe with distinct ContribMsg content producing distinct commit_hash) is the standard TLA+ projection of A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance) ÔÇö the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (FB24 MakeContribCommitment.tla). The FB-track here checks the state-machine consistency of the detection surface under the abstract-sig + abstract-hash discipline.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.md` ┬ž6):
- Apply-side slash mechanics (T-E1 / T-E2 / T-E3 / T-E5 / T-E7 of FA-Apply-10). The `drained_events` set is the spec-layer audit of "events that have been consumed by the apply pipeline"; the per-event stake-forfeit + registry-deactivation + accumulated-slashed update happens in FB15 EquivocationApply.tla, which this spec composes with via INV_EvidencePoolMonotone + INV_ReplaySafe (shared pool semantics + replay-safety).
- The V11 validator predicate re-verification at block-validate time. INV_TwoSigsValid captures the receive-time sig-verify; V11's re-verification at `validator.cpp:307..322` is FA6 territory. The two-layer check is documented in ┬ž4.4 of the prose proof.
- Cross-shard equivocation routing (the `shard_id` / `beacon_anchor_height` fields of the C++ EquivocationEvent). FA6 T-6.1 covers this; the spec abstracts cross-shard handling.
- The forensic-audit coarseness at pool-dedup time (┬ž6.3 of the prose proof). The (equivocator, block_index) key collapses multiple distinct same-(d, h) incidents into one observable event; this is intentional and matches the C++ behavior. INV_ReplaySafe captures the dedup contract; the multi-incident forensic audit is out of scope.
- The byte-identical retry case (┬ž6.1 of the prose proof). The spec's ReceiveContribSameGen B3 branch (existing_commit = c) short-circuits to "no event, drop silently" ÔÇö captured by the IF-branch in the action body that leaves pending_equivocation_evidence UNCHANGED on equal-commit retries.
- The F2 view-root binding contract (┬ž6.4 of the prose proof). The spec's `commit_hash` field is the equivalence-class output of `make_contrib_commitment` per FB24 MakeContribCommitment.tla; the distinct-pre-image lemmas L-2 / L-3 of FB24 are the cryptographic backing.
- The deleted `contrib_equivocations_` field (┬ž6.5 of the prose proof). The post-S-006 source has no such field; the spec doesn't model the deleted dead code.
- Cryptographic forgery resistance. SignAndSend admits any (signer, commit_hash) pair into valid_sigs without enforcing EUF-CMA at the spec layer; FB23 FrostVerify.tla covers the cryptographic side. The composition is via INV_TwoSigsValid's valid_sigs membership predicate.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/S006ContribMsgEquivocation.md` (the FA-S006 proof shipped R23A7; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 with the receive-path source citation in ┬ž3, per-theorem proofs in ┬ž4, adversary model in ┬ž5, identified gaps in ┬ž6, test-suite citation in ┬ž7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: INV_SameGenDetection lifts T-1's same-gen duplicate-detect coverage; INV_CrossGenNoFalsePositive lifts T-2's cross-gen no-false-positive; INV_EvidencePoolMonotone + INV_ChannelReuse lift T-3's composition + no-new-wire-format; INV_TwoSigsValid lifts T-4's two-sig soundness; INV_ReplaySafe lifts T-5's replay-safety pool-dedup contract.

Cross-reference. FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives ÔÇö the post-S-006 contrib commit binds via the DTM-F2-v1 path), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model ÔÇö the abstract-sig discipline INV_TwoSigsValid relies on), FB24 `MakeContribCommitment.tla` (S-030 D2 commit-binding model ÔÇö the distinct-pre-image property INV_SameGenDetection relies on), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 lifetime-bound model), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition), FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` (S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth).
