### BlockTimestampMonotonic.tla Ôćĺ R24A5 (Block.timestamp monotonicity + digest-exclusion contract)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `chains` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö each block carries the four invariant-relevant fields index/timestamp/prev_hash/txs), `pending_inbox` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö gossip queue), `tampered_at` (Nodes Ôćĺ 0..MaxChainLength Ôł¬ {"none"} ÔÇö interior tamper site, latches across actions), `load_throws` (Nodes Ôćĺ BOOLEAN ÔÇö reload reject latch) |
| `INV_TimestampMonotonic` | T-1 (forward-looking S-035 path-1 contract): when `monotonic_gate` is TRUE, every adjacent pair in every chain satisfies `chain[i].timestamp >= chain[i-1].timestamp`. When `monotonic_gate` is FALSE (the R24A5-pinned current behavior), the invariant is vacuously satisfied. The structural witness: ApplyBlock's `ts_ok` predicate gates on `b.timestamp >= head.timestamp` only when `monotonic_gate = TRUE`; rejects otherwise. ProduceBlock samples timestamps only in `[head.timestamp, head.timestamp + MaxTimestampSkew]`, so producer-side blocks always satisfy T-1 regardless of the gate setting ÔÇö the gate's role is to reject adversarial / tampered inbound blocks at apply time. The C++ correspondent is the documented absence of an inter-block timestamp gate in `Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54` ÔÇö the test-pinned current behavior under SECURITY.md ┬žS-035 path 1 |
| `INV_DigestExcludesTimestamp` | T-2 (digest invariance under timestamp): for every pair of conceptual blocks `b1, b2` identical in every field except timestamp, `compute_block_digest(b1) = compute_block_digest(b2)`. The structural witness: `compute_block_digest`'s pre-image tuple omits the timestamp field (see the operator definition in ┬ž1 of the .tla); pure-function equality + abstract-hash discipline makes the equality automatic. The K-of-K Phase-2 digest deliberately excludes consensus-time metadata so committee members converge on the same digest despite local clock skew within the ┬▒30s validator window. The C++ correspondent is the `compute_block_digest` implementation at `src/node/producer.cpp` (~line 577) ÔÇö the timestamp field is omitted from the digest's pre-image. Lifted from R24A5 test scenario 7; the analytic source is `docs/proofs/S030-D2-Analysis.md` (D2 selective-abort resistance) |
| `INV_SigningBytesIncludesTimestamp` | T-3 (signing_bytes timestamp binding): for every pair of blocks `b1, b2` identical in every field except timestamp where `b1.timestamp /= b2.timestamp`, `compute_signing_bytes(b1) /= compute_signing_bytes(b2)`. The structural witness: `compute_signing_bytes`'s pre-image tuple INCLUDES timestamp; by abstract-hash injectivity (distinct pre-images map to distinct outputs), distinct timestamps produce distinct signing_bytes. The producer's full block hash IS timestamp-bound for chain-history integrity; a committee member's signature cannot replay across blocks differing in timestamp. The C++ correspondent is the `Block::signing_bytes` implementation at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp` ÔÇö the timestamp field is included via the leading tuple, alongside index/prev_hash/txs (plus the conditional partner_subset_hash + state_root tails per PROTOCOL.md ┬ž4.1). Lifted from R24A5 test scenario 6 |
| `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades` | T-4 (cascade via prev_hash): tampering `chain[i].timestamp` for an interior block invalidates the `compute_hash` cascade for `chain[i+1..head]` via the prev_hash chain. The structural witness: `compute_hash` of the tampered block /= prev_hash of the next block (because `compute_hash` INCLUDES timestamp, so a single-field mutation breaks the cascade); `validate_chain` returns FALSE; ReloadChain's failure path latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. State-form invariant: at every reachable state, if `tampered_at[n] /= "none"` AND the tampered block has at least one successor, then `validate_chain(chains[n])` is FALSE. The C++ correspondent is the `Chain::append` prev_hash check at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58` (the spec's `validate_chain` helper mirrors it) + the `Chain::load` head_hash recompute at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1987-2054` (composes with FB26's INV_LoadDetectsTampering via the shared `validate_chain` discipline). Lifted from R24A5 test scenarios 5 + 8 + S-021 closure |
| `INV_EqualTimestampAccepted` | T-5 (non-strict monotonicity): adjacent equal timestamps (`chain[i].timestamp = chain[i-1].timestamp`) are admissible ÔÇö block production within the same UTC second is legal. The structural witness: ProduceBlock samples timestamps from `[head.timestamp, head.timestamp + MaxTimestampSkew]` inclusive of the lower bound, so `head.timestamp` is a reachable sample; ApplyBlock's `ts_ok` predicate uses non-strict `>=`, so equal-timestamp adjacent blocks are admissible under both gate-OFF and gate-ON disciplines. The C++ correspondent is R24A5 test scenario 2: `Chain::append` accepts equal adjacent timestamps verbatim |
| `PROP_EventualBlockProduction` | Liveness: under fairness on ProduceBlock, chain length grows over time ÔÇö eventually some chain reaches MaxChainLength. The structural witness: ProduceBlock's pre-condition `Len(chains[n]) <= MaxChainLength` is enabled until saturation; weak fairness on the action set guarantees it fires until disabled. The dual of FB26's "no silent divergence" liveness track |
| `PROP_NoSilentDivergence` | Temporal composition of T-4 + S-021: tampered chain at any node fires the load-time recompute reject before any downstream apply extends the tampered chain. State-form witness: for every reachable state where `tampered_at[n] /= "none"` AND `chain[n]` has a successor block past the tamper site, eventually ReloadChain fires and latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. Composes with FB26's `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` via the shared `validate_chain` helper + the shared prev_hash continuity discipline. T-4 (HistoricalTamperCascades) is the structural source; this temporal property asserts the cascade is observable via the `load_throws` gate within the bounded reachable schedule |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-six specs above). The recommended `BlockTimestampMonotonic.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2}, MaxChainLength = 3, MaxTimestamp = 3, MaxTimestampSkew = 1, TxUniverse = {t1}, monotonic_gate = FALSE) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (ProduceBlock, ApplyBlock, TamperHistoricalTimestamp, ReloadChain) exercises every reachable interleaving of legitimate block production, cross-node gossip, adversarial tampering, and load-time reload. Variables modeled: `chains` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö each chain seeded with the GenesisBlock pinned at index=0 / timestamp=0 / prev_hash=GenesisHash per `make_genesis_block` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp:301`), `pending_inbox` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö the gossip queue between nodes; ProduceBlock at one node appends to other nodes' inboxes, ApplyBlock drains the head subject to prev_hash + optional ts_ok gate), `tampered_at` (Nodes Ôćĺ 0..MaxChainLength Ôł¬ {"none"} ÔÇö interior tamper site logged by TamperHistoricalTimestamp), `load_throws` (Nodes Ôćĺ BOOLEAN ÔÇö latches TRUE the moment ReloadChain detects a cascade-broken prev_hash). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (samples timestamp from `[head.timestamp, head.timestamp + MaxTimestampSkew]` inclusive on both ends ÔÇö lower bound makes T-5 EqualTimestampAccepted reachable, upper bound makes T-1 monotonic samples reachable; broadcasts to other-node inboxes), `ApplyBlock(n)` (drains pending_inbox head; validates prev_hash continuity + the optional `monotonic_gate` strict-monotonic gate; appends on success, silently drops on reject ÔÇö the exception-surface invariants are FB26 / FB27 territory), `TamperHistoricalTimestamp(n)` (adversary mutates an interior block's timestamp; the post-tamper `compute_hash` differs because the pre-image INCLUDES timestamp, breaking the prev_hash cascade at the next block), `ReloadChain(n)` (the spec-layer projection of `Chain::load`; walks `validate_chain`; latches `load_throws` on prev_hash mismatch ÔÇö the T-4 boundary catch).

This spec captures the just-shipped R24A5 `test-time-monotonicity` unit test at the state-machine layer. The analytic source (`src/main.cpp::test-time-monotonicity` at lines 28776..29049 + `tools/test_time_monotonicity.sh`) pins 17 assertions across 9 scenarios; the TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the four cryptographic surfaces (chain identity, signing_bytes, digest, optional apply-time gate) into four actions + six invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **Strict-monotonic gate (T-1)** is captured by `INV_TimestampMonotonic` conditional on the `monotonic_gate` CONSTANT. The default cfg leaves the gate DISABLED to match the current `Chain::append` behavior pinned by R24A5 scenarios 1, 2, 3, 8 (backward / equal / far-future / negative timestamps all admitted at the chain layer). Flipping the gate to TRUE exercises the forward-looking S-035 path-1 contract for spec-coverage purposes ahead of the actual code change.

2. **Digest excludes timestamp (T-2)** is captured by `INV_DigestExcludesTimestamp`. The K-of-K Phase-2 digest deliberately omits consensus-time metadata so committee members converge on the same digest despite local clock skew within the ┬▒30s validator window. The C++ correspondent is `compute_block_digest` at `src/node/producer.cpp` ~line 577; the analytic backing is the D2 selective-abort resistance argument in `docs/proofs/S030-D2-Analysis.md`.

3. **Signing_bytes includes timestamp (T-3)** is captured by `INV_SigningBytesIncludesTimestamp`. The producer's full block hash IS timestamp-bound for chain-history integrity; a committee member's signature cannot replay across blocks differing in timestamp. The C++ correspondent is `Block::signing_bytes` at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp` (the timestamp field is included via the leading tuple, alongside the conditional partner_subset_hash + state_root tails per PROTOCOL.md ┬ž4.1).

4. **Historical tamper cascades (T-4)** is captured by `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades`. Tampering an interior block's timestamp breaks `compute_hash` at that block (since `compute_hash` INCLUDES timestamp), which breaks `prev_hash` at the next block, which makes `validate_chain` return FALSE at load time, which latches `load_throws`. Composes with FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla's `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` via the shared `validate_chain` helper.

5. **Equal-timestamp acceptance (T-5)** is captured by `INV_EqualTimestampAccepted`. Block production within the same UTC second is admissible (non-strict monotonicity); ProduceBlock's sample range includes `head.timestamp` as the lower bound, and ApplyBlock's `ts_ok` predicate uses non-strict `>=`.

The two temporal properties (PROP_EventualBlockProduction + PROP_NoSilentDivergence) lift the live-progress + cascade-observability claims to the temporal layer. PROP_NoSilentDivergence is the headline composition: any tamper at any node fires the load-time reject before downstream apply extends the tampered chain ÔÇö the dual liveness of FB26's safety track.

**Out of scope** (consistent with the R24A5 test's documented scope):
- The validator's wall-clock window check (`|B.timestamp - now()| <= 30s` at `src/node/validator.cpp::check_timestamp`). This is a validator-time gate (Preliminaries V14) orthogonal to the chain-layer monotonicity contract; the spec abstracts `now()` and the ┬▒30s window into the `MaxTimestampSkew` constant at ProduceBlock time.
- The partner_subset_hash + state_root threading in signing_bytes (PROTOCOL.md ┬ž4.1, R4 Phase 3 conditional + S-033 conditional). The spec's `compute_signing_bytes` is a timestamp-focused projection; the full signing_bytes specification is FB26 (BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla) territory.
- The genesis-trust pin (validator.cpp:19 short-circuit at index 0). The chain init seeds with `GenesisBlock`; the spec never re-applies genesis.
- Cryptographic soundness of SHA-256 (A2) and Ed25519 EUF-CMA (A1). The abstract-hash discipline + abstract-sig pattern is FA-track territory (FB23 FrostVerify.tla).
- The ┬▒30s validator window's interaction with operator-side clock skew. The spec's `MaxTimestampSkew` abstracts this; the wall-clock skew model is documented in ┬žV14 of Preliminaries + the S-003 validator-window analysis.

Companion analytic source: `src/main.cpp::test-time-monotonicity` (R24A5, 17 assertions across 9 scenarios at lines 28776..29049) + `tools/test_time_monotonicity.sh` (the shell wrapper). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of those assertions: INV_TimestampMonotonic lifts T-1's forward-looking strict-monotonic gate (current code has the gate DISABLED per S-035 path 1); INV_DigestExcludesTimestamp lifts T-2's digest-omission (R24A5 scenario 7); INV_SigningBytesIncludesTimestamp lifts T-3's signing_bytes inclusion (R24A5 scenario 6); INV_HistoricalTamperCascades lifts T-4's prev_hash cascade (R24A5 scenarios 5 + 8 + S-021 composition); INV_EqualTimestampAccepted lifts T-5's non-strict monotonicity (R24A5 scenario 2).

Cross-reference. FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model ÔÇö the abstract-sig discipline this spec's compute_signing_bytes operator relies on for INV_3 injectivity), FB24 `MakeContribCommitment.tla` (S-030 D2 commit-binding ÔÇö the distinct-pre-image property this spec's abstract-hash discipline mirrors), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 lifetime-bound model), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition ÔÇö sibling state-integrity surface; this spec's T-4 HistoricalTamperCascades + PROP_NoSilentDivergence compose with FB26's INV_LoadDetectsTampering via the shared prev_hash continuity discipline + the shared `validate_chain` helper), FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` (S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth), FB28 `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.tla` (S-006 Phase-1 same-gen detection). FB29 (this spec ÔÇö the Block.timestamp monotonicity + digest-exclusion contract state machine). Together FB26 + FB29 witness the chain-identity + timestamp-binding surface end-to-end: FB26 covers the state_root + apply-time + load-time integrity gates; FB29 covers the timestamp threading across compute_hash / signing_bytes / compute_block_digest plus the forward-looking strict-monotonic gate at apply time.

### ChainPrevHashLink.tla Ôćĺ R25 (prev_hash chain-link contract + cascade-detection invariants)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `chains` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö each block carries the four invariant-relevant fields index/prev_hash/body_hash/compute_hash), `pending_inbox` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö gossip queue between nodes), `tampered_at` (Nodes Ôćĺ 0..MaxChainLength Ôł¬ {"none"} ÔÇö interior tamper site, latches across actions), `load_throws` (Nodes Ôćĺ BOOLEAN ÔÇö reload reject latch), `rejected_by` (Nodes Ôćĺ {"none", "chain", "validator", "both"} ÔÇö latches WHICH gate fired on the most recent reject; "both" indicates the two-layer defense fired in concert), `ghost_chain_history` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö append-only legitimate-history record that TamperHistorical does NOT mutate; the INV_AppendOnly witness) |
| `INV_PrevHashLinkValid` | T-1 (happy path): for every non-genesis block in every chain, `block[i].prev_hash = block[i-1].compute_hash`. The structural witness: the chain only grows via ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock, both of which construct/validate blocks with `prev_hash = head_hash(chains[n])` before appending. The invariant is asserted on the SUBCHAIN preceding the tamper site (`tampered_at[n] = "none" \/ i <= tampered_at[n]`) so TamperHistorical doesn't spuriously invalidate INV_1 (the cascade past the tamper site is captured by INV_HistoricalTamperCascades). The C++ correspondent is the per-block link discipline enforced by `Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58` (every append checks `b.prev_hash == head_hash()`). Lifted from R25 test scenario 1 |
| `INV_GenesisPrevHashZero` | T-2 (chain-anchor convention): the genesis block (chain[1] in 1-indexed TLA) has `prev_hash = ZeroHash`. The structural witness: Init seeds with `GenesisBlock` whose `prev_hash = ZeroHash`; TamperHistorical's quantifier is `i \in 2..Len(chains[n])` so genesis is skipped. The C++ correspondent is `make_genesis_block` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp` leaving `prev_hash` at its default-constructed all-zero `Hash{}` (the chain-identity anchor for the empty-chain bootstrap path). Lifted from R25 test scenario 2 |
| `INV_WrongPrevHashRejected` | T-3 (two-layer defense): for every reachable state, every block that has ever been appended to `chains[n]` satisfied `prev_hash_ok(b, chains[n])` at append time. The state-form witness: ApplyBlock's success branch is the ONLY path that drains an inbox block into the chain, and it's gated on the shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate; the reject branch silently drops from inbox without extending the chain, latching `rejected_by[n] = "both"` to record the two-layer defense (chain-layer + validator-layer both gate on the same condition). The C++ correspondents are `Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58` (chain-layer gate; throws `"Block prev_hash mismatch"`) AND `BlockValidator::check_prev_hash` at `src/node/validator.cpp:43-48` (validator-layer gate; returns `{false, "prev_hash mismatch"}`). The two-layer defense ensures any regression weakening one gate is caught by the other. Lifted from R25 test scenarios 3a (all-zero prev_hash at height 2), 3b (0xFF... prev_hash at height 2), and 6 (empty prev_hash at height 1) |
| `INV_ReloadPreservesLinks` | T-4 (round-trip identity): for every reachable state where the chain is untampered (`tampered_at[n] = "none"`), `load_throws[n]` is FALSE AND every per-block link in `chains[n]` holds. The structural witness: the abstract-hash discipline is purely structural (no serialization noise), so the in-memory chain and a hypothetical reloaded copy have byte-identical prev_hash linkage. The C++ correspondent is `Chain::save` + `Chain::load` round-trip ÔÇö the S-021 chain-integrity gate enforces head_hash globally; T-4 additionally pins the per-block link discipline so a regression that bypassed the head_hash check OR changed compute_hash inputs would still trip on a per-block link recompute. Lifted from R25 test scenario 4 |
| `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades` | T-5 (cascade via prev_hash): tampering ANY compute_hash-contributing field at `chain[i]` invalidates the downstream prev_hash linkage at `chain[i+1]` ÔÇö because `chain[i+1].prev_hash` was bound to the PRE-tamper compute_hash of `chain[i]`. The structural witness: compute_hash is injective over its full pre-image tuple (abstract-hash discipline); any single-field mutation changes compute_hash; `validate_chain` returns FALSE at load time; ReloadChain's failure path latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. State-form invariant: at every reachable state, if `tampered_at[n] = k` with `k \in 2..Len(chains[n])` AND `k < Len(chains[n])`, then `validate_chain(chains[n])` is FALSE. The C++ correspondent is the load-time recompute discipline at `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::load` (the per-block prev_hash continuity walk inside the S-021 wrap). Lifted from R25 test scenario 5 |
| `INV_AppendOnly` | T-7 (no retroactive rewrite): for every reachable state with no tamper, `chains[n]` and `ghost_chain_history[n]` are byte-identical sequences. The structural witness: `ghost_chain_history` is updated only by ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock (the legitimate extension actions); TamperHistorical does NOT touch the ghost. Equality between `chains[n]` and `ghost_chain_history[n]` in the no-tamper branch proves legitimate chain extension never rewrites earlier blocks ÔÇö the append-only contract on which fork-resolution and snapshot consistency depend. The C++ correspondent is `Chain::append`'s vector-push-back semantics at `src/chain/chain.cpp` (the chain's `blocks_` vector grows via `push_back`; existing entries are not rewritten). Lifted from R25 test scenario 7 |
| `PROP_EventualBlockProduction` | Liveness: under fairness on ProduceBlock, chain length grows over time ÔÇö eventually some chain reaches MaxChainLength. The structural witness: ProduceBlock's pre-condition `Len(chains[n]) <= MaxChainLength` is enabled until saturation; weak fairness on the action set guarantees it fires until disabled. The dual of FB26's + FB29's "no silent divergence" liveness track |
| `PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected` | Temporal composition of T-5 + S-021: if `tampered_at[n] /= "none"` AND `chains[n]` has at least one successor block past the tamper site, then eventually ReloadChain fires and latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. State-form witness: ReloadChain's failure path is enabled whenever `validate_chain(chains[n])` is FALSE; INV_HistoricalTamperCascades pins that the tamper structurally invalidates validate_chain; weak fairness on ReloadChain guarantees the load_throws latch within the bounded reachable schedule. Composes with FB26's `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` + FB29's `PROP_NoSilentDivergence` via the shared `validate_chain` helper + the shared prev_hash continuity discipline |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-seven specs above). The recommended `ChainPrevHashLink.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2}, MaxChainLength = 3, BodyHashes = {bh1, bh2, bh3}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (ProduceBlock, ApplyBlock, TamperHistorical, ReloadChain) exercises every reachable interleaving of legitimate block production, cross-node gossip, adversarial body-hash tampering, and load-time reload. Variables modeled: `chains` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö each chain seeded with the GenesisBlock pinned at index=0 / prev_hash=ZeroHash / body_hash=GenesisBodyHash per `make_genesis_block` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp`), `pending_inbox` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö the gossip queue between nodes; ProduceBlock at one node appends to other nodes' inboxes, ApplyBlock drains the head subject to the shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate), `tampered_at` (Nodes Ôćĺ 0..MaxChainLength Ôł¬ {"none"} ÔÇö interior tamper site logged by TamperHistorical), `load_throws` (Nodes Ôćĺ BOOLEAN ÔÇö latches TRUE the moment ReloadChain detects a cascade-broken prev_hash), `rejected_by` (Nodes Ôćĺ {"none", "chain", "validator", "both"} ÔÇö latches "both" on every wrong-link reject to record the two-layer defense), `ghost_chain_history` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) ÔÇö append-only legitimate-history record that TamperHistorical does NOT mutate; the INV_AppendOnly witness). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (constructs a block with `prev_hash = head_hash(chains[n])` and a fresh `body_hash` from BodyHashes; appends to chains[n] AND ghost_chain_history[n]; broadcasts to other-node inboxes), `ApplyBlock(n)` (drains pending_inbox head; validates via `prev_hash_ok`; appends on success AND mirrors into ghost_chain_history, drops + latches `rejected_by = "both"` on reject), `TamperHistorical(n)` (adversary mutates an interior block's body_hash; the post-tamper `compute_hash` differs because the pre-image INCLUDES body_hash, breaking the prev_hash cascade at the next block; `ghost_chain_history` is UNCHANGED), `ReloadChain(n)` (the spec-layer projection of `Chain::load`; walks `validate_chain`; latches `load_throws` on prev_hash mismatch ÔÇö the T-5 boundary catch).

This spec captures the just-shipped R25 `test-chain-prev-hash-link` unit test at the state-machine layer. The analytic source (`src/main.cpp::test-chain-prev-hash-link` at lines 29088..29395 + `tools/test_chain_prev_hash_link.sh`) pins ~22 assertions across 7 scenarios; the TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the five operational surfaces (chain-layer apply, validator-layer apply, hash injectivity, reload integrity, adversarial tamper cascade) into four actions + seven invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **Happy path (T-1)** is captured by `INV_PrevHashLinkValid`. The chain only grows via ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock, both of which require `prev_hash = head_hash(chains[n])` before appending; the post-condition is the per-block link `chain[i].prev_hash = chain[i-1].compute_hash` on every legitimately-extended chain.

2. **Genesis anchor (T-2)** is captured by `INV_GenesisPrevHashZero`. The chain init seeds with `GenesisBlock` whose `prev_hash = ZeroHash` (the all-zero sentinel ÔÇö no predecessor). TamperHistorical's quantifier is `i \in 2..Len(chains[n])`, so the genesis block is structurally excluded from tampering.

3. **Two-layer defense (T-3)** is captured by `INV_WrongPrevHashRejected`. The shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate models both the chain-layer (`Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58`) and the validator-layer (`BlockValidator::check_prev_hash` at `src/node/validator.cpp:43-48`) gates; ApplyBlock's reject branch latches `rejected_by = "both"` to observe the two-layer defense firing in concert. The defense ensures any regression weakening one gate is caught by the other.

4. **Reload integrity (T-4)** is captured by `INV_ReloadPreservesLinks`. The abstract-hash discipline is purely structural; the in-memory chain and a hypothetical reloaded copy have byte-identical prev_hash linkage. T-4 composes with S-021 (the chain.json wrapping object's head_hash recompute at load time) ÔÇö INV_4 pins the per-block link discipline so a regression bypassing the head_hash check OR changing compute_hash inputs would still trip.

5. **Cascade detection (T-5)** is captured by `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades` + `PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected`. TamperHistorical's body_hash mutation changes compute_hash (abstract-hash injectivity); `chain[i+1].prev_hash` no longer matches the post-tamper compute_hash; `validate_chain` returns FALSE; ReloadChain latches `load_throws`. The temporal property pins that the cascade is eventually observable.

6. **Empty-prev-hash at height 1 (T-6)** is captured by `INV_WrongPrevHashRejected`. A height-1 block with `prev_hash = ZeroHash` differs from `head_hash(genesis-only-chain) = GenesisBlock.compute_hash` (which is NOT zero ÔÇö genesis hashes its own index/body_hash/etc. via the BLOCK-tagged tuple); the shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate rejects, and `rejected_by = "both"` records the two-layer defense firing.

7. **Append-only (T-7)** is captured by `INV_AppendOnly` via the ghost-history snapshot. `ghost_chain_history` is updated only by ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock (legitimate extension); TamperHistorical does NOT touch the ghost. In the no-tamper branch, `chains[n] = ghost_chain_history[n]` proves legitimate extension never rewrites earlier blocks ÔÇö the contract on which fork-resolution and snapshot consistency depend.

**Out of scope** (consistent with the R25 test's documented scope):
- Cryptographic soundness of SHA-256 (A2). The abstract-hash discipline + pre-image injectivity is the spec-layer abstraction; FB23 FrostVerify.tla covers the cryptographic side.
- The C++-side throw-exception semantics. The spec models the chain-state outcome (block dropped from inbox without extending `chains[n]`); the exception-surface invariants live in FB27 JsonValidation.tla (S-018 clear-diagnostic).
- The wrap-on-disk byte format (chain.json head_hash + blocks). The spec abstracts serialization into the pure-function `validate_chain` helper; S-021's chain.json wrapping is FB26 territory.
- Fork-resolution semantics (S-029). The spec is single-chain; `resolve_fork`'s heaviest-sig-set + fewer-aborts + smallest-hash tie-breaker is FA-track territory.
- The specific identity of the field being tampered. FB30's body_hash abstraction collapses ALL compute_hash-contributing fields (timestamp, creators, txs, etc.) into a single opaque body-hash universe; FB29 BlockTimestampMonotonic.tla covers the timestamp-specific cascade as a sibling specialization.

Companion analytic source: `src/main.cpp::test-chain-prev-hash-link` (R25, ~22 assertions across 7 scenarios at lines 29088..29395) + `tools/test_chain_prev_hash_link.sh` (the shell wrapper). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of those assertions: INV_PrevHashLinkValid lifts T-1's happy-path linkage; INV_GenesisPrevHashZero lifts T-2's chain-anchor convention; INV_WrongPrevHashRejected lifts T-3 + T-6's two-layer defense; INV_ReloadPreservesLinks lifts T-4's round-trip identity; INV_HistoricalTamperCascades + PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected lift T-5's cascade; INV_AppendOnly lifts T-7's no-retroactive-rewrite contract.

Cross-reference. FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model ÔÇö the abstract-sig discipline), FB24 `MakeContribCommitment.tla` (S-030 D2 commit-binding ÔÇö the distinct-pre-image property this spec's abstract-hash discipline mirrors), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 lifetime-bound model), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition ÔÇö sibling state-integrity surface; this spec's INV_HistoricalTamperCascades + PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected compose with FB26's INV_LoadDetectsTampering via the shared prev_hash continuity discipline + the shared `validate_chain` helper), FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` (S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth), FB28 `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.tla` (S-006 Phase-1 same-gen detection), FB29 `BlockTimestampMonotonic.tla` (R24A5 timestamp monotonicity + digest-exclusion ÔÇö closely related sibling; FB29 pins the cascade for the timestamp field specifically, while FB30 generalizes to any compute_hash-contributing field via the body_hash abstraction). FB30 (this spec ÔÇö the prev_hash chain-link state machine + cascade-detection invariants). Together FB26 + FB29 + FB30 witness the chain-identity surface end-to-end: FB26 covers the state_root + apply-time + load-time integrity gates; FB29 covers the timestamp threading across compute_hash / signing_bytes / compute_block_digest plus the forward-looking strict-monotonic gate; FB30 covers the prev_hash chain-link contract at both the chain-layer and validator-layer gates plus the append-only + reload-preserve + tamper-cascade properties.
### SnapshotIntegrity.tla Ôćĺ FA-Snapshot (S-012 + S-037 + S-038 composition)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `live_chain` (Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block) where Block = [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs]), `live_state` (Nodes Ôćĺ [accounts, stakes, registrants, dapp_registry] each a SUBSET of Slots ÔÇö the four mutable maps that survive across snapshot boundaries and contribute to the a:/s:/r:/d: state_root namespaces), `snapshot_blob` (Nodes Ôćĺ Snapshot Ôł¬ {NoSnapshot} where Snapshot has [tail_chain, serialized_state, head_state_root]), `apply_throws` / `restore_throws` (Nodes Ôćĺ BOOLEAN), `tampered_at` (Nodes Ôćĺ TamperSite where TamperSite = {"none", "chain", "state", "dapp_registry"}) |
| `INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces` | T-S1 composed with T-S2 (10-namespace round-trip + S-037 dapp_registry inclusion). For every node-pair (n, n2) where n2 has successfully restored from n's snapshot (no `restore_throws` latch + `live_chain[n2] = snapshot_blob[n].tail_chain`), the restored `live_state[n2]` equals `snapshot_blob[n].serialized_state` across all four namespaces AND `state_root_of(live_state[n2]) = snapshot_blob[n].head_state_root`. The headline composition: dapp_registry round-trips under the `d:` namespace AND the state_root over all namespaces matches byte-for-byte. The structural witness for "the S-037 closure threads dapp_registry through serialize_state + restore_from_snapshot symmetrically; the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911 verifies the recomputed state_root equals the snapshot's stored head_state_root byte-for-byte" ÔÇö without S-037 the recompute would fail on any DApp-active chain |
| `INV_StateRootGateFiresOnRestoreTamper` | T-S4 (Tamper Detection at Snapshot Boundary). If a node's snapshot has been tampered at state or dapp_registry layer AND another node has installed live_state from the tampered snapshot, then `restore_throws` MUST be TRUE ÔÇö the contrapositive: if `restore_throws[n2] = FALSE` after installing live_state from a tampered snapshot, then `state_root_of(serialized_state) = head_state_root`, contradicting the tamper. The structural witness for the post-restore recompute-vs-stored gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911 catching any state-modifying tamper that did NOT also re-sign the head_state_root |
| `INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038` | T-S3 (Producer-Side State_Root Wiring / S-038 closure). Across every reachable state, every block in `live_chain[n]` has `state_root` in `{ZeroRoot, state_root_of(head_state(prefix))}` where prefix is the chain up to that block. The post-S-038 invariant: the producer's tentative-chain dry-run at node.cpp:1024-1117 (steps 1-5) guarantees `body.state_root` is populated with the canonical post-apply Merkle root, NOT empty. The pre-S-038 dormant-gate case (where `body.state_root = Hash{}` and the apply-time gate's `if (b.state_root != zero)` short-circuit meant the gate never actually fired on production blocks) is captured by the `ZeroRoot` disjunct; post-S-038 every produced block satisfies the second disjunct |
| `INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips` | T-S2 standalone (S-037 closure isolated). For every node-pair (n, n2) where n2 has successfully restored n's snapshot AND no tampering was observed, `live_state[n2].dapp_registry = snapshot_blob[n].serialized_state.dapp_registry`. Standalone sub-claim of INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces ÔÇö called out so a regression that re-removes the `d:` namespace from `Chain::serialize_state` at chain.cpp:1653-1669 would surface as a single-invariant failure in TLC traces (instant regression diagnosis). The structural witness for the S-037 closure: dapp_registry is emitted at serialize AND consumed at restore symmetrically; without the symmetry the recompute gate fires |
| `INV_RestoreDeterminism` | T-S5 (Restore Determinism). For every node-pair (n1, n2): if `snapshot_blob[n1] = snapshot_blob[n2]` AND `live_chain[n1] = live_chain[n2]` AND both have completed restore without throwing, then `live_state[n1] = live_state[n2]`. The structural witness for "restore is a pure function of (snapshot, current_chain) ÔÇö the C++ `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` has no fresh-randomness inputs". The state-machine projection of byte-determinism: two nodes consuming byte-identical snapshots reach byte-identical post-restore states |
| `INV_NoSilentDivergence` | T-S4 cross-node form (the snapshot-pathway mirror of FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla's same-named invariant). If two nodes have the same restored chain but different state_roots, at least one of `apply_throws` or `restore_throws` MUST be TRUE ÔÇö the integrity gates fire before the divergent state can survive at apply time. Restricted to the snapshot pathway via the antecedent's requirement that both nodes have non-empty `live_chain` (i.e., either produced or restored). Composed with FB26's INV_NoSilentDivergence (the chain.json wrap + apply-time pathway), the two invariants together exhaust the state-divergence surface across both at-rest pathways (chain.json save/load AND snapshot serialize/restore) |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-seven specs above). The recommended `SnapshotIntegrity.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2}, MaxHeight = 3, Slots = {sl1, sl2}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. The seven-action state machine (ProduceBlock, SerializeSnapshot, RestoreFromSnapshot, ApplyBlockAfterRestore, TamperSnapshot, TamperLiveState, Stutter) exercises every reachable interleaving of producer-side state_root population (S-038 wiring), snapshot emission, cross-node restore with post-restore gate firing, post-restore apply with the S-033 gate firing, and the four adversary surfaces (chain-tamper / state-tamper / dapp_registry-tamper / live-state tamper). Variables modeled: `live_chain` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ Seq(Block)` where Block has [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs] ÔÇö matches the C++ `std::vector<Block> blocks_` at `include/determ/chain/chain.hpp`), `live_state` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ [accounts, stakes, registrants, dapp_registry]` each a SUBSET of Slots ÔÇö the four mutable maps that survive across snapshot boundaries and contribute to the a:/s:/r:/d: state_root namespaces; the spec's collapse of the C++ `std::map<std::string, AccountState> accounts_`, `std::map<std::string, StakeEntry> stakes_`, `std::map<std::string, RegistryEntry> registrants_`, `std::map<std::string, DAppEntry> dapp_registry_` into the SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction is the standard FB-track tractability move ÔÇö distinct contents per namespace produce distinct state_roots by the abstract-hash discriminator), `snapshot_blob` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ Snapshot Ôł¬ {NoSnapshot}` where Snapshot has [tail_chain, serialized_state, head_state_root] ÔÇö matches the JSON form at chain.cpp:1541-1701; the `head_state_root` field corresponds to the tail-head's `state_root` field stored in the snapshot's tail-header bundle and consumed by the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911), `apply_throws` / `restore_throws` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ BOOLEAN` ÔÇö latching sentinels for the two integrity gates: `apply_throws` for the S-033 apply-time gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446; `restore_throws` for the post-restore state_root recompute gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911), `tampered_at` (function `NodeId Ôćĺ TamperSite` where TamperSite = {"none", "chain", "state", "dapp_registry"} ÔÇö spec-only audit field tracking the most-recent adversary site; the dapp_registry branch is called out separately so a regression that re-removes the `d:` namespace from `Chain::serialize_state` surfaces as a tamper-detection failure on this specific site). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (the C++ Node::try_finalize_round at node.cpp:1024-1117 ÔÇö five steps collapsed into a single atomic action: build_body with state_root=Hash{}, tentative-chain dry-run, populate `body.state_root` via the tentative chain's `compute_state_root()` (the S-038 wiring), apply on live chain, advance. INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038 is the structural witness that step 4 always fires ÔÇö every produced block carries a non-zero `state_root`), `SerializeSnapshot(n)` (Chain::serialize_state at chain.cpp:1541-1701 ÔÇö emits the four-map state shape verbatim plus tail_chain and head_state_root; pre-S-037 the `dapp_registry` field was absent, the spec models the post-S-037 form with all four maps emitted; INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips locks in the S-037 closure), `RestoreFromSnapshot(n2)` (Chain::restore_from_snapshot at chain.cpp:1703-1932 ÔÇö replays tail_chain, rehydrates serialized_state, recomputes state_root_of(restored) and compares to head_state_root via the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911; on mismatch latches `restore_throws[n2]` and leaves the chain uninstalled), `ApplyBlockAfterRestore(n2)` (Chain::apply_transactions S-033 gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446 ÔÇö the post-restore apply path; declared state_root must match computed post-apply state_root or `apply_throws` latches), `TamperSnapshot(n)` (three-disjunct adversary surface: (a) interior tail-chain block, (b) state-namespace contents, (c) dapp_registry specifically ÔÇö the S-037 closure surface; the wrap header's `head_state_root` is NOT patched, so the next RestoreFromSnapshot MUST detect by recompute-vs-stored mismatch), `TamperLiveState(n)` (at-rest tamper of live state between serialize and restore ÔÇö mutates live_state.accounts; exercises the cross-node INV_NoSilentDivergence: producer's drift relative to a previously-emitted snapshot is observable at the state-root layer).

This spec captures the post-S-037 / post-S-038 snapshot-pathway state-integrity surface at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-S1..T-S5 in `S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` ┬ž1 / ┬ž4.5 + the FA-Apply-12 sub-theorem in `AppliedReceiptRestore.md`) establishes that three independently-shipped mechanisms compose:

1. **S-033 (state_root commitment)**: `Block::signing_bytes` binds `state_root` under the zero-skip backward-compat shim. The apply-time gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446 recomputes the state root post-apply and compares to the block's declared `state_root`, throwing on mismatch.

2. **S-037 (dapp_registry + applied_inbound_receipts snapshot coverage)**: the `d:` and `i:` namespaces contribute leaves to the state_root Merkle commitment. Pre-S-037 the snapshot serializer omitted these; a DApp-active chain's snapshot would carry the tail head's correct state_root in JSON, but `restore_from_snapshot` would rehydrate a chain whose recomputed state_root differed ÔÇö the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911 would loud-fail. S-037 added both namespaces to `serialize_state` + `restore_from_snapshot` with the full set of fields needed to reproduce the value-hash byte-for-byte.

3. **S-038 (producer-side state_root population)**: pre-S-038 every produced block had `body.state_root = Hash{}`; the apply-time gate's `if (b.state_root != zero)` short-circuit meant the receiver-side check was DORMANT on production blocks. S-038 added the tentative-chain dry-run pattern at node.cpp:1024-1117 so every produced block carries a non-zero `state_root`.

The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into seven actions + six invariants:

- **Ten-namespace round-trip** is captured by `INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces`. The four-map state shape `[accounts, stakes, registrants, dapp_registry]` is the post-S-037 mutable-state surface that contributes to the state_root commitment via the a:/s:/r:/d: namespaces; the remaining six namespaces (i:/b:/m:/p:/k:/c:) collapse cleanly into the same SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction under `state_root_of`'s tuple discriminator (the abstract-hash discipline used by FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla).

- **DApp registry round-trip (S-037 closure)** is captured by `INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips`, called out as a standalone sub-claim so a regression that re-removes the `d:` namespace from `Chain::serialize_state` surfaces as a single-invariant failure in TLC traces.

- **Producer-side state_root wiring (S-038 closure)** is captured by `INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038`. The post-S-038 contract: every produced block carries a non-zero `state_root` populated via the tentative-chain dry-run.

- **Tamper detection at snapshot boundary** is captured by `INV_StateRootGateFiresOnRestoreTamper` (post-restore recompute fires on any state-modifying tamper) + `INV_NoSilentDivergence` (cross-node form ÔÇö divergent state_roots imply at least one throw-gate latched).

- **Restore determinism** is captured by `INV_RestoreDeterminism`. Restore is a pure function of (snapshot, current_chain).

The abstract-hash model (`state_root_of` as a pure function returning a tagged tuple over the four namespace contents) is the standard TLA+ projection of A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance) ÔÇö distinct pre-images map to distinct outputs by tuple inequality. The cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (Preliminaries.md ┬ž2.1).

**Out of scope** (consistent with `S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` ┬ž6 + this spec's ┬ž11 header comment):

- The basic apply-determinism invariant (covered by FA-Apply-1 / FB5 AccountState.tla). FB31's `apply` operator is the spec-layer projection; the underlying determinism property is FB5 territory.
- The cross-shard receipt dedup invariant (covered by FB17 AppliedReceiptRestore.tla / FA-Apply-12). FB31 composes this via INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces' `i:` namespace coverage (collapsed into the SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction).
- The chain.json wrap (FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla territory). FB31's RestoreFromSnapshot models the in-memory snapshot restore path; the disk-level chain.json wrap + head_hash check is the parallel state-integrity boundary covered by FB26.
- The byte-level codec round-trip (the JSON encoding / decoding fidelity). The `serialized_state` field is modeled as a TLA+ record; the codec is FA-track territory (`tools/test_state_root_namespaces.sh`, 12 assertions).
- Pre-S-038 historical blocks bypass the apply-time gate (intentional backward-compat via the zero-skip shim). INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038 captures this via the `b.state_root = ZeroRoot` disjunct; post-S-038 every produced block has non-zero state_root by construction.
- Ed25519 EUF-CMA / SHA-256 collision resistance bounds (the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory).

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` (the ten-namespace coverage theorem T-1..T-5; FB31 lifts T-5 Snapshot Round-Trip Soundness to the state-machine layer with the cross-node restore + adversarial tamper enumeration), `docs/proofs/AppliedReceiptRestore.md` (FA-Apply-12 ÔÇö the receipt dedup-set restore correctness sub-theorem; FB17 AppliedReceiptRestore.tla covers the receipt-set's standalone state machine; FB31 unifies this with the broader 10-namespace surface via INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces' `i:` namespace coverage), `docs/proofs/BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` (the composition theorem T-1..T-5; FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla covers the chain.json wrap + apply-time gate composition; FB31 is the snapshot-pathway sibling), `docs/proofs/AccountStateInvariants.md` (FA-Apply-1 ÔÇö apply determinism, the prerequisite for restore equivalence).

Cross-reference. FB5 `AccountState.tla` (FA-Apply-1 ÔÇö apply determinism, the load-bearing input to INV_RestoreDeterminism and the ApplyBlockAfterRestore action's determinism contract), FB6 `Snapshot.tla` (FA-Apply-2 ÔÇö the basic snapshot/restore state machine; FB31's foundation. FB6 collapses the 10 state_root namespaces to two ÔÇö `a:` balances+nonces and `b:` accumulated counters ÔÇö per its file header; FB31 extends to the full four-map surface that contributes to the a:/s:/r:/d: namespaces plus the SUBSET-of-Slots projection for the remaining six namespaces, the dapp_registry round-trip via INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips, and the producer-side state_root wiring via INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038), FB17 `AppliedReceiptRestore.tla` (FA-Apply-12 ÔÇö the `i:` namespace's standalone snapshot lifecycle, the S-037 closure witness for the receipt dedup-set; FB31 composes this with the nine other namespaces via the SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (chain.json wrap + apply-time gate ÔÇö S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition; FB31 is the snapshot-pathway sibling; FB26's INV_NoSilentDivergence and FB31's INV_NoSilentDivergence together exhaust the state-divergence surface across both at-rest pathways). FB31 (this spec ÔÇö the post-S-037 / post-S-038 snapshot integrity surface). Together FB6 + FB17 + FB26 + FB31 witness the full state-integrity surface at the state-machine layer: FB6 is the basic snapshot/restore foundation; FB17 is the cross-shard receipt-set sub-claim; FB26 covers the chain.json + apply-time gates; FB31 closes the snapshot-pathway gap to the post-S-037 + post-S-038 closure.
### CrossShardReceiptRoundtrip.tla Ôćĺ FA-CrossShard (composition of FA-Apply-9 + FA-Apply-12 + FA-Apply-13)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `INV_TypeOK` | shape of `live_state_src` (SrcState = [balance: Domains Ôćĺ Nat, outbound_emitted_count: Nat, height: Nat]), `live_state_dst` (DstState = [balance: Domains Ôćĺ Nat, applied_inbound_receipts: SUBSET DedupKey, inbound_first_seen: DedupKey Ôćĺ Nat, height: Nat]), `gossip_inflight` / `inbound_pool_dst` / `eligible_for_apply` (Seq(Receipt) ÔÇö the three transit queues), `snapshot_blob_src` / `snapshot_blob_dst` (per-shard snapshot or NoSnapshot sentinel), `apply_throws` (BOOLEAN ÔÇö latches on dedup violation or apply-time invariant breach) |
| `INV_NoDoubleCredit` | T-RT4 (apply-side dedup, composition of FA-Apply-9 / T-R1 + T-R2 from FB14). For every receipt R applied at destination, R.dedup_key is in `applied_inbound_receipts` AND no two `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst` steps for the same dedup_key both fire the first-credit branch. The structural witness is the if/then/else split in `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst`: the fresh branch requires `k \notin applied_inbound_receipts`, so a second apply for the same key MUST route to the duplicate branch. Matches `chain.cpp:1363-1381` + the dedup check helper at `chain.cpp:204-206` |
| `INV_TimeOrderedAdmission` | T-RT3 (CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY=3 wait, S-016 Option 2 partial closure). For every receipt in `eligible_for_apply`, `first_seen[k] + LATENCY <= dst.height`. The admission wait is enforced; receipts cannot short-circuit the latency gate. Matches `node.cpp:1577-1597` (`Node::inbound_receipts_eligible_for_inclusion`) and the production constant `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY = 3` at `node.cpp:1574`. v2.7 F2 (Option 1) closes fully via the Phase-1 intersection rule ÔÇö composition with FB22 F2ViewReconciliation.tla is future-work |
| `INV_OutboundDebitPrecedesInboundCredit` | T-RT1 (FA7 Lemma L-7.3 state-form witness). `outbound_emitted_count >= |applied_inbound_receipts|` ÔÇö every applied receipt corresponds to an emitted-on-source step, and the source-side debit is an atomic part of `EmitOutboundReceipt`. The strict-precedence claim is structural: `EmitOutboundReceipt` atomically increments `outbound_emitted_count` AND applies the source-side debit; the corresponding destination credit is at least one Gossip + Admit + Apply step later. The state-form witness for the temporal-precedence theorem |
| `INV_A1SourceDstComposition` | T-RT2 (cross-shard A1 supply identity). `Sum(src balances) + Sum(dst balances) + Sum(in-flight receipt amounts) <= InitialTotalSupply`. The receipt-as-conserved-quantity contract spanning source debit, transit, time-order admission queue, and destination credit. The strict-inequality form accommodates the fee component (fee stays on source for creator distribution per FB10; the receipt amount is the cross-shard supply movement). Matches the A1 algebra at `chain.cpp:1397-1404` lifted to the cross-shard composition |
| `INV_DedupSetSurvivesSnapshot` | T-RT5 (FA-Apply-12 / T-AR3 lifted, S-037 closure). For every snapshot taken at destination, the post-restore `applied_inbound_receipts` set is a superset of the snapshot's saved set. Pre-S-037 the snapshot lacked the `i:` namespace; `restore_from_snapshot` would silently drop the dedup-set and allow a re-injected receipt to credit a second time. Post-S-037 the live set is always a superset ÔÇö `RestoreFromSnapshot` preserves verbatim. Matches `chain.cpp:330-344` (`i:` namespace emission in `serialize_state`) + `chain.cpp:1778-1783` (consumer in `restore_from_snapshot`) |
| `INV_ReplayDetected` | T-RT6 (replay catches at apply, composed adversary). For every receipt-dedup_key k in `applied_inbound_receipts`, no spurious balance increment is reachable from any transit queue's apply path. The `AttemptReplayReceipt` adversary's state-form witness: re-injecting an already-applied receipt into `gossip_inflight` flows through the normal pipeline and the eventual `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst` fires the duplicate branch ÔÇö no balance mutation, no throw, no orphaned receipt. The structural impossibility of double-credit under replay |
| `INV_NoSilentDivergence` | T-RT7 (composition no-stuck-receipt). `outbound_emitted_count >= |applied_inbound_receipts|` (every applied receipt came from an emission) AND every emitted receipt is accounted for as either applied OR in one of the three transit queues. The cross-shard composition's no-receipt-lost claim ÔÇö every emission has a trackable destination (apply OR dedup-skip) and no receipt is silently dropped between source debit and destination credit |
| `INV_SourceA1OutboundApply` | T-RT8 (FA-Apply-13 / T-O1 + T-O3 state-form witness). Per-domain balance non-negativity across both shards: `\A d : src.balance[d] >= 0 AND dst.balance[d] >= 0`. The action-level T-O1 + T-O3 form is structurally enforced by `EmitOutboundReceipt`'s EXCEPT clause (which mutates only `balance[from]`; the to-domain on source is UNCHANGED ÔÇö the destination credit lives on the OTHER shard via the receipt path); the state-level invariant is the standing claim that no domain's balance ever wraps or goes negative |
| `PROP_EventualReceiptApply` (temporal) | under fairness on `GossipReceiptArrival` + `AdmitTimeOrderedEligibleReceipts` + `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst`, every emitted receipt is eventually applied (fresh-credit branch) OR rejected for dedup (duplicate-skip branch). State-form: a non-empty `gossip_inflight` queue leads to either an empty queue (drained) OR the apply path firing. The no-receipt-stuck-forever liveness contract |
| `PROP_NoLossOfFunds` (temporal) | under fairness, the A1 cross-shard supply identity is eventually re-established after every `EmitOutboundReceipt`: the receipt is either applied (in-flight term Ôćĺ destination balance) OR silently dropped per the dedup gate. The refund path for stuck receipts is v2.X future-work (per S-016 partial closure narrative ÔÇö out of scope for this spec); `INV_A1SourceDstComposition`'s in-flight component captures the transient state |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-five specs above). The recommended `CrossShardReceiptRoundtrip.cfg` (`Domains = {d_src, d_dst}`, `Hashes = {h1, h2}`, `Shards = {sh_src, sh_dst}`, `MaxAmount = 3`, `MaxFee = 0`, `InitialBalance = 10`, `MaxHeight = 4`, `LATENCY = 1`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. `LATENCY = 1` (relaxed from production `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY = 3` at `node.cpp:1574`) keeps the TLC state space tractable while preserving the time-order-gate semantics; production-equivalent runs with `LATENCY = 3` are feasible at MaxHeight=6+ on multi-core TLC. Seven actions cover the cross-shard cycle: `EmitOutboundReceipt(from, to, amount, fee, tx_h)` (source-side cross-shard TRANSFER apply at chain.cpp:752-766), `GossipReceiptArrival` (head of gossip_inflight Ôćĺ inbound_pool_dst with first_seen latched), `AdmitTimeOrderedEligibleReceipts` (head of inbound_pool_dst Ôćĺ eligible_for_apply if `first_seen + LATENCY <= dst.height` ÔÇö mirrors `Node::inbound_receipts_eligible_for_inclusion`), `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst` (the if/then/else dedup-on-apply branch ÔÇö fresh: credit + insert; duplicate: silent skip ÔÇö chain.cpp:1363-1381), `SerializeSnapshotSrc` / `SerializeSnapshotDst` (per-shard snapshot emission; dst snapshot binds `applied_inbound_receipts` + `inbound_first_seen` ÔÇö the S-037 `i:` namespace), `RestoreFromSnapshotSrc` / `RestoreFromSnapshotDst` (per-shard restore), `AttemptReplayReceipt(r)` (adversary re-injects an already-applied or in-transit receipt into gossip_inflight). The replay adversary's structural defeat is the `if/then/else` split in `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst`: the fresh branch's pre-condition `k \notin applied_inbound_receipts` blocks re-firing on a previously-applied dedup_key, routing the apply to the silent-skip branch. `MaxFee = 0` in the default cfg lets the A1 algebra collapse cleanly to the receipt-amount sum (the fee-paying case is FB10 territory and introduces an additive TotalFeesPaid term tracked separately).

This spec is the cross-shard composition lift of FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup ÔÇö destination dedup primitive), FB17 (AppliedReceiptRestore ÔÇö snapshot lifecycle of the destination dedup set), and FB18 (CrossShardOutboundApply ÔÇö source-side debit primitive). Where each predecessor covers a slice of the cross-shard lifecycle in isolation, FB32 composes the four mechanisms (V12 source-emit + gossip transit + S-016 time-order admission + FA-Apply-9 dst-dedup + FA-Apply-12 snapshot-survival) into a single state machine. The eight invariants pin the cross-shard cycle at every transition: source debit precedes destination credit (T-RT1); A1 holds with an in-flight term that accounts for transit-receipts (T-RT2); admission waits `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY` blocks (T-RT3); apply is dedup-safe (T-RT4); restore preserves the dedup set (T-RT5); replay is caught (T-RT6); no silent divergence is reachable (T-RT7); source-side debit equals exactly `amount + fee` (T-RT8). Together FB14 + FB17 + FB18 + FB32 witness the cross-shard receipt-as-conserved-quantity contract at the state-machine layer: FB14 + FB17 + FB18 each cover a sub-claim in isolation; FB32 closes the cross-shard receipt lifecycle gap by composing them with the source-emit + gossip + time-order pipeline that FA7 implicitly relies on but no prior FB-track spec covered end-to-end.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's ┬ž9 header comment):

- Refund path for stuck receipts. v2.X future-work (per S-016 partial closure narrative); the model captures the transient state via `INV_A1SourceDstComposition`'s in-flight component but does not model an explicit refund action.
- Cryptographic receipt-hash binding. FA7 / FB23 FrostVerify-style territory. The wire-level cryptographic admission (signature verification, K-of-K committee sign-off, V13 dst-side dedup at admission) is abstracted via the action discipline (`GossipReceiptArrival` models successful wire-level admission).
- v2.7 F2 Option 1 intersection rule. The model implements S-016 Option 2 (time-ordered admission); v2.7 F2 closes fully via the Phase-1 intersection rule. FB22 F2ViewReconciliation.tla covers F2 in isolation; the composition with FB32 is future-work once F2 ships.
- Per-block apply-loop composition. FB20 MultiEventComposition territory. FB32 zooms in on the receipt-only state machine; the per-block composition with other event classes (transfers, aborts, equivocations, subsidies) is the FB20 lift.
- Cross-shard fee accounting. The fee accrues to source-side creators per FB10; the receipt's amount field is the cross-shard supply movement. The A1 algebra collapses the fee component into the source-balance reduction with a strict inequality (`TotalLiveBalance + TotalInFlight <= InitialTotalSupply`).

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/CrossShardReceiptDedup.md` (FA-Apply-9 ÔÇö destination-side dedup contract; FB14 is the standalone state-machine companion), `docs/proofs/AppliedReceiptRestore.md` (FA-Apply-12 ÔÇö snapshot-pathway survival of the dedup set; FB17 is the standalone companion), `docs/proofs/CrossShardOutboundApply.md` (FA-Apply-13 ÔÇö source-side debit contract; FB18 is the standalone companion), `docs/proofs/CrossShardReceipts.md` (FA7 ÔÇö high-level cross-shard correctness theorem; FB32 unifies the three sub-theorems at the state-machine layer).

Cross-reference. FB14 `CrossShardReceiptDedup.tla` (destination-side dedup primitive in isolation; FB32 composes), FB17 `AppliedReceiptRestore.tla` (snapshot-pathway survival in isolation; FB32 composes via `INV_DedupSetSurvivesSnapshot`), FB18 `CrossShardOutboundApply.tla` (source-side debit primitive in isolation; FB32 composes via `INV_SourceA1OutboundApply` + `INV_OutboundDebitPrecedesInboundCredit`), FB6 `Snapshot.tla` (basic snapshot/restore foundation; FB32's snapshot actions follow the same shape). FB32 (this spec ÔÇö the composed cross-shard receipt lifecycle). Together FB14 + FB17 + FB18 + FB32 witness the full cross-shard receipt-as-conserved-quantity surface at the state-machine layer.
### MempoolAdmission.tla Ôćĺ FA-S008 (bounded mempool admission composition of S-008 + S-002 + FA-Apply-3 + FB23)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `mempool` (Seq(Tx) where Tx = [hash, from, nonce, fee, sig_valid]), `mempool_cap` (Nat ÔÇö operator-tunable cap; mirrors `MEMPOOL_MAX_TXS = 10000`), `applied_nonces` (Domains Ôćĺ Nat ÔÇö per-account applied frontier; mirrors `chain_.next_nonce(d)`), `rejection_log` (Seq(Rejection) where Rejection = [tx, reason] and reason Ôłł {"cap_full", "bad_sig", "stale_nonce", "future_nonce", "duplicate"}) |
| `INV_MempoolBounded` | T-MA1 (Bounded Mempool, S-008 headline witness). `Len(mempool) <= mempool_cap` at every reachable state. Structural argument: `AdmitTransaction` (5b) eviction branch strictly preserves the cap (evict-one-insert-one), `AdmitTransaction` (5a/6) honors the cap as a pre-condition, RBF replace at (3b) preserves the cap (in-place swap), `AdjustCap` requires `new_cap >= Len(mempool)`. The S-008 closure: an adversarial flood cannot blow the cap past its operator-configured ceiling. Maps to `Node::mempool_admit_check` global-cap branch at `src/node/node.cpp:1980-1992` + `Node::mempool_make_room_for` at lines 2001-2017 |
| `INV_NoStaleAdmission` | T-MA2 (No Stale Admission). No tx in mempool has `tx.nonce < applied_nonces[tx.from]`. Two-stage defense: `AdmitTransaction` (1) rejects stale-nonce at intake; `EvictStale` sweeps any tx that becomes stale post-admission (when `ApplyBlock` advances the frontier past it). Composes with FA-Apply-3 monotonicity (`INV_NonceMonotonic`): once-advanced, frontier never retreats, so a swept-stale tx cannot become re-admittable. Maps to the stale-nonce drop at `src/node/node.cpp:2022-2023` + the sweep loop at `src/node/node.cpp:1796-1803` |
| `INV_NoDuplicateAccountNonce` | T-MA3 (No Duplicate (Account, Nonce)). For every (from, nonce) pair, at most one tx in mempool. The RBF semantics: same-slot submissions replace rather than coexist (via `AdmitTransaction` (3b)'s in-place swap or `OverwriteSameAccountSameNonce`'s standalone form); cross-sender coincidence is structurally permitted (different `from` values are distinct slots). Maps to the `is_replace` short-circuit at `src/node/node.cpp:1965-1967` + the RBF tie-break at `src/node/node.cpp:2041-2043` |
| `INV_RejectionLogCorrectness` | T-MA4 (Rejection-Log Correctness). Every rejection in the audit trail has reason Ôłł {"cap_full", "bad_sig", "stale_nonce", "future_nonce", "duplicate"}. The five-bucket taxonomy exhausts the admission-check decision tree; every adversary input that fails admission falls into exactly one bucket. Structural argument: `AdmitTransaction`'s seven disjuncts cover the universe of (tx, state) inputs, and each rejection-emitting disjunct (1, 2, 3a, 4, 5a) labels its log entry with one of the five reasons. Maps to the error-string returns at `src/node/node.cpp::mempool_admit_check` lines 1971-1973 + 1987-1990 (plus the implicit silent-drop branches in `Node::on_tx`) |
| `INV_SigValidityNecessary` | T-MA5 (Sig-Validity Necessary, S-002 composition with S-008). Every tx currently in mempool has a valid signature under the abstract sig verifier (modeled via the FB23 FrostVerify-style boolean precondition `sig_valid`). Pre-S-002 admission could land bad-sig txs; post-S-002 every code path through `AdmitTransaction`'s success branches requires `tx.sig_valid = TRUE`. Composes with FB23 T-1 (verification soundness): a tx in mempool has a valid sig AND a valid sig implies the holder of the corresponding key signed the tx Ôçĺ no forged-sig tx ever reaches `Node::build_body`. Maps to `Node::on_tx::verify_tx_signature_locked` at `src/node/node.cpp:2025-2028` + the RPC sibling at `src/node/node.cpp:3164-3167` |
| `INV_NonceMonotonic` | FA-Apply-3 sub-claim (per-account nonce monotonicity, direct lift of FB7 Nonce.tla's `Inv_NonceMonotonic`). `applied_nonces[d]` is monotone non-decreasing across every `[Next]_vars` step. The structural witness is the EXCEPT clause in `ApplyBlock` which uses `@ + 1` (Nat-typed; monotone non-decreasing by construction); all other actions preserve `applied_nonces`. The load-bearing input to `INV_NoStaleAdmission`'s two-stage defense. Maps to the `sender.next_nonce++` advance in `Chain::apply_transactions` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:739`+ |
| `PROP_EventualAdmissionOrRejection` (temporal) | every transaction submission attempt eventually lands in mempool OR has an entry in rejection_log. The no-stuck-in-limbo liveness contract: a tx cannot be lost between the admission gate's decision and the audit log. The structural argument: `AdmitTransaction`'s seven disjuncts cover the universe of (tx, state) inputs; under fairness, every submitted tx routes to one of the two collections (mempool or rejection_log) |
| `PROP_MempoolEventuallyDrains` (temporal) | under fairness on `ApplyBlock`, a non-empty mempool with an applicable tx (nonce matching the per-sender applied frontier) eventually shrinks. Captured as a leads-to: a tx in mempool with `tx.nonce = applied_nonces[tx.from]` eventually leaves mempool (drained by `ApplyBlock`, replaced by `OverwriteSameAccountSameNonce`, or swept by `EvictStale`). The producer-side block-build progress guarantee |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-five specs above). The recommended `MempoolAdmission.cfg` (`Domains = {d1, d2}`, `Hashes = {h1, h2, h3, h4}`, `MaxNonce = 3`, `MaxFee = 3`, `Cap = 3`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. `Cap = 3` is the smallest value that lets the global-cap eviction branch fire while still leaving room for fresh-admit traces; `MaxFee = 3` gives four distinct fee tiers so the RBF tie-break + fee-priority eviction tie-break can both surface non-trivially; `MaxNonce = 3` is enough to exercise `ApplyBlock` advancing `applied_nonces` across multiple steps so `INV_NonceMonotonic` + `EvictStale`'s surface are both reachable. Six actions cover the admission / apply / sweep / RBF / cap-tuning surfaces: `AdmitTransaction(tx)` (the unified five-clause admission gate with seven disjuncts covering stale-nonce / bad-sig / RBF-lose / RBF-win / per-sender-quota / cap-full-reject / cap-full-evict / happy-path), `ApplyBlock` (drains one nonce-matching tx and advances the per-sender frontier ÔÇö collapses build_body + apply into a single atomic action), `EvictStale` (sweeps a tx whose nonce has fallen behind the frontier ÔÇö mirrors the inline cleanup at `src/node/node.cpp:1798-1803`), `OverwriteSameAccountSameNonce(tx_new)` (standalone form of the RBF replace branch ÔÇö exposed separately so `INV_NoDuplicateAccountNonce` is observable at TLC trace granularity), `AdjustCap(new_cap)` (operator-side parameter change; modeled to ensure a regression that shrinks the cap below `Len(mempool)` surfaces as an `INV_MempoolBounded` failure), `Stutter` (bounds TLC state space).

This spec captures the S-008 closure (bounded mempool with operator-configurable cap + per-sender quota + fee-priority eviction) at the state-machine layer, composing it with the FA-Apply-3 nonce gate (FB7 sibling), the FB23 FrostVerify abstract-sig precondition (S-002 closure), and the RBF (replace-by-fee) tie-break that `Node::on_tx` inherits. The seven invariants pin the admission discipline at every transition: cap is bounded (T-MA1); no stale admission (T-MA2); no duplicate (account, nonce) (T-MA3); every rejection is labeled with one of five documented reasons (T-MA4); every admitted tx has a valid signature (T-MA5); the apply frontier is monotone (FA-Apply-3 sub-claim). Together with the two temporal properties ÔÇö `PROP_EventualAdmissionOrRejection` (no-stuck-in-limbo) + `PROP_MempoolEventuallyDrains` (producer-side progress) ÔÇö the eight-property bundle covers the safety + liveness of the mempool admission surface.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's ┬ž9 header comment):

- Per-tx-type apply semantics (TRANSFER / REGISTER / STAKE / etc.). FB5 AccountState.tla + FB8 StakeLifecycle.tla + FB9 DAppRegistry.tla territory. FB33's `ApplyBlock` action collapses per-tx-type routing into a single "drain head + advance nonce" abstract action; the per-type body is the downstream FB-track sibling's domain.
- Cross-shard mempool composition. Each shard has an independent mempool; the multi-shard composition is FB32 CrossShardReceiptRoundtrip.tla territory (the receipt-level state-machine surface). FB33 models a single-shard mempool.
- Wire-level gossip propagation. The gossip path admission gate is identical to the RPC path admission gate (both call `Node::mempool_admit_check`); the wire-level cryptographic-binding side is FA7 / FB23 territory.
- Mempool encryption / privacy. Out of v1 scope (future-work under v2.22 Privacy).
- Runtime-tunable cap. The C++ side has `MEMPOOL_MAX_TXS` as a compile-time `constexpr` at `include/determ/node/node.hpp:459`; the `AdjustCap` action models the operator's recompile-and-redeploy with a smaller cap. Future-work: runtime-tunable cap via the PARAM_CHANGE governance subsystem (FB13 GovernanceParamChange.tla territory if extended).
- Quantitative far-future-nonce attack bounds. The spec models the per-sender quota as the implicit far-future ceiling; the production constant `MEMPOOL_MAX_PER_SENDER = 100` means an adversary can pipeline up to 100 nonces ahead of the current frontier per sender, which is the operator-tuned tradeoff between honest pipelining and attacker mempool occupation. The `"future_nonce"` bucket in `RejectionReason` captures this surface; a TLC trace that hits the per-sender quota produces a `"future_nonce"` rejection.

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/SECURITY.md` ┬žS-008 (the bounded mempool closure narrative ÔÇö operator-configurable cap + fee-priority eviction + per-sender quota together constitute the S-008 mitigation; `INV_MempoolBounded` + `INV_NoStaleAdmission` + `INV_RejectionLogCorrectness` are the three sub-mechanism witnesses at the state-machine layer), `docs/proofs/NonceMonotonicity.md` (FA-Apply-3 ÔÇö the per-account nonce monotonicity theorem; `INV_NonceMonotonic` is the direct lift), `docs/proofs/FrostVerifyDelegation.md` (FB23 T-1 verification soundness; `INV_SigValidityNecessary` composes), `docs/proofs/S002-Mempool-Sig-Verify.md` (the S-002 closure paired with the `binary_codec::decode_tx_frame` integer-bounds tightening; the bad-sig rejection branch of `AdmitTransaction` is the S-002 enforcement point).

Cross-reference. FB7 `Nonce.tla` (per-account nonce gate in isolation ÔÇö apply-layer focus; FB33 composes FB7's nonce gate with the S-008 mempool admission state machine ÔÇö the two specs are stacked, FB33's mempool feeds FB7's applied layer), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (FROST-Ed25519 verify soundness ÔÇö `INV_SigValidityNecessary` is the mempool-level consumer), FB20 `MultiEventComposition.tla` (composed per-block apply pipeline ÔÇö FB33's `ApplyBlock` action is the upstream feed to FB20's per-event composition; the two specs cover disjoint pre-/post-apply phases). FB33 (this spec ÔÇö the bounded-mempool admission state machine; the S-008 + S-002 composition at the mempool layer). Together FB7 + FB20 + FB23 + FB33 witness the tx-lifecycle from gossip-arrival Ôćĺ mempool-admission Ôćĺ block-build Ôćĺ apply at the state-machine layer.

## Mapping to source code

Each invariant directly mirrors a structure or check in the C++ implementation:

| Spec construct | Source location |
|---|---|
| `Consensus.contribs` | `src/node/node.cpp::on_contrib` (Phase-1 commit gather into `pending_contribs_`) |
| `Consensus.secrets_revealed` | `src/node/node.cpp::on_block_sig` (Phase-2 reveal gate, `pending_block_sigs_` admission) |
| `Consensus.SeenKCommits` | `src/node/node.cpp::on_contrib` (the `pending_contribs_.size() == current_creator_domains_.size()` check that fires `start_block_sig_phase`) |
| `Consensus.Finalize` quorum | `src/node/validator.cpp::check_block_sigs` (MD: K-of-K full committee; BFT: Q = ceil(2┬Ěk_bft/3) within the shrunk k_bft = ceil(2K/3) committee ÔÇö two-level shrinkage, see PROTOCOL.md ┬ž5.3). The spec uses `Keff = ceil(2K/3)` which only models the first-level shrinkage; this is correct degenerately at K=3 (Q=k_bft=2) and an over-approximation at K>=6 (safe direction for the Inv_OneDigest invariant; see Consensus.tla comment above the Keff definition). |
| `Sharding.emitted_receipts` | `chain::Block::cross_shard_receipts` field |
| `Sharding.pending_inbound` | `node::Node::pending_inbound_receipts_` |
| `Sharding.applied` | `chain::Chain::applied_inbound_receipts_` |
| `Receipts.applied` | same as above; isolated for focused check |

| `AccountState.stakes` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::stakes_` (map<string, StakeState> with locked + unlock_height) |

| `StakeLifecycle.Unstake` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_transactions` UNSTAKE success branch at lines 889ÔÇô893 (`sit->second.locked -= amount; sender.balance += amount;`) |

| `DAppRegistry.dapp_registry` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::dapp_registry_` (map<string, DAppEntry> keyed by domain ÔÇö the v2.18 substrate) |
| `DAppRegistry.registered_domains` | implicit: `dapp_registry_.find(d) != dapp_registry_.end()` ÔÇö the C++ map's membership predicate; the TLA model lifts this into an explicit set to make set-membership reasoning cleaner |
| `DAppRegistry.first_registered` | implicit: the chain has no explicit "first-registered" set, but the same predicate is witnessed at apply time via the `existing == dapp_registry_.end()` check at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1107-1112` (the branch that sets `registered_at = height`). The TLA model lifts this into an explicit provenance set so that Inv_NefDrainsOnlyOnce can be expressed as an action-level invariant |
| `DAppRegistry.nef_pool` | `accounts_[ZEROTH_ADDRESS].balance` ÔÇö the ZEROTH pool balance documented in `tools/test_nef_pool_drain.sh`; the TLA model abstracts the validator-REGISTER drain semantics into the DAppRegistry first-time-Register branch (the apply-path lifecycle is identical: half-drain on first-time registration, untouched on re-registration) |
| `DAppRegistry.height` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::current_height_` (advanced once per applied block) |
| `DAppRegistry.Register` (first-time branch) | `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_transactions` DAPP_REGISTER op=0 branch at lines 1064-1116, specifically the `existing == dapp_registry_.end()` branch at line 1110-1112 (sets `e.registered_at = height` and `e.active_from = height; e.inactive_from = UINT64_MAX;`) |
| `DAppRegistry.Update` | same DAPP_REGISTER op=0 branch, the `existing != dapp_registry_.end()` branch at lines 1107-1109 (preserves `e.registered_at = existing->second.registered_at;`) |
| `DAppRegistry.RejectUpdateByNonOwner` / `RejectDeactivateByNonOwner` | validator-layer ed_pub authentication rejects the tx before apply; if the tx slips through validation, the apply layer's `tx.from` ownership check (implicit in the dispatch ÔÇö the C++ key into `dapp_registry_` is `tx.from`, so a non-owner cannot mutate another's entry) silently no-ops with fee + nonce advance |
| `DAppRegistry.Deactivate` | DAPP_REGISTER op=1 branch at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1055-1062` (sets `dapp_registry_[tx.from].inactive_from = height + DAPP_GRACE_BLOCKS`) |
| `DAppRegistry.DappActive` | apply-side DAPP_CALL gate at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1142` (`if (dapp.inactive_from <= height) ... skip credit`) ÔÇö the TLA helper lifts this into a state predicate |
| `DAppRegistry.AdvanceHeight` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::apply_block` block-index increment (shared with all other FB-track specs) |

| `CrossShardOutboundApply.ApplyCrossShardTransfer` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_transactions` TRANSFER cross-shard branch at lines 762-766: the `else` branch of the `is_cross_shard(tx.to)` discriminator routes here when `tx.to` lives on a different shard; the apply body debits sender (line 745, shared with the same-shard branch) and increments the per-block `block_outbound` counter by `tx.amount` (line 765, which feeds `accumulated_outbound_` at chain.cpp:1394). The matching producer-side emission at `src/node/producer.cpp:459-465` appends the receipt to `b.cross_shard_receipts` ÔÇö the TLA model collapses the producer-side emission into the apply-side action since the receipt list is validator-gated and atomic with the apply body (Lemma L-7.3 ÔÇö source-side debit precedes receipt emission within the same apply_transactions call) |
| `CrossShardOutboundApply.ApplyInsufficientBalance` | the `continue` silent-skip at `src/chain/chain.cpp:744` (`if (sender.balance < cost) continue;`) ÔÇö no balance mutation, no fee accumulation, no receipt emission, no nonce advance. The validator's pre-apply admission check should normally reject these txs before they reach apply (FA-track territory), but the apply-layer `continue` is the safety net. T-O5 structural witness: no partial state mutation, no orphan receipt emission |
| `CrossShardOutboundApply.FinalizeBlock` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_block` block-finalize tail at lines 1393-1394 (`accumulated_outbound_ += block_outbound`); the TLA model lifts the per-block aggregation into immediate per-step bumps so the cumulative invariant is state-level rather than per-block-reset. FinalizeBlock in the model is a stutter on the conservation-relevant variables (the receipts physically move into `b.cross_shard_receipts` and the per-block accumulator clears at chain.cpp:715 on the next block, but the chain-level `accumulated_outbound_` and the cumulative receipt sum both persist) |
| `MultiEventComposition.balances` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::accounts_` (the `balance` field of each AccountState entry; the TLA model collapses the multi-field AccountState into just `balance` because the nonce / stake / ed_pub side is consumed by sibling FB-track specs ÔÇö FB7 / FB8 / FB5 ÔÇö and the composition layer only needs the supply-axis projection) |

| `MultiEventComposition.ApplyBlock` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_block` ÔÇö the canonical apply pipeline at chain.cpp:734 (tx loop) Ôćĺ 1313 (abort loop) Ôćĺ 1344 (equiv loop) Ôćĺ 1363 (receipt loop) Ôćĺ 1286 (distribution loop). | `FrostVerify.key_pubs` | `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:61` (the `Point` typedef = `std::array<uint8_t, 32>` ÔÇö the Ed25519 compressed group public key).
