| `FrostVerify.signed_sigs` | `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:62` (the `FrostSig` typedef = `std::array<uint8_t, 64>` ÔÇö the canonical `R ÔÇľ z` Ed25519 signature shape produced by `frost_aggregate` per RFC 9591 ┬ž5.1). The TLA model lifts the 64-byte array to a 64-element sequence over Bytes; the `static_assert(sizeof(FrostSig) == sizeof(Signature))` at `src/crypto/frost.cpp:108` pins the size equality with the underlying `Signature` type. The `signed_sigs` set is the spec-layer model of the honest-signing oracle's output history ÔÇö every (key, message) pair that has been signed produces a canonical triple in this set |
| `FrostVerify.valid_pairs` | implicit: the abstract Ed25519Verify acceptance relation ÔÇö the spec-layer model of the EUF-CMA verify predicate from Preliminaries ┬ž2.2 A2. Captures `EVP_PKEY_ED25519` verify acceptance at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:79-91` (which OpenSSL implements per RFC 8032 ┬ž5.1.7). The TLA model populates `valid_pairs` only via `SignMessage` (honest signing); the EUF-CMA assumption that no polynomial-time adversary forges signatures is modeled as `<<adversary_forged_sig, ..., ...>> \notin valid_pairs` ÔÇö a deterministic abstraction of the ÔëĄ 2Ôü╗┬╣┬▓ÔüŞ-per-attempt cryptographic bound |
| `FrostVerify.tampered_sigs` | implicit: the byte-tampered-variant set. Models the adversary's `sig'` construction in T-1.1 (corollary of `FrostVerifyDelegation.md` T-1). The action's universal-quantifier clause `\A k2 Ôłł generated : \A m2 Ôłł Messages : <<key_pubs[k2], m2, sig_prime>> \notin valid_pairs` is the spec-layer enforcement of the EUF-CMA assumption ÔÇö every tampered sig is structurally excluded from the verify-acceptance relation under any (pub, msg) combination |
| `FrostVerify.verify_log` | implicit: the observable history of `FrostVerify` calls. Indexed by scenario tag (`"canonical"`, `"tampered_sig"`, `"wrong_key"`, `"tampered_msg"`) so INV-1..INV-5 can be evaluated per-case. Lifts the runtime regression at `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 (`determ test-view-root`) ÔÇö the five assertions there are the runtime witnesses of INV-1..INV-5; the TLA log is the state-machine projection of those assertions across the bounded universe |
| `FrostVerify.scenario` | implicit: a 4-phase marker (`"init"`, `"keygen"`, `"signed"`, `"verified"`) that sequences the workflow actions. No direct C++ correspondent ÔÇö the C++ side has no explicit phase tracker because `frost_verify` is a stateless function; the TLA marker is purely a state-space-bounding device for TLC (without it, the action enumeration would be unbounded over the seq-of-verify-calls log) |
| `FrostVerify.GenKeypair` | implicit: not exercised by `frost_verify` itself (which consumes `group_pubkey` as an input). Models the v2.10 DKG ceremony's output (group_pubkey + verification_shares per `LocalShare` at `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:110-115`) ÔÇö or, equivalently, a single-party Ed25519 keygen via `EVP_PKEY_keygen` at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:17-33`. | `FrostVerify.SignMessage` | implicit: not exercised by `frost_verify` itself. Models the v2.10 t-of-K partial-aggregation pipeline (`frost_sign_round1` + `frost_sign_round2` + `frost_aggregate` at `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:146-169`) as a single atomic step that produces a canonical aggregate. The joint extension `signed_sigs Ôł¬= {<<k, msg, sig>>}` + `valid_pairs Ôł¬= {<<pub, msg, sig>>}` captures RFC 9591 ┬ž3 Theorem 1's structural-Ed25519-sig property (the analytic proof's L-1). When v2.10 Phase D ships the real sign primitives, this action becomes the spec-layer abstraction of the multi-round protocol |
| `FrostVerify.Tamper` / `FrostVerify.VerifyTampered` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 2 ÔÇö the byte-flip + re-verify sequence (`sig[0] ^= 0xff; assert(frost_verify(sig, group_pub, msg) == false)`). The TLA `Tamper` action models the byte-flip; `VerifyTampered` models the re-verify call. The structural EUF-CMA exclusion (`sig_prime \notin valid_pairs`) is the spec-layer reduction of the assertion's "expected false" expectation to a deterministic predicate |
| `FrostVerify.VerifyWrongKey` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 3 ÔÇö `frost_verify(sig, wrong_pub, msg) == false`. The TLA action's `key_pubs[k_other] # key_pubs[k]` filter ensures wrong-key distinctness; `valid_pairs` only contains the signing-key triple, so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Matches the analytic proof's T-1.2 reduction to Ed25519 EUF-CMA over the `pk'` key's secret |
| `FrostVerify.VerifyTamperedMsg` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 4 ÔÇö `frost_verify(sig, group_pub, msg') == false` with `msg' Ôëá msg`. The TLA action's `msg_other # msg` filter ensures message distinctness; `valid_pairs` only contains the original-message triple, so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Matches the analytic proof's T-1.3 reduction to Ed25519 EUF-CMA + SHA-512 collision resistance over the challenge derivation |
| `FrostVerify.VerifyCanonical` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 1 ÔÇö `frost_verify(sig, group_pub, msg) == true` for the canonical aggregate. The TLA action returns `result = TRUE` by definition: `FrostVerify(sig, key_pubs[k], msg) = Ed25519Verify(key_pubs[k], msg, sig) = (<<key_pubs[k], msg, sig>> \in valid_pairs) = TRUE` (SignMessage populated it). Matches the analytic proof's T-1 forward direction (L-1 + L-2 + delegation operator) |
| `FrostVerify.FrostVerify` | `src/crypto/frost.cpp:101-118` ÔÇö the function under test. The TLA model abstracts this to a `valid_pairs` membership check; the analytic proof's L-2 establishes the equivalence between `determ::crypto::verify` and the RFC equation; the FA-Crypto-Verify track gives the cryptographic tightness, and the FB-track checks the state-machine consistency of the delegation abstraction |

| `MakeContribCommitment.IsZero` | `src/node/producer.cpp:242-245` ÔÇö the `is_zero_hash` lambda: `for (auto byte : h) if (byte != 0) return false; return true;`. The spec-layer `IsZero(h) == h = ZERO` captures the predicate verbatim via the designated `ZERO` element of `Hashes` (= the value-initialized `Hash{}` per `[array.cons]` + `[dcl.init.aggr]`, which is `std::array<uint8_t, 32>{}` = all-zero bytes) |
| `MakeContribCommitment.AllViewsZero` | `src/node/producer.cpp:246-248` ÔÇö the `!any_view` composite predicate: `bool any_view = !is_zero_hash(view_eq_root) \|\| !is_zero_hash(view_abort_root) \|\| !is_zero_hash(view_inbound_root);`. The spec-layer `AllViewsZero(eq, ab, inb) == IsZero(eq) /\ IsZero(ab) /\ IsZero(inb)` is the negation of `any_view`; when TRUE, the C++ `if (any_view)` branch at lines 249-258 is skipped and the implementation follows the v1 commit shape (L-1 of the companion analytic proof) |
| `MakeContribCommitment.V1Commit` | `src/node/producer.cpp:225-233 + 259` ÔÇö the v1 commit shape (pre-F2 implementation, also the reachable path when `AllViewsZero` holds): `SHA256Builder inner; for (auto& h : sorted_tx_hashes) inner.append(h); Hash inner_root = inner.finalize();` (lines 225-227) followed by `SHA256Builder b; b.append(block_index); b.append(prev_hash); b.append(inner_root); b.append(dh_input);` (lines 229-233) followed by `return b.finalize();` (line 259, when the `if (any_view)` body is skipped). The spec-layer `V1Commit(idx, prev, txs, dh) == << "V1", idx, prev, InnerRoot(txs), dh >>` captures the four-element pre-image structurally with a `"V1"` discriminator tag for cross-family distinctness (L-3 of the companion proof). InnerRoot itself is the spec-layer abstraction of the inner SHA-256 at lines 225-227 |
| `MakeContribCommitment.F2Commit` | `src/node/producer.cpp:249-258 + 259` ÔÇö the F2 commit shape (the v2.7 extension when at least one view root is non-zero): the v1 prefix at lines 229-233 PLUS the F2 branch body at lines 249-258 (`b.append(std::string("DTM-F2-v1")); b.append(view_eq_root); b.append(view_abort_root); b.append(view_inbound_root);`) PLUS the finalize at line 259. The spec-layer `F2Commit(idx, prev, txs, dh, eq, ab, inb) == << "F2", idx, prev, InnerRoot(txs), dh, "DTM-F2-v1", eq, ab, inb >>` captures the nine-element pre-image structurally with an `"F2"` discriminator tag. The `"DTM-F2-v1"` literal is encoded as a discriminator-level element rather than a byte-level append because L-3 of the companion proof gives the length-distinguishing argument (104-byte v1 vs 209-byte F2) that the spec layer captures as discriminator-distinctness |
| `MakeContribCommitment.MakeCommit` | `src/node/producer.cpp:219-260` ÔÇö the function under test. The spec-layer operator `MakeCommit(idx, prev, txs, dh, eq, ab, inb) == IF AllViewsZero(eq, ab, inb) THEN V1Commit(...) ELSE F2Commit(...)` is the structural formalization of the C++ if-branch at lines 242-258: the `is_zero_hash` short-circuit at lines 242-248 evaluates to `AllViewsZero`, and the branch at line 249 picks between the v1 prefix (when `!any_view`) and the F2 prefix + extension (when `any_view`). The C++ header declaration at `include/determ/node/producer.hpp:117-139` with the three default-zero trailing args is what makes the v1 short-circuit reachable from legacy call sites (pre-F2 callers that omit the view-root args) |
| `MakeContribCommitment.InnerRoot` | `src/node/producer.cpp:225-227` ÔÇö the inner SHA-256 over the sorted-deduped tx-hash list: `SHA256Builder inner; for (auto& h : sorted_tx_hashes) inner.append(h); Hash inner_root = inner.finalize();`. The spec-layer `InnerRoot(txs) == << "inner", txs >>` is the abstraction: a tagged tuple over the tx-list values, structurally distinct from any V1 or F2 pre-image (different tag). The inner-root is injective on distinct tx-lists by A2 (collision resistance of SHA-256); the spec layer captures this by tuple equality on the underlying `txs` value |
| `RateLimiterEviction.buckets` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:151` ÔÇö `std::map<std::string, Bucket> buckets_` (the per-key bucket map; key = peer-IP string typed as `std::string`, value = `Bucket` struct). The TLA model lifts the C++ map into a function `ActiveKeys Ôćĺ Bucket` where the active subset of `Keys` is the spec-layer analog of `buckets_.find(key) != buckets_.end()` membership. The map's other entries are touched only via per-key operator[] references; per-key locality matches L-3 of the prose proof |
| `RateLimiterEviction.buckets[k].tokens` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:121` ÔÇö `double tokens{0.0};` field of `struct Bucket`. The TLA model collapses the `[0, C]` interval (per L-1 of the prose proof) into a FULL/EMPTY boolean because the F-1 invariants depend on `last_touch`, not on the precise integer-fractional token amount. The token-bucket arithmetic at rate_limiter.hpp:109-113 (`b.tokens = std::min(burst_, b.tokens + elapsed_sec * rate_per_sec_)` + `b.tokens -= 1.0`) is captured by L-1's interval bound and is orthogonal to the F-1 mitigation; the spec abstracts to FULL after every Consume because that is the post-refill-clamp state under realistic configs |
| `RateLimiterEviction.buckets[k].last_touch` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:122` ÔÇö `std::chrono::steady_clock::time_point last;` field of `struct Bucket`. Updated unconditionally to `now` on every Consume call at rate_limiter.hpp:108 + 112; the eviction predicate at line 135 uses this field exclusively (`now - it->second.last > threshold`). The TLA model uses Nat-typed time units; the C++ `steady_clock::duration` is bijectively mapped at the spec layer (Preliminaries.md ┬ž2.2 L-5 monotonicity preserved by the AdvanceTime action's `delta >= 1` clause) |
| `RateLimiterEviction.next_sweep_at` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:149` ÔÇö `std::chrono::steady_clock::time_point next_sweep_at_;` instance member. The default-constructed value (`time_since_epoch().count() == 0` at line 96) is the sentinel for "no sweep has fired yet"; the spec models this as `next_sweep_at = 0` at Init. Advanced by the amortized-sweep branch at lines 99-101 (`next_sweep_at_ = now + sweep_interval_sec_;`); the spec mirrors via the Consume action's LET-bound `post_sweep_at` when `sweep_fires` is true |
| `RateLimiterEviction.now` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:89` ÔÇö `auto now = std::chrono::steady_clock::now();` at the top of every `consume()` call. The TLA model uses Nat-typed monotonic time; the C++ side's `std::chrono::steady_clock` is RFC-mandated monotonic (Preliminaries.md ┬ž2.2 L-5 + C++ ISO/IEC 14882:2017 ┬ž20.17.7.4 [time.clock.steady]). AdvanceTime's `now' = now + delta` with `delta >= 1` enforces strict-increase, matching the steady_clock contract |
| `RateLimiterEviction.evicted_count` | implicit: the C++ side returns per-call evicted counts from `sweep_idle_locked` at `rate_limiter.hpp:128-143` (`size_t evicted = 0; ... ++evicted; ... return evicted;`) and `sweep_idle()` at line 82 ÔÇö but does NOT maintain a cumulative counter. The TLA model lifts the per-call return into a chain-level cumulative spec variable to make INV-2 (`EvictionMonotone`) observable across the trace. Operators wanting to observe monotone eviction counts in production would need to wrap `sweep_idle()` with an external counter ÔÇö the spec captures the desired contract |
| `RateLimiterEviction.was_evicted` | implicit: the C++ side has no equivalent set because eviction is destructive on `buckets_` (the `buckets_.erase(it)` at line 136 deletes the entry; subsequent `buckets_[key]` on the same key default-constructs a fresh entry per the std::map::operator[] semantics). The TLA model lifts the resurrection history into a spec-only audit set so INV-3 (`ResurrectionSafe`) can observe re-touched-after-eviction keys. Structurally equivalent to "would a logging hook on the per-entry erase witness this key" |
| `RateLimiterEviction.ActiveKeys` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:69-72` ÔÇö the C++ side observes the size via `bucket_count() const { return buckets_.size(); }` (lifted as `Cardinality(ActiveKeys)`). The TLA `DOMAIN buckets` is the spec-layer analog of `buckets_`'s key set |
| `RateLimiterEviction.IsStale` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:135` ÔÇö the strict-greater eviction predicate inside `sweep_idle_locked`: `if (now - it->second.last > threshold)`. The TLA `IsStale(k) == now - buckets[k].last_touch > EvictionThreshold` is the structural lift; the strict-greater comparison preserves the C++ side's behavior at the boundary (a bucket touched EXACTLY `EvictionThreshold` seconds ago is NOT stale) |
| `RateLimiterEviction.SweepIdle` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:128-143` ÔÇö the `sweep_idle_locked` private method: short-circuits when eviction is disabled (`if (eviction_threshold_sec_ <= 0.0) return 0;` at line 129), then walks `buckets_.begin()..end()` erasing stale entries (lines 134-141). The TLA model's IF-branch mirrors the short-circuit; the active branch restricts `buckets` to `ActiveKeys \ StaleKeys`, bumps `evicted_count` by `Cardinality(StaleKeys)`, and unions the stale keys into `was_evicted` |
| `RateLimiterEviction.Consume` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:86-117` ÔÇö the public `consume(const std::string& key)` method. The boolean return (`return false` / `return true`) is not invariant-relevant for F-1 ÔÇö it's covered by FA-T1 (bounded burst) of the prose proof |
| `RateLimiterEviction.AdvanceTime` | implicit: no C++ method advances the clock ÔÇö `std::chrono::steady_clock::now()` is queried per-consume at line 89, and the OS provides the monotonic value. | `RateLimiterEviction.ForcedSweep` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:79-82` ÔÇö the public `size_t sweep_idle()` method exposed for tests + operator monitoring. Wraps `sweep_idle_locked(std::chrono::steady_clock::now())` under the mutex; returns the number of entries evicted. The TLA model captures this as a no-op-when-disabled / SweepIdle-when-enabled action with `now` and `next_sweep_at` UNCHANGED (the C++ side does NOT advance `next_sweep_at_` on a ForcedSweep ÔÇö only the amortized-sweep branch in `consume()` advances it at lines 99-101) |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.chains` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::blocks_` ÔÇö the in-memory chain held by each node; the TLA model lifts it to `Nodes Ôćĺ Seq(Block)` since the spec models three nodes concurrently. | `BlockchainStateIntegrity.local_state` | the canonical post-apply state of each node, lifted into a single record per node. The C++ side spreads this across `Chain::accounts_`, `Chain::stakes_`, `Chain::registrants_`, etc. (the ten S-033 namespaces enumerated at `PROTOCOL.md ┬ž4.1.1`); the spec collapses to `[height, txs: SUBSET TxUniverse]` because the state-integrity invariants only need a canonical equality predicate on state (FA-Apply-1's determinism contract), not the per-namespace mutation semantics |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.chain_at_rest` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::save` output at chain.cpp:1944-1985 ÔÇö the wrapped JSON form `{head_hash, blocks}`. The TLA model abstracts the JSON encoding to a record `[head_hash: Hash, blocks: Seq(Block)]`; the byte-level serialization is orthogonal to the integrity invariants |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.pending_inbox` | `node::Node::pending_blocks_` (the gossip-ingress queue after V1..V20 validator admission); the TLA model abstracts the wire-level signature verification and V-gate sequence into the implicit "any block in pending_inbox is admissible-pending-state-root-check" |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.apply_throws` | implicit: latches when `Chain::apply_transactions` throws `"state_root mismatch at block <h>: ..."` at chain.cpp:1432-1444. The C++ side propagates the exception out through `apply_block_locked` and the A9 atomic-apply rolls back the in-progress mutations. The TLA model lifts the exception propagation into an observable BOOLEAN sentinel because state-machine invariants need a positive marker of "an integrity gate has fired" |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.load_throws` | implicit: latches when `Chain::load` throws `"chain file: head_hash mismatch (tampering or corruption?)"` at chain.cpp:2046-2050 OR when `Chain::append` throws `"Block prev_hash mismatch"` at chain.cpp:54-58 during replay. Both throws sit on the load-time integrity path; the TLA model collapses them into a single BOOLEAN sentinel since the invariant target (INV_LoadDetectsTampering) is "at least one of the integrity gates fired" |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tampered_at` | implicit: no C++ correspondent ÔÇö the chain.json file on disk has no "I have been tampered with" flag (that's the whole point of the integrity-check ladder). The TLA model lifts the tamper into an observable spec-only audit field so INV_LoadDetectsTampering can observe the post-tamper state without requiring the model to enumerate over byte-level mutations. The 0..MaxHeight range identifies which block was tampered; "none" is the no-tamper sentinel |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.ProduceBlock` | `src/node/node.cpp::Node::try_finalize_round` at node.cpp:1024-1117 ÔÇö the six-step producer flow (build_body / tentative-chain dry-run / state_root computation / self-apply / broadcast). The TLA model collapses the six steps into a single atomic action because the C++ side holds the chain mutex across all six; T-3 (Producer Self-Apply Consistency) is the structural witness that the gate-pass on self-apply is unconditional under this serialization |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.ApplyBlockOnReceive` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::apply_transactions` at chain.cpp:1421-1446 ÔÇö the S-033 gate's central mechanism. The TLA model captures the prev_hash continuity check (chain.cpp:54-58, lifted into the `prev_ok` LET binding) AND the state_root gate (chain.cpp:1432-1444, lifted into the `gate_passes` LET binding). On either failure the apply latches `apply_throws[n]` and refuses to extend the chain; on success the chain is advanced atomically |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.SerializeChain` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::save` at chain.cpp:1944-1985 ÔÇö writes the wrapping JSON `{head_hash, blocks}` form per S-021. The TLA model captures the head_hash population at chain.cpp:1949 (`out["head_hash"] = to_hex(blocks_.back().compute_hash())`); the action also resets the tampered_at sentinel to "none" since an honest save would overwrite any prior on-disk tampering |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.LoadChain` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::load` at chain.cpp:1987-2054 ÔÇö the T-1 primary mechanism. The TLA model captures both integrity layers: the per-block `prev_hash` continuity check (via the `validate_chain` helper, mirroring chain.cpp:54-58 inside each `apply_transactions(b)` replay call) AND the head's wrapping `head_hash` recompute (via the `head_hash_ok` LET binding, mirroring chain.cpp:2046-2050). On either failure the load latches `load_throws[n]` and refuses to install the chain |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.TamperAtRest` | the disk-level adversary surface from `BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` ┬ž5 case (d) ÔÇö no direct C++ source-line (the C++ side doesn't tamper with itself); the spec models the adversarial mutation of one block's `txs` field at an arbitrary height. The wrap header's stored `head_hash` is NOT patched (case (c) of T-1, which would require forging committee signatures per A1 / FrostVerify.tla, is out of scope for the state-machine layer). The next LoadChain MUST detect via interior prev_hash mismatch (case (a)) or head head_hash mismatch (case (b)) |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.DivergentTxPropose` | the Byzantine-producer adversary surface from `BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` ┬ž5 case (b) ÔÇö node n submits a block to dest with a state_root that doesn't match the canonical post-apply state. The spec models this via an arbitrary `fake_state` choice constrained to differ from the apply-time computed state. The next ApplyBlockOnReceive at dest MUST latch apply_throws via the S-033 gate's loud-fail. No direct C++ source-line ÔÇö the wire-level adversary would manipulate the body bytes between sig-gathering and broadcast; the apply-time gate is the structural safety net |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.state_root_of` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::compute_state_root` at chain.cpp:413-415 ÔÇö the central S-033 primitive. The TLA operator returns the abstract-hash tuple `<<"ROOT", height, txs>>` as the spec-layer projection of the C++ side's SHA-256 over the ten-namespace sorted-leaves Merkle tree at chain.cpp:267+. Pure function: identical state Ôçĺ identical root; distinct state Ôçĺ distinct root (A2 / Preliminaries ┬ž2.1 lift) |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.compute_hash` | `chain::Block::compute_hash` ÔÇö the per-block hash binding (index, prev_hash, state_root, txs); under the zero-skip backward-compat shim, state_root is included when non-zero. The TLA operator returns `<<"HASH", index, txs>>` (the spec's abstract-hash projection); the "HASH" discriminator separates this output namespace from `state_root_of`'s "ROOT" namespace, capturing the C++ side's domain-separation between block-hash and state-root |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.validate_chain` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::append` at chain.cpp:54-58 ÔÇö the per-block prev_hash continuity check inside the replay loop. The TLA helper recursively walks the chain blocks checking `c[i].prev_hash = head_hash(prefix)` for every block index; mirrors the C++ "for each block, append it (which verifies prev_hash before pushing)" pattern at chain.cpp:1987-2054 |
| `JsonValidation.input_objects` | implicit: the spec-layer accumulator of admitted JSON inputs per surface. No direct C++ correspondent ÔÇö the 5 surfaces (Wire / RPC / Snapshot / Keyfile / Genesis) each have their own admission paths (`net::Message::deserialize`, `RpcServer::dispatch`, `Chain::restore_from_snapshot`, `crypto::load_node_key`, `GenesisConfig::from_json`); the TLA model lifts them into a per-surface tracking surface for INV-3's surface-tag invariant |
| `JsonValidation.validation_log` | implicit: the spec-layer observable for INV-1 / INV-2 / INV-3 / INV-4. No direct C++ correspondent ÔÇö the C++ side throws exceptions that propagate up the call stack; the TLA model lifts the per-required-field outcome into a logged sequence so the field-name-context contract can be observed as a state-machine invariant. The byte-level exception message (the `what()` string at the C++ catch site) is abstracted into the BOOLEAN `has_diagnostic` tag |
| `JsonValidation.fired_surfaces` | implicit: SUBSET of Surfaces tracking which entry points have been exercised. Purely a TLC state-bounding device for the SaturateSurface stutter; no direct C++ correspondent |
| `JsonValidation.RequireField` | `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp:37-49` ÔÇö the `template <typename T> T json_require(const nlohmann::json& j, const char* field)` helper. The TLA operator returns "MissingField" when `key \notin DOMAIN obj` (mirroring the `if (!j.contains(field)) throw std::runtime_error("S-018: missing required JSON field 'FIELD'")` branch at lines 38-40), "WrongType" when `obj[key][1] /= expected_type` (mirroring the `catch (const std::exception& e) throw std::runtime_error("S-018: JSON field 'FIELD' has wrong type: ...")` branch at lines 44-48), "Pass" otherwise (mirroring `return j.at(field).get<T>()` at line 43). The `json_require_hex` and `json_require_array` length-mismatch / wrong-array branches collapse into the same WrongType outcome at the spec layer |
| `JsonValidation.OptionalField` | `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp` (no helper ÔÇö the C++ side uses `j.value(field, default)` from `nlohmann::json` directly + the `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` guard pattern). The TLA operator returns `obj[key]` when present, `default` when absent ÔÇö captures the `j.value(field, default)` semantics structurally |
| `JsonValidation.ValidateMessage` | implicit: not a single function ÔÇö every converted from_json (the 14-row inventory in `JsonValidationSoundness.md` ┬ž3.3) is a ValidateMessage invocation at its surface. The TLA operator walks a schema sequence invoking RequireField per entry; the C++ side walks the structural sequence of `json_require_*` calls in the from_json body. Both produce O(\|schema\|) bounded work |
| `JsonValidation.ValidateAtSurface` | the headline action ÔÇö exercises the per-surface from_json invocation. The 5 surfaces correspond to: Wire = `net::Message::deserialize` at `src/net/messages.cpp:44` + per-message-type from_json (Block / Transaction / ContribMsg / BlockSigMsg / AbortClaimMsg / EquivocationEvent / CrossShardReceipt); RPC = `RpcServer::dispatch` at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp` + structured-payload args (`submit_tx`'s `"tx"`, `submit_equivocation`'s `"event"`); Snapshot = `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` collection wrappers at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1748-1850`; Keyfile = `crypto::load_node_key` at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:55-56`; Genesis = `GenesisConfig::from_json` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp:189-275` |
| `JsonValidation.ExtractOptional` | the optional-field extraction action. The C++ correspondents are the `j.value(field, default)` and `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` patterns scattered across the 14-row consumer inventory (e.g., `ContribMsg::aborts_gen` at `producer.cpp` reading `j.value("aborts_gen", uint64_t{0})`; `Block::tx_root` / `delay_seed` / `delay_output` / `consensus_mode` / `bft_proposer` / `partner_subset_hash` / `state_root` at `Block::from_json` each wrapped in `if (j.contains(...))`). The TLA action leaves `validation_log` UNCHANGED ÔÇö captures the silent-default-on-absence contract that backward-compat rolling upgrades rely on |

A reviewer who is suspicious of a particular invariant can:

1. Identify the source-code line that should enforce it (table above).
2. Read the code at that location.
3. Confirm the code matches the spec's guard or update.

## Counter-examples found (none expected)

If any TLC run produces an invariant violation, this section will record:

- The violated invariant.
- The trace TLC printed (state sequence leading to violation).
- The diagnosis: spec bug vs. real implementation bug.
- The fix.

**Current entries:** none.

---

## Known TLA+ spec limitations

These are *modeling* limitations ÔÇö not implementation gaps:

1. **No cryptography modeled.** Signatures are abstracted as set membership. The FA-track analytic proofs (FA1, FA6) handle EUF-CMA bounds; the TLA+ spec only models the message flow.
2. **Single-height projection (Consensus).** The model checks one height at a time. Cross-height safety (chain growth, fork-choice) is a separate concern that follows from per-height safety + linear chain structure.
3. **No actual hashes.** Digests are small integers; the spec asserts no collisions trivially. SHA-256 collision resistance is an external cryptographic assumption (FA-track).
4. **Bounded state.** `MaxRounds`, `MaxTransfers`, `MaxBlocks` cap the model. TLC exhausts the bounded state space; analytic proofs (FA-track) give the unbounded result.

These limitations are *intentional* ÔÇö TLA+ is for state-machine correctness, not cryptographic security. The FA-track and FB-track together cover both layers.

---

## CI integration (future)

The natural next step is wiring TLC into CI:

```yaml
# .github/workflows/formal.yml (sketch)
- name: TLA+ model check
  run: |
    cd docs/proofs/tla
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry FeeAccounting; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry SubsidyDistribution; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry CrossShardReceiptDedup; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange EquivocationApply; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange AbortApply; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange AppliedReceiptRestore; do
      java -jar tla2tools.jar -config $cfg.cfg $cfg.tla
    done
```

This isn't shipped yet (no Java in the build container). When it lands, this document gets the actual transcript appended.

## Conclusion

The nine TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and per-block fee-accounting properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The nine TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and block-subsidy-distribution properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The nine TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and governance-parameter-change properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The ten TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and cross-shard-receipt-dedup properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The ten TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, governance-parameter-change, and equivocation-slashing-apply properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:

- **FA-track**: human-readable, cryptographically tight, unbounded.
- **FB-track**: machine-checkable, structurally exhaustive over bounded models.

Both tracks cite the same source-code locations, so a reviewer can trace any property end-to-end: theorem Ôćĺ state-machine model Ôćĺ source code.
